Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Identifying Ibn Taymiyya's Radd 'ala al-Mantiqiyyin
Title page showing the book's full title, author, and publication details.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the full title, author, and purpose of Ibn Taymiyya's Radd 'ala al-Mantiqiyyin from its title page.

Core Idea
This book's full title reveals its mission: to refute Greek logic as an act of faith.

Before diving into Ibn Taymiyya's arguments, we must first know exactly what work we are reading. The title page provides crucial information: the book's full name, its author, and the scholarly context of this edition. Understanding these details gives us the proper framework for engaging with the text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary title
Look at the first line: 'كتاب الرَّد على المنطقيين'. This is the main title, meaning 'The Refutation of the Logicians'. Note that 'المنطقيين' refers to adherents of Greek logic.
2
Identify the secondary title
The subtitle 'نصيحة أهل الإيمان في الرد على منطق اليونان' frames the work as 'Advice to the People of Faith'. This shows Ibn Taymiyya's purpose is religious counsel, not just academic critique.
3
Confirm the author and his credentials
The author is named as 'تقي الدين أبي العباس أحمد بن عبد الحليم ابن تيمية' with the honorific 'شيخ الإسلام'. His birth (661 AH) and death (728 AH) are given, establishing his historical context.
Ibn Taymiyya is a major Hanbali theologian and jurist.
4
Note the publication details
The page lists an editor and publisher. This modern edition (with 'مؤسسة الريان') shows the book's continued relevance. The editor's name and position indicate scholarly authentication.
OCR uncertainties exist in some names; treat with caution.

Book: The Refutation of the Logicians. Also called: Advice to the People of Faith in Refuting the Logic of the Greeks. By the noble Imam, Shaykh al-Islam, the scholar Taqi al-Din Abi al-Abbas Ahmad ibn Abd al-Halim Ibn Taymiyya al-Iraqi, born in 661 AH and died in 728 AH, may God have mercy on him. Introduced by the Turkish scholar al-Kathir al-Yamat al-Tarwi, died in 1373 AH, director of the journal Ma'arif and judge in the religious court of Byukov. Edited, revised and prepared for this edition by Shaykh Abd al-Samad Sharaf al-Din al-Kabti and Muhammad Talha Bilal Manar, may God have mercy on them. Al-Rayyan Foundation for Printing, Publishing and Distribution.
Source pages p. 1

Commentary
This passage is the title page and publication information of Ibn Taymiyya's famous work 'The Refutation of the Logicians' (Radd 'ala al-Mantiqiyyin). The full title includes the alternative name 'Advice to the People of Faith in Refuting the Logic of the Greeks' (Nasihat Ahl al-Iman fi al-Radd 'ala Mantiq al-Yunan), indicating that the author's purpose is to defend the Islamic faith against the influence of Greek logic. The author is identified as the revered Shaykh al-Islam Taqi al-Din Ibn Taymiyya, a prominent Hanbali theologian and jurist born in 661 AH and died in 728 AH. The page then lists the editor and publisher of this modern edition, showing that the book has been republished with scholarly care. The presence of the editor's introduction and the publisher's details situates this edition in the 20th century, making the work accessible to contemporary readers.

Key Takeaway
The title page establishes the author, the full title, and the religious purpose of Ibn Taymiyya's critique of Greek logic.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Ibn Taymiyya's Radd al-Mantiqiyyin: Title Page
Title page with book title, author, and publication details

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key biographical elements of Ibn Taymiyya as given on the title page of Radd al-Mantiqiyyin and explain the significance of the term 'al-mantiqiyyin' in his critique.

Core Idea
The title page of Radd al-Mantiqiyyin establishes Ibn Taymiyya's authority and targets: the logicians of Greek tradition.

This lesson examines the title page of Ibn Taymiyya's famous work, 'Radd al-Mantiqiyyin'. The page provides not only bibliographic details but also sets the stage for his critique of Aristotelian logic as the sole arbiter of truth. By understanding this front matter, you gain insight into the scholarly context and the author's mission.

Guided Path
1
Locate the author's full name and titles
Find the name: Taqi al-Din Abu al-'Abbas Ahmad ibn 'Abd al-Halim ibn Taymiyya. Notice the honorifics: Imam, Shaykh al-Islam.
This establishes his authority in the Islamic tradition.
2
Note the birth and death years (661-728 AH)
Record the hijri dates. This places him in the 7th-8th centuries AH, a period of political and intellectual upheaval.
His lifespan helps contextualize his works.
3
Identify the full title and its alternate
The main title is 'Al-Radd 'ala al-Mantiqiyyin' with an alternate 'Nasihat Ahl al-Iman fi al-Radd 'ala Mantiq al-Yunan'. This shows the dual purpose: refutation and advice.
The word 'Nasihat' (advice) indicates a pastoral concern.
4
Understand who 'al-mantiqiyyin' are
The term refers to the logicians, especially those adhering to Greek logic. Ibn Taymiyya critiques their claim that logic is the exclusive path to sound reasoning.
This is key to his overall argument.
5
Trace the scholarly chain on this edition
Note the Turkish scholar who introduced it, and the editors. This shows the work's transmission and continued relevance.
Modern scholarly apparatus connects us to the text.

Book: The Refutation of the Logicians, also called Advice to the People of Faith in Refuting the Logic of the Greeks. By the eminent Imam, Shaykh al-Islam, the scholar Taqi al-Din Abu al-'Abbas Ahmad ibn 'Abd al-Halim ibn Taymiyya al-'Iraqi, born in the year 661 AH and died in the year 728 AH, may Allah have mercy on him. Presented by the Turkish scholar [unclear] al-Turwi?, died in 1373 AH, director of the journal Ma'arif and judge in the religious court of [Biufal?]. Edited and reviewed for this edition by Shaykh 'Abd al-Samad Sharaf al-Din al-Kibti, Muhammad Talha Bilal Manar, may Allah have mercy on them. Source pages p. 2

Commentary
This passage is the title page of the book 'Radd Mantiqiyyin' (Refutation of the Logicians) by the renowned scholar Ibn Taymiyya. It provides the full title, which also includes a secondary title 'Nasihat Ahl al-Iman fi al-Radd 'ala Mantiq al-Yunan' (Advice to the People of Faith in Refuting the Logic of the Greeks). The author is identified as Imam Taqi al-Din Abu al-'Abbas Ahmad ibn 'Abd al-Halim ibn Taymiyya al-Iraqi, with his birth year 661 AH and death year 728 AH. The passage then mentions a Turkish scholar who introduced the work, though the name is unclear in the OCR. This scholar died in 1373 AH and held positions as director of the journal Ma'arif and a judge in the religious court of a place possibly called Biufal. Finally, the editors of this edition are listed: 'Abd al-Samad Sharaf al-Din al-Kibti and Muhammad Talha Bilal Manar, and the publisher is Mu'assasat al-Rayyan for printing and distribution.

Key Takeaway
The title page of Radd al-Mantiqiyyin immediately establishes Ibn Taymiyya's identity and the central target of his refutation: the logicians who elevate Greek logic to an epistemological absolute.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Using the title page data, write a one-paragraph description of Ibn Taymiyya that includes his full name, lifespan, and the target of his refutation.
?

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Introduction to Ibn Taymiyya's Critique of Greek Logic
Reviewer introduces Ibn Taymiyya's work and its historical significance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Ibn Taymiyya considered Greek logic harmful to Islamic creed and how his critique aimed to distinguish truth from falsehood.

Core Idea
Greek logic threatened harmony of naql and aql; Ibn Taymiyya exposed its flaws.

This lesson introduces the historical background of Ibn Taymiyya's 'Refutation of the Logicians'. The reviewer describes how Greek logic entered the Islamic world and caused conflict between revelation and reason. You will learn why Ibn Taymiyya's critical examination was necessary and what distinguished his approach.

Guided Path
1
Identify the historical context
Greek logic entered the Islamic world through translations of ancient sciences (ʿulūm al-awāʾil). Note the reviewer's phrase 'invaded' (iqtaḥama) to describe its entry.
2
Recognize the problem
Uncritical acceptance of Greek premises as unquestionable truths (musallamāt) led to a perceived contradiction between transmitted knowledge (naql) and reason (ʿaql), causing disputes in creed.
3
Understand Ibn Taymiyya's role
Ibn Taymiyya, armed with transmitted sciences (ʿulūm al-naql), took up the defense. He examined Greek logic with scrutiny (nadhara fīhi nadhrat al-fāḥiṣ al-mudaqqiq).
4
Note the outcome
The result was 'The Book of Refutation of the Logicians' (Kitāb al-Radd ʿalā al-Mantiqiyyīn), where he distinguished truth from falsehood in logical matters.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم
مقدمة المراجع
الحمد لله الذي هدانا للإسلام وجعلنا من أمة سيد الأنام، محمد بن عبد الله عليه الصلاة والسلام أحمده سبحانه وتعالى وأشكره، هدى من شاء برحمته وفضله، ففاز بالمغفرة والرضوان، وأضل من شاء بعدله وحكمته، فباء بالإثم والخُسْران، وأشهد أن لا إله إلا الله وحده لا شريك له، وأشهد أن محمداً عبده ورسوله، اللهم صل وسلم وبارك عليه وعلى آله وصحبه أجمعين، والتابعين ومن تبعهم بإحسان إلى يوم الدين.
وبعد: فهذا سفر جليل للناقد البصير، الإمام شيخ الإسلام أحمد عبد الحليم ابن تيمية رحمه الله تعالى في نقد المنطق (اليوناني) الذي اقتحم العالم الإسلامي عند ترجمة علوم الأوائل. ولقد أدى التأثر به واعتبار قضاياه مسلمات لا يتطرق إليها الشكّ إلى التنافر بين النقل والعقل وجرَّ إلى كثير من الخصومات في مسائل العقيدة .
ولم يأل المتبصرون من أئمة العلم يحذرون من الخوض فيه والولوج في مضايقه، إلى أن تسلَّم راية الدفاع عن الإسلام في القرن السابع الإمام المجاهد الناقد ابن تيمية رحمه الله تعالى فقام بالكشف عن دخائل هذا الفن وتمييز صوابه من خطئه ، ونظر فيه نظرة الفاحص المدقق، بعد أن تسلّح بعلوم النقل بحيث لا تزعزعـه الترهات، وكان نتيجة هذه الدراسة الفاحصة : هذا الكتاب المسمى «كتاب الرد على المنطقيين» الذي اختصره الإمام السيوطي رحمه الله تعالى في كتابه «جَهْدُ القَرِيحة في تجريد النصيحة» وفيه سمى كتاب ابن تيمية باسم آخر وهو : نصيحة أهل الإيمان في
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful.
Introduction of the Reviewer
Praise be to Allah who guided us to Islam and made us from the nation of the master of mankind, Muhammad ibn Abdullah, peace and blessings be upon him. I praise Him, glorified and exalted, and thank Him. He guides whom He wills by His mercy and grace, so they attain forgiveness and pleasure, and He misguides whom He wills by His justice and wisdom, so they incur sin and loss. I bear witness that there is no god but Allah alone, with no partner, and I bear witness that Muhammad is His servant and messenger. O Allah, send blessings, peace, and benedictions upon him, upon his family, his companions, the followers, and those who follow them in righteousness until the Day of Judgment.
To proceed: This is a magnificent work by the insightful critic, the Imam, Shaykh al-Islam Ahmad ibn Abd al-Halim ibn Taymiyya, may Allah have mercy on him, critiquing (Greek) logic which invaded the Islamic world with the translation of the ancient sciences. The influence of this logic and the consideration of its premises as unquestionable truths led to a contradiction between transmitted knowledge and reason, and caused many disputes in matters of creed.
The insightful scholars of the ummah did not cease warning against delving into it and entering its difficulties, until in the seventh century the Imam, the mujahid critic Ibn Taymiyya, may Allah have mercy on him, took up the banner of defending Islam. He uncovered the intricacies of this art and distinguished its truth from falsehood, examining it with the scrutiny of a meticulous investigator, after arming himself with the transmitted sciences such that falsehoods could not shake him. The result of this thorough study is this book called 'The Book of Refutation of the Logicians', which Imam al-Suyuti, may Allah have mercy on him, abridged in his book 'Jahd al-Qariha fi Tajrid al-Nasiha', where he named Ibn Taymiyya's book by another name: 'Nasiha Ahl al-Iman fi...'
Source pages p. 5

Commentary
This passage is an introductory preface (muqaddima) written by a reviewer, not by Ibn Taymiyya himself. It opens with the basmala and hamdala, followed by praise of the Prophet. The reviewer then describes Ibn Taymiyya's book as a 'magnificent work' (safar jaleel) by an 'insightful critic' (naaqid baseer). The reviewer explains the historical context: Greek logic entered the Islamic world through translation of ancient sciences (tr. 'ulum al-awa'il). The uncritical acceptance of Greek logic as unquestionable truths (musallamat la yataraqqa ilayha al-shakk) led to a perceived conflict between transmitted knowledge (naql) and reason ('aql), and caused many disputes in matters of creed (masa'il al-'aqeeda). The reviewer notes that until the seventh century, scholars warned against engaging with logic, but then Ibn Taymiyya took up the defense, uncovering its inner workings and distinguishing truth from falsehood. Ibn Taymiyya, armed with transmitted sciences (ulum al-naql), examined logic with scrutiny. The result is this book, 'Kitab al-Radd 'ala al-Mantiqiyyin', later abbreviated by al-Suyuti. The reviewer's introduction sets the stage for the critical content that follows, emphasizing the harm of Greek logic and the necessity of Ibn Taymiyya's corrective work.

Key Terms
المنطق اليوناني
النقد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the reviewer, what negative effect did the adoption of Greek logic have on the Islamic world?
A) It led to the decline of grammar studies.
B) It caused conflict between transmitted knowledge and reason, and disputes in creed.
C) It was unanimously rejected by all scholars.
D) It had no effect on Islamic thought.

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya's critique did not reject all logic but aimed to separate valid reasoning from imported philosophical assumptions that conflict with Islamic revelation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Based on the passage, summarize in one sentence the negative impact of uncritically accepting Greek logic according to the reviewer.
?
Think of one example from Islamic theology where accepting a philosophical principle uncritically could lead to a contradiction with revelation (e.g., the issue of divine attributes). How might Ibn Taymiyya's approach help?

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Understanding the Context of Ibn Taymiyya's Refutation of Greek Logic
Editor introduces Ibn Taymiyya's critique of Greek logic and describes this corrected edition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Ibn Taymiyya wrote 'al-Radd 'ala al-Mantiqiyyin' and identify the key editorial features of this corrected edition.

Core Idea
Ibn Taymiyya's refutation of Greek logic aims to restore harmony between revelation and reason.

In this introductory passage, the editor of Ibn Taymiyya's 'Refutation of the Logicians' sets the stage for one of the most important critiques of philosophical logic in Islamic history. You will learn why this book was written, what problems Greek logic caused, and how the present edition corrects previous errors to provide a reliable text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Problem
Read the passage to find how Greek logic affected the Islamic world. Note the phrase 'led to a contradiction between transmitted knowledge and reason'.
2
Recognize the Response
Identify Ibn Taymiyya's role: he scrutinized logic after arming himself with transmitted sciences, distinguishing truth from falsehood.
3
Note the Textual History
Observe that the book has two titles, and earlier editions suffered from copyist errors. The editor explains the need for a corrected edition.
4
Understand the Current Edition's Improvements
List the two features mentioned: complete correction of typographical errors and modern typesetting with diacritical marks.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم
مقدمة المراجع
الحمد لله الذي هدانا للإسلام وجعلنا من أمة سيد الأنام، محمد بن عبد الله عليه الصلاة والسلام أحمده سبحانه وتعالى وأشكره، هدى من شاء برحمته وفضله، ففاز بالمغفرة والرضوان، وأضل من شاء بعدله وحكمته، فباء بالإثم والخُسْران، وأشهد أن لا إله إلا الله وحده لا شريك له، وأشهد أن محمداً عبده ورسوله، اللهم صل وسلم وبارك عليه وعلى آله وصحبه أجمعين، والتابعين ومن تبعهم بإحسان إلى يوم الدين.
وبعد: فهذا سفر جليل للناقد البصير، الإمام شيخ الإسلام أحمد عبد الحليم ابن تيمية رحمه الله تعالى في نقد المنطق (اليوناني) الذي اقتحم العالم الإسلامي عند ترجمة علوم الأوائل. ولقد أدى التأثر به واعتبار قضاياه مسلمات لا يتطرق إليها الشكّ إلى التنافر بين النقل والعقل وجرَّ إلى كثير من الخصومات في مسائل العقيدة .
ولم يأل المتبصرون من أئمة العلم يحذرون من الخوض فيه والولوج في مضايقه، إلى أن تسلَّم راية الدفاع عن الإسلام في القرن السابع الإمام المجاهد الناقد ابن تيمية رحمه الله تعالى فقام بالكشف عن دخائل هذا الفن وتمييز صوابه من خطئه ، ونظر فيه نظرة الفاحص المدقق، بعد أن تسلّح بعلوم النقل بحيث لا تزعزعـه الترهات، وكان نتيجة هذه الدراسة الفاحصة : هذا الكتاب المسمى «كتاب الرد على المنطقيين» الذي اختصره الإمام السيوطي رحمه الله تعالى في كتابه «جَهْدُ القَرِيحة في تجريد النصيحة» وفيه سمى كتاب ابن تيمية باسم آخر وهو : نصيحة أهل الإيمان في الردّ على منطق «اليونان ولكن الاسم الأول هو الذي كتب على النسخة الأصل، ولذا اقتصر عليه المحقق الشيخ عبد الصمد شرف الدین رحمه الله تعالى عندما قام بنشر الكتاب لأول مرة سنة ١٣٦٨، ونحن في طبعتنا هذه جمعنا بين الاسمين مع تقديم الأول.
وكان الكتاب قد طبع على نفقة المغفور له الملك عبد العزيز بن عبد الرحمن آل سعود رحمه الله تعالى .
والمحقق الشيخ عبد الصمد شرف الدین رحمه الله تعالى، كان قد فاته في طبعته الأولى تصحيح الكتاب بسبب عدم دقة الناسخ الذي نسخ الكتاب من الأصل ولما قام بمقابلة الكتابة بالأصل بعد أن طبع قدراً كبيراً من الكتاب، ذُهل لكثرة الأخطاء والفروقات، فاضطر إلى إصدار ملحق بالأخطاء في آخر الكتاب . ثم صُوّر الكتاب في الباكستان في سنة ١٣٩٦ وما بعدها مرات عدة مع تصحيح ما أمكن من الأخطاء، ولكن بقي فيه مع ذلك أشياء مهمة لم يتم تصحيحها .
وقد نَفِدت نسخ الكتاب منذ مدة، ولم يُعد تصويره فرأينا مع حلول الذكرى المئوية لتأسيس المملكة العربية السعودية إعادة نشر الكتاب إحياء للمآثر العلمية للملك الراحل رحمه الله تعالى .
فاستأنفنا النظر في الكتاب لإعداده للطباعة، فاستكملنا تصحيح الكتاب، وأضفنا الأسقاط المشار إليها في ملحق الأخطاء في الطبعة الأولى، وأنزلنا ما استدركه المحقق من التراجم في مواضعها من الكتاب .
وباختصار، فإن هذه الطبعة تمتاز بما يلي :
١ - التصحيح التام لجميع الأغلاط المطبعية وإضافة الأسقاط والاستدراكات المثبتة في آخر الطبعة الأولى.
٢ - إعادة صف الكتاب بالحروف الطباعية الحديثة، مع زيادة شكل الألفاظ المشكلة.
In the name of God, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful.
Introduction of the Reviewer
Praise be to God who guided us to Islam and made us of the nation of the Master of Mankind, Muhammad ibn Abdullah, peace and blessings be upon him. I praise Him, exalted is He, and thank Him. He guides whom He wills by His mercy and favor, so he attains forgiveness and pleasure, and He leads astray whom He wills by His justice and wisdom, so he incurs sin and loss. I bear witness that there is no god but God alone, with no partner, and I bear witness that Muhammad is His servant and Messenger. O God, send blessings and peace and blessings upon him, upon his family, his companions altogether, the followers, and those who follow them in goodness until the Day of Judgment.
To proceed: This is a noble work of the perceptive critic, Imam Sheikh al-Islam Ahmad ibn Abd al-Halim Ibn Taymiyya, may God have mercy on him, concerning the critique of (Greek) logic, which invaded the Islamic world upon the translation of the sciences of the ancients. Indeed, being influenced by it and considering its premises as unquestionable axioms led to a contradiction between transmitted knowledge and reason, and dragged into many disputes in matters of creed.
The insightful scholars of knowledge did not cease warning against delving into it and entering its difficulties, until in the seventh century the banner of defense of Islam was taken up by the mujahid critic Ibn Taymiyya, may God have mercy on him. He uncovered the intricacies of this art and distinguished its truth from its falsehood, and examined it with the scrutiny of a thorough investigator, after having armed himself with the transmitted sciences such that falsehoods could not shake him. The result of this thorough study was this book called 'The Book of Refutation of the Logicians' which Imam al-Suyuti, may God have mercy on him, summarized in his book 'Juhd al-Qariha fi Tajrid al-Nasiha', in which he named Ibn Taymiyya's book by another name: 'Nasiha Ahl al-Iman fi al-Radd 'ala Mantiq al-Yunan'. However, the first name is the one written on the original manuscript, so the editor Sheikh Abd al-Samad Sharaf al-Din, may God have mercy on him, restricted himself to it when he published the book for the first time in 1368 AH. In this edition of ours, we have combined the two names while giving precedence to the first.
The book was printed at the expense of the late King Abd al-Aziz ibn Abd al-Rahman Al Saud, may God have mercy on him.
The editor Sheikh Abd al-Samad Sharaf al-Din, may God have mercy on him, missed correcting the book in his first edition due to the inaccuracy of the copyist who copied the book from the original. When he compared the text with the original after having printed a large part of the book, he was astonished by the abundance of errors and differences, so he was compelled to issue an appendix of errors at the end of the book. Then the book was reproduced in Pakistan in 1396 AH and several times thereafter, with correction of as many errors as possible, but important matters remained uncorrected.
Copies of the book have been out of print for some time, and it was not reprinted. So we saw, with the advent of the centennial of the founding of the Kingdom of Saudi Arabia, the re-publication of the book to revive the scholarly achievements of the late king, may God have mercy on him.
So we resumed examining the book to prepare it for printing. We completed the correction of the book, added the missing parts indicated in the appendix of errors in the first edition, and inserted the biographical entries that the editor had added into their proper places in the book.
In short, this edition is distinguished by the following:
1. Complete correction of all typographical errors and addition of the omissions and emendations recorded at the end of the first edition.
2. Re-typesetting of the book in modern typography, with increased diacritical marks on problematic words.
Source pages p. 5

Commentary
This passage is the editor's introduction to the new edition of Ibn Taymiyya's 'Radd ala al-Mantiqiyyin'. It begins with the basmala and a praise of God, then introduces the book as a noble work critiquing Greek logic, which had caused a conflict between transmitted knowledge and reason in the Islamic world. The editor notes that earlier scholars warned against this logic, but Ibn Taymiyya took up the defense and scrutinized it, producing this book. The book has two names: the original 'Kitab al-Radd 'ala al-Mantiqiyyin' and al-Suyuti's summary title 'Nasiha Ahl al-Iman'. The editor explains that the previous edition used only the first name, but this edition combines both. The history of the text includes errors in the first edition due to a copyist, leading to an appendix of corrections. Later reproductions in Pakistan corrected some errors but left many. The current edition aims to complete the corrections, add missing parts, and re-typeset the text with proper diacritics. The passage concludes by listing two features of the new edition: complete typographic correction and modern typesetting with diacriticals.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
8 min
Critical Editions: How Textual Accuracy Shapes Islamic Knowledge
Editor describes corrections and additions in the new edition of Radd Mantiqiyyin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the features of a critical edition and explain their role in preserving the integrity of Islamic texts.

Core Idea
A critical edition safeguards the author's original argument from scribal corruption.

This preface details the editorial work behind the new edition of Ibn Taymiyya's Radd al-Mantiqiyyin. While it may seem like mere bookkeeping, each correction and addition is a tool for recovering what the author actually wrote. Understanding these features helps you assess the reliability of any published Islamic source.

Guided Path
1
Identify the editorial problem
The first edition had many errors due to an inaccurate scribe. The editor was forced to add an appendix of corrections. This shows that even printed texts can contain significant mistakes.
2
List the five features of the new edition
The text enumerates five improvements: complete correction of typographical errors, resetting with modern type and diacritics, inclusion of a scholar's introduction, inclusion of all photographs from the original, and preservation of original page numbers for cross-reference.
3
Classify each feature by function
Some features restore the original text (corrections, photographs), others add supplementary material (introduction, indices), and others aid citation (page numbers). Each serves a distinct purpose in making the edition more faithful and usable.
4
Assess the scholarly impact of omitted material
The introduction by Sayyid Sulayman al-Nadwi was omitted in Pakistani editions. This shows how editorial decisions can deprive scholars of valuable context. A complete edition includes all paratexts.
5
Reflect on the role of the editor (muhaqqiq)
The editor is not just a publisher; he is a scholar who compares manuscripts, corrects errors, and provides apparatus. Without his work, the text's reliability is compromised.
The term 'muhaqqiq' implies verification and accuracy.

الردّ على منطق «اليونان» ولكن الاسم الأول هو الذي كتب على النسخة الأصل، ولذا اقتصر عليه المحقق الشيخ عبد الصمد شرف الدين رحمه الله تعالى عندما قام بنشر الكتاب لأول مرة سنة ١٣٦٨، ونحن في طبعتنا هذه جمعنا بين الاسمين مع تقديم الأول.
وكان الكتاب قد طبع على نفقة المغفور له الملك عبد العزيز بن عبد الرحمن آل سعود رحمه الله تعالى.
والمحقق الشيخ عبد الصمد شرف الدين رحمه الله تعالى، كان قد فاته في طبعته الأولى تصحيح الكتاب بسبب عدم دقة الناسخ الذي نسخ الكتاب من الأصل ولما قام بمقابلة الكتابة بالأصل بعد أن طبع قدراً كبيراً من الكتاب، ذُهل لكثرة الأخطاء والفروقات، فاضطر إلى إصدار ملحق بالأخطاء في آخر الكتاب. ثم صُوّر الكتاب في الباكستان في سنة ١٣٩٦ وما بعدها مرات عدة مع تصحيح ما أمكن من الأخطاء، ولكن بقي فيه مع ذلك أشياء مهمة لم يتم تصحيحها.
وقد نَفِدت نسخ الكتاب منذ مدة، ولم يُعد تصويره فرأينا مع حلول الذكرى المئوية لتأسيس المملكة العربية السعودية إعادة نشر الكتاب إحياء للمآثر العلمية للملك الراحل رحمه الله تعالى.
فاستأنفنا النظر في الكتاب لإعداده للطباعة، فاستكملنا تصحيح الكتاب، وأضفنا الأسقاط المشار إليها في ملحق الأخطاء في الطبعة الأولى، وأنزلنا ما استدركه المحقق من التراجم في مواضعها من الكتاب.
وباختصار، فإن هذه الطبعة تمتاز بما يلي:
١ - التصحيح التام لجميع الأغلاط المطبعية وإضافة الأسقاط والاستدراكات المثبتة في آخر الطبعة الأولى.
٢ - إعادة صف الكتاب بالحروف الطباعية الحديثة، مع زيادة شكل الألفاظ المشكلة.
٣ - إثبات مقدمة العلامة السيد سليمان الندوي المتوفى سنة ۱۳۷۳ رحمه الله تعالى، وهي مقدمة مهمّة لعالم متمكن مُنْصِف، وفيها الكشف عن كيفية وصول نسخة هذا الكتاب الأصلية إلى الهند ثم إلى المكتبة الآصفية بحيدرآباد حيث هي الآن، وفيها بيان اغتباط بعض علماء الهند بهذا الكتاب ونسخه والنقل منه وفيها المحقق الشيخ عبد الصمد رحمه الله تعالى في نشر هذا الكتاب، إلى غير ذلك من المعلومات المهمة. ومع ذلك جرى حذف هذه المقدمة من الطبعات الباكستانية!
٤ - إثبات جميع الصور المأخوذة عن النسخة الأصل، وهي تسع صور أثبتها المحقق الشيخ عبد الصمد شرف الدين في الطبعة الأولى، وأشار إلى أرقامها في مقدمته، ولكن سقطت بعض الصور في الطبعات الباكستانية.
ه - نظراً لأن الطبعة الأولى ومصوراتها بقيت متداولة في أيدي العلماء والباحثين وجرى الاعتماد عليها في النقل والعزو، فإنه حين أعدنا صف الكتاب، أثبتنا أرقام صفحات الطبعة الأولى السابقة، حتى يتيسر الاستفادة من الطبعتين مع سهولة الوصول إلى المطلوب.
بقيت أمنية واحدة كنا نود لو تحققت وهي أن محقق الكتاب الشيخ عبد الصمد رحمه الله تعالى، أشار في مقدمته (ص) (۳۰) أنه عمل فهارس مفيدة للكتابة: مثل فهرس الأعلام، والكتب والأماكن والفرق، وأنه ينوي عمل فهرس عام للموضوعات مرتب على حروف المعجم، وأن هذه الفهارس لم يتيسر طبعها لضيق الوقت. ونحن لو كنا وقفنا على هذه الفهارس لما ترددنا في إلحاقها بهذه الطبعة، ولن نتردد في المستقبل بإذن الله تعالى.

۱ - منطق ابن تيمية ومنهجه الفكري للدكتور محمد حسني الزين، صدر
Preface of the Reviewer. The refutation of the logic of the Greeks, but the first name is the one written on the original copy, so the investigator Sheikh Abd al-Samad Sharaf al-Din, may Allah have mercy on him, limited himself to it when he published the book for the first time in the year 1368. And we, in this our edition, combined the two names with the precedence of the first. The book was printed at the expense of the late King Abd al-Aziz ibn Abd al-Rahman Al Saud, may Allah have mercy on him. The investigator Sheikh Abd al-Samad Sharaf al-Din, may Allah have mercy on him, had missed correcting the book in his first edition due to the inaccuracy of the scribe who copied the book from the original. When he compared the writing with the original after having printed a large amount of the book, he was astonished at the abundance of errors and differences, so he was forced to issue an appendix of errors at the end of the book. Then the book was reproduced in Pakistan in the year 1396 and thereafter several times with correction of as many errors as possible, but there remained some important things that were not corrected. The copies of the book ran out some time ago, and it was not reprinted. So we, upon the occasion of the centenary of the founding of the Kingdom of Saudi Arabia, decided to republish the book to revive the scholarly achievements of the late king, may Allah have mercy on him. We then renewed our examination of the book to prepare it for printing. We completed the correction of the book, added the omissions indicated in the appendix of errors in the first edition, and placed the biographical notices that the investigator had added in their proper places in the book. In short, this edition is distinguished by the following: 1 - Complete correction of all typographical errors and addition of the omissions and corrections recorded at the end of the first edition. 2 - Resetting the book in modern type, with addition of diacritical marks to problematic words. 3 - Including the introduction of the scholar Sayyid Sulayman al-Nadwi, who died in 1373 AH, may Allah have mercy on him. It is an important introduction by a competent and fair scholar, containing the disclosure of how the original copy of this book reached India and then the Asafiyya Library in Hyderabad where it now resides, and containing the expression of delight of some scholars of India at this book, and its copying and quotation from it, and also concerning the investigator Sheikh Abd al-Samad, may Allah have mercy on him, in publishing this book, and other important information. Nevertheless, this introduction was omitted from the Pakistani editions! 4 - Including all the photographs taken from the original copy, which are nine pictures that the investigator Sheikh Abd al-Samad Sharaf al-Din included in the first edition, and he referred to their numbers in his introduction, but some pictures were dropped in the Pakistani editions. 5 - Because the first edition and its reproductions remained in circulation among scholars and researchers and were relied upon for quotation and attribution, when we reset the book, we included the page numbers of the earlier first edition, so that benefit may be had from both editions with ease of access to what is sought. One wish remained that we hoped would be realized: namely, that the investigator of the book, Sheikh Abd al-Samad, may Allah have mercy on him, indicated in his introduction (p. 30) that he had prepared useful indices for the book, such as an index of names, books, places, and sects, and that he intended to make a general index of subjects arranged alphabetically, and that these indices were not printed due to lack of time. And if we had come across these indices, we would not have hesitated to append them to this edition, and we will not hesitate in the future, Allah willing. Commentary
This passage is the editor's preface to the new edition of Ibn Taymiyya's Radd Mantiqiyyin. It opens by discussing the title of the book: the first name (The Refutation of the Logic of the Greeks) was written on the original manuscript, and the first editor Sheikh Abd al-Samad relied on that. The present edition combines both names but prefers the first. It then states that the book was originally printed at the expense of King Abd al-Aziz. The editor explains the problems of the first edition: the scribe made many errors, and after printing a large portion, the investigator was shocked by the discrepancies, so he issued an appendix of errors. Later Pakistani editions corrected some but not all mistakes. Due to the centenary of Saudi Arabia, this new edition was undertaken. The improvements are enumerated: 1) complete correction of typographical errors and inclusion of omitted parts; 2) resetting with modern type and diacritics; 3) inclusion of an important introduction by Sayyid Sulayman al-Nadwi (missing from Pakistani editions); 4) inclusion of all nine photographs from the original; 5) preserving original page numbers for cross-reference. Finally, the editor laments that the original investigator's planned indices were never found, but hopes to include them in the future. The passage concludes with a reference to a study about Ibn Taymiyya's logic. The overall style is that of an editorial report, recounting the history of the edition and its features.

Editorial Decisions and Textual Authenticity
Reviewer describes editorial choices and lists studies on the book.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the reliability of a critical edition by analyzing its inclusion of original introductions, facsimiles, and page numbering.

Core Idea
A critical edition's value lies in its fidelity to the original manuscript and its scholarly apparatus.

When studying a classical Islamic text like Ibn Taymiyya's *Radd 'ala al-Mantiqiyyin*, the edition you use matters. The reviewer's introduction explains three key editorial decisions: restoring the original introduction by Sayyid Sulayman al-Nadwi, including all facsimiles, and retaining original page numbers. Understanding these choices helps you assess the edition's trustworthiness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the editorial decisions
The reviewer lists three main actions: adding al-Nadwi's introduction, including all nine facsimiles, and keeping original page numbers. List these three decisions.
2
Consider what was omitted in other editions
The reviewer notes that Pakistani editions deleted the introduction and some facsimiles. Reflect on why such omissions might occur—cost, neglect, or deliberate choice.
3
Assess the impact on research
How does each decision affect a scholar's ability to verify references? The introduction provides provenance, facsimiles allow checking the original, and page numbers enable cross-referencing with earlier scholarship.
4
Evaluate the reviewer's transparency
The reviewer admits that the indexes prepared by the editor were not included (due to unavailability). How does this honesty affect your trust in the edition?

الناشر والمراجع
Introduction of the Reviewer
3 - Affixing the introduction of the scholar Sayyid Sulayman al-Nadwi, who died in the year 1373 AH, may Allah have mercy on him. It is an important introduction by a competent, fair scholar. In it is the disclosure of how the original copy of this book arrived in India and then to the Asifiyya Library in Hyderabad where it is now, and in it is the expression of delight of some Indian scholars with this book, copying it, and quoting from it, and in it is the editor Sheikh Abd al-Samad, may Allah have mercy on him, regarding the publication of this book, and other important pieces of information. Yet this introduction was deleted from the Pakistani editions!
4 - Affixing all the facsimiles taken from the original copy, which are nine facsimiles that the editor Sheikh Abd al-Samad Sharaf al-Din included in the first edition, and he indicated their numbers in his introduction, but some facsimiles were omitted in the Pakistani editions.
5 - Because the first edition and its facsimiles remained in circulation among scholars and researchers and were relied upon for citation and referencing, when we revised the book, we fixed the page numbers of the previous first edition, so that both editions can be utilized with ease of access to what is desired.
One wish remained that we wished had been fulfilled: that the editor of the book, Sheikh Abd al-Samad, may Allah have mercy on him, indicated in his introduction (p. 30) that he had prepared useful indexes for the writing, such as an index of proper names, books, places, and sects, and that he intended to prepare a general subject index arranged alphabetically, and that these indexes were not printed due to lack of time. Had we come across these indexes, we would not have hesitated to append them to this edition, and we will not hesitate in the future, by Allah's permission.
Now, important studies have been published about this book, explaining the status and authenticity of this book, among them:
1 - 'The Logic of Ibn Taymiyya and His Intellectual Method' by Dr. Muhammad Husni al-Zain, published by al-Maktab al-Islami in Beirut in the year 1399 AH.
2 - 'The Roots of the Science of Occidentalism: A Stop with the Refutation of the Logicians by Ibn Taymiyya' by Dr. Mahmud Madi, published by Dar al-Da'wa in Alexandria in the year 1416 AH.
- 'Muslim Thinkers Facing Greek Logic' by Mr. Mustafa Tabatabai, in which the eighth chapter is titled 'Ibn Taymiyya, the Great Critic of Logic', an important chapter rich with benefits.
And other studies that I have not come across.
This is the summary of the preface to this edition. I ask Allah, the Exalted, to make it beneficial and to grant ample reward to everyone who contributed to the publication of this rare book. May Allah bless our master Muhammad and his family and companions, and praise be to Allah, Lord of the worlds.
The Publisher and Reviewer

Commentary
This passage is the reviewer's introduction to the new edition of Ibn Taymiyya's *Radd Mantiqiyyin*. The reviewer explains several editorial decisions made for this edition. First, he includes the important introduction by Sayyid Sulayman al-Nadwi, which reveals the journey of the original manuscript to India and its eventual location at the Asifiyya Library in Hyderabad. He notes that this introduction was unfortunately omitted in Pakistani editions. Second, he includes all nine facsimiles from the original manuscript that were part of the first edition, as some were dropped in later Pakistani editions. Third, he retains the page numbers of the first edition to facilitate cross-referencing. The reviewer then mentions a regret that the indexes prepared by the original editor, Sheikh Abd al-Samad, were not available for inclusion, but expresses hope to add them in the future. Finally, he lists three significant studies on Ibn Taymiyya's logic and the *Radd Mantiqiyyin*, giving publication details. The passage concludes with a prayer for benefit and gratitude.

صور فوتوغرافية
أرقام الصفحات
فهارس

Understanding the Editor's Preface in Scholarly Works
Editor concludes the preface with a prayer and acknowledgments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the role of the editor's preface in framing a critical work like Ibn Taymiyya's *Refutation of the Logicians* and recognize how it establishes scholarly credibility.

Core Idea
An editor's preface anchors the work in a tradition of critique and scholarship.

This passage concludes the editor's preface to a modern edition of Ibn Taymiyya's *al-Radd 'ala al-Mantiqiyyin*. While it does not contain logical argumentation, it reveals how the editor positions the work within existing scholarship. Understanding this framing helps you evaluate the authority of the edition you are reading.

Guided Path
1
Identify the bibliographic references
List the sources the editor mentions (e.g., book from Beirut, study by Dr. Mahmoud Madi, work by Mustafa Tabatabai). Consider why the editor includes these—they establish the scholarly lineage of this edition.
These references show that the editor has consulted prior studies, lending credibility to the edition.
2
Note the editor's stated purpose
The editor says this is a 'brief statement in the introduction of this edition.' He asks Allah to make it beneficial. This indicates his intent to serve the Muslim scholarly community.
3
Analyze the closing prayer (du'a)
The editor ends with praise of Allah and blessings on the Prophet. This is a standard scholarly practice that underscores the religious nature of the work and the editor's humility.
Prayer in such contexts asserts that the work is for Allah's sake, not worldly gain.
4
Evaluate the editor's signing
The editor signs as 'al-Nashir wa al-Muraji'' (the publisher and reviewer). This dual role implies he is responsible for both production and scholarly accuracy.
Recognizing the editor's role helps assess the potential biases or strengths of the edition.

Preface of the reviewer. The book from the Islamic Office in Beirut, year 1399. 2 - Roots of the science of Occidentalism: a pause with the Refutation of the Logicians by Ibn Taymiyya, by Dr. Mahmoud Madi, published by Dar al-Da'wa in Alexandria, year 1416. - 'Muslim Thinkers Facing Greek Logic' by Mr. Mustafa Tabatabai, in which the eighth chapter is titled (Ibn Taymiyya, the Great Critic of Logic), an important chapter full of benefits. And other studies that I have not come across. This is a brief statement in the introduction of this edition. I ask Allah, the Exalted, to make it beneficial widely, and to reward abundantly everyone who contributed to the publication of this rare book. May Allah bless our master Muhammad and his family and companions, and praise be to Allah, Lord of the worlds. The publisher and reviewer.
Source pages p. 8

Commentary
This passage is the conclusion of the editor's preface (muqaddimat al-muraji'). It lists some references and studies related to Ibn Taymiyya's critique of logic, then closes with a prayer. The editor acknowledges the sources he consulted, including the book's original publication details and modern studies. He then expresses hope that this edition brings benefit and asks Allah for reward for all who contributed. This is typical of Islamic scholarly works where the editor ends with praise and prayer. The passage is front matter and not part of the main logical argument, but it sets the stage for the reader.

Key Terms
مقدمة (muqaddima): Preface or introduction written by the reviewer/editor of this edition.
الرد على المنطقيين (al-radd 'ala al-mantiqiyyin): Title of Ibn Taymiyya's work; 'The Refutation of the Logicians'.

Navigating Ibn Taymiyya's Refutation via its Table of Contents
Index listing the main sections and topics of the book.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to extract the main argumentative structure of Ibn Taymiyya's 'Refutation of the Logicians' from its table of contents.

Core Idea
The table of contents is a roadmap to Ibn Taymiyya's systematic dismantling of Greek logic.

This lesson uses the index of Ibn Taymiyya's 'Refutation of the Logicians' to show you how he organises his critique. By understanding the book's structure, you can trace his argument against the logicians' theory of definition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four maqamat
The index mentions four 'stations' (maqamat). Find them in the Arabic. Only the first two are detailed here, but note the overall plan.
2
Extract the main claim of the first maqam
Look at the title of the first maqam: 'On refuting their claim that concepts (tasawwurat) are only attained through definition (hadd).' What specific claim is being attacked?
3
Count the proofs against it
The index lists eleven pieces of evidence (adilla) against the logicians' claim. List them mentally or note the numbering.
The proofs range from circularity to empirical sufficiency.
4
Identify the second maqam's target
The second maqam refutes the claim that definition yields knowledge. Note that it includes a discussion of al-Ghazali's view and the artificial nature of definition.

Index of the book 'The Refutation of the Logicians'. Subject: Preface of the reviewer. Preface of the scholar Sayyid Suleiman al-Nadwi. Preface of the publisher. Preface of the author. Summary of the principles of logic and its terminology; discourse in four stations. The first station: On refuting their claim that concepts (tasawwurat) are only attained through definition (hadd). Evidence of its falsehood: First: The foundation of logic is speaking without knowledge. Second: Defining the limited by another definition entails circularity. Third: The particulars of sciences are conceptualized without definitions. Fourth: A straight definition is not known according to their principles. Fifth: The real definition is either impossible or difficult. Sixth: Knowing species without definition is better than knowing what has no composition. Seventh: The priority of conceptualizing the meaning over knowing the indication of the word upon it. Eighth: The possibility of conceptualizing meaning without a word. Ninth: All existents are perceived by man through his senses only. Tenth: Refutation and objection cannot occur except after conceptualizing the limited without the definition. Eleventh: Self-evidence and discursive reasoning are not necessary concomitants of information. The second station: On refuting their claim that definition yields knowledge. Imam al-Ghazali's view on logic. The benefit of definition according to the theologians. Al-Ghazali's admission of the impossibility of definition in the standard of knowledge. The refutation of al-Ghazali's statement. The art of definition is an artificial, non-instinctive convention. The mixing of the articles of the logicians with the prophetic sciences. Evidence of its falsehood: First: The definition does not yield knowledge of the defined. (Innovation of mentioning the singular name - digression). Second: A single report without proof does not yield knowledge. Third: If the conceptualization of the defined occurred through the definition, it would occur before knowledge of the validity of the definition. Fourth: Knowledge of the defined depends only on knowledge of the named and its name. The definition may sometimes prompt an awareness.
Source pages p. 9

Commentary
This passage is the table of contents of Ibn Taymiyya's 'Refutation of the Logicians'. It lists the major sections and subsections of the book, providing a roadmap for the reader. The index shows that the book is structured around four 'stations' (maqamat), but only the first two are detailed in this part. The first station refutes the logicians' claim that concepts (tasawwurat) can only be attained through definition (hadd). It lists eleven proofs against this claim. The second station refutes the claim that definition yields knowledge, and includes a discussion of al-Ghazali's views. The index also includes page numbers, indicating the original pagination. This is a typical feature of classical Islamic works, helping the reader navigate the text. The student should use this index to understand the overall argument of the book: Ibn Taymiyya systematically dismantles the logicians' theory of definition, both as a means of attaining concepts and as a source of knowledge.

Introduction and Front Matter

The Critical Term 'Tasawwurat' in Ibn Taymiyya's Refutation
Introduction to the key term tasawwurat in the context of the table of contents.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish Ibn Taymiyya's critical use of 'tasawwurat' from the standard logicians' definition.

Core Idea
Ibn Taymiyya redefines 'tasawwurat' to attack the very foundation of logical epistemology.

In the table of contents, 'tasawwurat' appears as the first target. Ibn Taymiyya denies that concepts require definition. This lesson unpacks the critical redefinition.

Guided Path
1
Locate 'tasawwurat' in the index
Find the Arabic term 'التصورات' in the table of contents. It appears in the title of the first maqam.
2
Recall the standard meaning
In standard Islamic logic, tasawwurat (conception) is the first type of knowledge, often attained through definition (hadd). This is the view Ibn Taymiyya attacks.
You may recall from earlier lessons that tasawwurat is contrasted with tasdiq (assent).
3
Identify Ibn Taymiyya's claim
The first maqam title says: 'On refuting their claim that concepts are only attained through definition.' So Ibn Taymiyya argues that definition is not necessary for concept-formation.
4
Understand the shift
Ibn Taymiyya is rejecting the necessity and sufficiency of definition for attaining concepts. He offers alternative means: senses, prior knowledge, etc. (as listed in the subsequent proofs).
This shift has profound implications for epistemology.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
10 min
Overview of Ibn Taymiyya's Three Maqamat
Table of contents outlining three maqamat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three main claims of the logicians that Ibn Taymiyya refutes and the number of proofs he presents for each maqam.

Core Idea
Ibn Taymiyya attacks the very foundations of Greek logic: definition and syllogism.

This lesson explores the table of contents of Ibn Taymiyya's Radd Mantiqiyyin, which serves as a roadmap for his systematic refutation of Aristotelian logic. The fihris reveals the author's strategy: three major stations (maqamat) each targeting a core epistemological claim of the logicians. By understanding this structure, you will grasp the scope and organization of his critique before delving into the arguments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three maqam titles
Read the Arabic text and locate the headings for al-maqam al-awwal, al-maqam al-thani, and al-maqam al-thalith. Note the claim being refuted in each.
The first maqam refutes that conceptualizations require definition, the second that definition conveys knowledge, and the third that assents require syllogism.
2
Count the proofs per maqam
Count the numbered subpoints under each maqam. The first maqam has eleven proofs, the second has nine, and the third has four. This shows the relative weight Ibn Taymiyya gives to each issue.
3
Notice references to other scholars
Scan for mentions of al-Ghazali and Ibn Sina in the second maqam. Ibn Taymiyya engages with their views, showing his critique is not just of anonymous logicians but of prominent Islamic thinkers who adopted Greek logic.
Al-Ghazali's 'Mi'yar al-Ilm' and Ibn Sina's 'Shifa' are referenced.
4
Observe the inclusion of non-logical topics
Note the presence of terms like 'translation', 'legal definitions', and 'ijtihad' in the second maqam. This indicates Ibn Taymiyya broadens the discussion to include Islamic jurisprudence.

الأول : أساس المنطق القول بلا علم
الثاني : تعريف المحدود بحد آخر يستلزم الدور
الثالث : تُتَصَوَّر مفردات العلوم بغير الحدود
الرابع : لا يُعلم حدّ مستقيم على أصلهم
الخامس : الحد الحقيقي إما متعذر وإما متعسر
السادس : معرفة الأنواع بغير حد أولى من معرفة ما لا تركيب فيه
السابع : سَبْقية تصور المعنى على العلم بدلالة اللفظ عليه
الثامن : إمكان تصور المعنى بدون اللفظ
التاسع : جميع الموجودات يتصورها الإنسان بمشاعره فقط
العاشر : لا يمكن النقض والمعارضة إلا بعد تصور المحدود بدون الحد
الحادي عشر : البداهة والنظر ليسا من لوازم المعلومات
المقام الثاني
في رد قولهم إن الحد يفيد العلم بالتصورات.
رأى الإمام الغزالي في المنطق فائدة الحد عند المتكلمين
اعتراف الغزالي باستعصاء الحد في معيار العلم.
الرد على كلام الغزالي
صانعة الحد وضع اصطلاحي غير فطري.
خلط مقالات أهل المنطق بالعلوم النبوية.
وجوه الأدلة على بطلانه
الأول : الحد لا يفيد معرفة المحدود. بدعة ذكر الاسم) المفرد) - استطراد
الثاني : خبر الواحد بلا دليل لا يفيد العلم.
الثالث : لو حصل تصور المحدود بالحد لحصل ذلك قبل العلم بصحة الحد
الرابع : معرفة المحدود يتوقف على العلم بالمسمى واسمه فقط
الحد قد يُنَبِّه تنبيهاً
اعتراف ابن سينا بأن من الأمور ما هو متصور بذاته.
التحقيق السديد في مسألة التحديد.
مطلوب السائل المتصوّر للمعنى الجاهل بدلالة اللفظ عليه.
الترجمة وأحكامها.
معرفة الحدود الشرعية من الدين.
أقسام الحدود اللفظية
الاجتهاد والتأويل
فصل: مطلوب السائل الغير المتصورِ للمعنى الجاهل باسمه
الخامس : التصورات المفردة يمتنع أن تكون مطلوبة.
السادس : التفريق بين الذاتي والعَرَضي باطل
الكلام على الفرق بين الماهية ووجودها
الكلام على التفريق بين الذاتي واللازم.
السابع : اشتراط الصفات الذاتية المشتركة أمر وضعي محض.
الثامن : اشتراط ذكر الفصول مع التفريق بين الذاتي واللازم غير ممكن
التاسع : توقف معرفة الذات على معرفة الذاتيات وبالعكس يستلزم الدور
أبحاث في حد العلم والخبر.
المقام الثالث
في رد قولهم إن التصديقات لا تُنال إلا بالقياس
حصر حصول العلم في القياس قول بغير علم
الفرق بين البديهي والنظري أمر نسبي محض
بطلان منعهم الاحتجاج بالمتواترات والمجربات.
إنكار المتواترات هو من أصول الإلحاد
شرك الفلاسفة أشنع من شرك أهل الجاهلية
بطلان دعواهم : لا بد في البرهان من قضية كلية
فساد قولهم بأنه لا بد في كل علم نظري من مقدمتين
القضايا الكلية تعلم بقياس التمثيل
دعواهم في البرهان أنه يفيد العلوم الكمالية
وجوه الأدلة على بطلانه
الأول: البرهان لا يفيد العلم بشيء من الموجودات
الثاني : لا يعلم بالبرهان واجب الوجود إلخ
الثالث : ليس العلم الإلهي عندهم علماً بالخالق ولا بالمخلوق
إيراد لابن المطهر الحلي وتخطئة المصنف له عليه
العلم الأعلى عند المنطقيين ليس علماً بموجود
الرابع: العلم الرياضي لا تكمل به النفوس، وإن ارتاضت به العقول الأسباب المُغرية بالاشتغال بالعلم الرياضي وما أشبهه
Index of the book 'The Refutation of the Logicians'. Topics: Introduction of the reviewer, Introduction of Sayyid Sulayman al-Nadwi, Publisher's introduction, Author's introduction, Summary of the principles of logic and its terminology: discourse in four stations. First station: Refuting their claim that conceptualizations are only attained through definition. Proofs of its falsity: First: The foundation of logic is speaking without knowledge. Second: Defining the defined by another definition entails circularity. Third: The particulars of the sciences are conceptualized without definitions. Fourth: A correct definition is not known according to their principle. Fifth: The real definition is either impossible or difficult. Sixth: Knowing the species without definition is better than knowing that which has no composition. Seventh: The priority of conceptualizing the meaning over knowing the indication of the word upon it. Eighth: The possibility of conceptualizing the meaning without the word. Ninth: All existents are conceptualized by humans only through their senses. Tenth: Refutation and objection cannot occur except after conceptualizing the defined without the definition. Eleventh: Self-evidence and consideration are not necessary attributes of known things. Second station: Refuting their claim that definition conveys knowledge of conceptualizations. The view of Imam al-Ghazali on logic: the benefit of definition according to the theologians. Al-Ghazali's acknowledgment of the impossibility of definition in the Criterion of Knowledge. Refutation of al-Ghazali's statement. The craft of definition is a conventional, non-instinctive postulate. Mixing the articles of the logicians with prophetic sciences. Proofs of its falsity: First: Definition does not convey knowledge of the defined. Innovation of mentioning the (singular) name - digression. Second: A single reporter without evidence does not convey knowledge. Third: If conceptualization of the defined occurred through definition, it would have occurred before knowing the validity of the definition. Fourth: Knowledge of the defined depends on knowledge of the named and its name only. Definition may prompt a prompting. Avicenna's acknowledgment that some matters are intrinsically conceptualized. The sound investigation concerning the issue of definition. The seeker who conceptualizes the meaning but is ignorant of its linguistic indication. Translation and its rulings. Knowledge of legal definitions from religion. Types of verbal definitions. Ijtihad and interpretation. Section: The seeker who has not conceptualized the meaning and is ignorant of its name. Fifth: Individual conceptualizations cannot be sought. Sixth: Distinguishing between essential and accidental is false. Discourse on the difference between essence and existence. Discourse on the distinction between essential and necessary. Seventh: The condition of shared essential attributes is a purely conventional matter. Eighth: The condition of mentioning differentiae along with the distinction between essential and necessary is impossible. Ninth: Knowledge of the essence depends on knowledge of the essential attributes and vice versa, leading to circularity. Investigations concerning the definition of knowledge and report. Third station: Refuting their claim that assents are only attained through syllogism. Confining the attainment of knowledge to syllogism is a statement without knowledge. The difference between self-evident and theoretical is purely relative. The nullity of their prohibition of argumentation by mutawatir and experimental reports. Denial of mutawatir reports is a principle of atheism. The polytheism of the philosophers is more heinous than the polytheism of the pre-Islamic people. The nullity of their claim: In demonstration, a universal proposition is necessary. The corruption of their statement that in every theoretical knowledge two premises are necessary. Universal propositions are learned by analogical reasoning. Their claim that demonstration yields perfectional sciences. Proofs of its falsity: First: Demonstration does not convey knowledge of any existent. Second: The Necessary Existent is not known by demonstration, etc. Third: Their theological science is not knowledge of the Creator nor of the created. Objection by Ibn al-Mutahhar al-Hilli and the author's correction of him. The highest science according to the logicians is not knowledge of an existent. Fourth: Mathematical science does not perfect souls, even if minds are exercised by it; the enticing causes for occupation with mathematical science and the like.
Source pages p. 9

Commentary
This passage is the table of contents (fihris) of Ibn Taymiyya's 'Radd Mantiqiyyin'. It provides an overview of the book's structure, which is organized into three main 'maqamat' (stations) after a summary of the principles of logic. The first maqam refutes the claim that conceptualizations (tasawwurat) are only attained through definition (hadd). It lists eleven proofs of the falsity of this claim, including points about circularity, the possibility of conceiving without definition, and the reliance on senses. The second maqam refutes the claim that definition conveys knowledge of conceptualizations, discussing al-Ghazali's views, Avicenna's admission, and nine proofs against the utility of definition, including arguments about essential vs. accidental attributes and circularity. The third maqam refutes the claim that assents (tasdiqat) are only attained through syllogism (qiyas), discussing the relativity of self-evidence, the rejection of mutawatir reports, and four proofs against demonstration, including the failure of demonstration to yield knowledge of existents. The fihris shows that Ibn Taymiyya's critique is comprehensive, targeting both the epistemological foundations of Greek logic and its specific doctrines on definition and syllogism. The table of contents also indicates that the book engages with other thinkers like al-Ghazali and Avicenna, and includes discussions on translation, legal definitions, and ijtihad. The structure is polemical, systematically dismantling the logicians' claims. The fihris itself is not a logical argument but a roadmap of the book's arguments.

تصديق

According to the fihris, what is the subject of the second maqam?

D) Summary of the principles of logic

Key Takeaway
The fihris reveals that Ibn Taymiyya's refutation targets three foundational claims: the necessity of definition for concepts, the utility of definition for knowledge, and the necessity of syllogism for assents.

?

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
15 min
First Maqam: Conceptualizations Do Not Require Definition
First maqam: proofs against necessity of definition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list at least five of Ibn Taymiyya's eleven proofs that conceptualizations can be attained without definition.

Core Idea
Definition is not necessary for knowledge; the senses and innate knowledge suffice.

In this lesson, we examine the first maqam of Ibn Taymiyya's Radd, where he attacks the logicians' claim that all conceptualizations (tasawwurat) require definition (hadd). The fihris lists eleven distinct proofs, ranging from circularity to the sufficiency of sensory perception. By working through these proofs, you will see how Ibn Taymiyya uses both logical and empirical arguments to undermine the foundational role of definition in Aristotelian epistemology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the target claim
Locate the heading of the first maqam: 'Refuting their claim that conceptualizations are only attained through definition'. This is the proposition Ibn Taymiyya sets out to disprove.
2
Scan the eleven proofs
Read through the numbered subpoints (الأول through الحادي عشر). Each is a concise argument. Note that some are logical (e.g., circularity) while others are empirical (e.g., all existents are sensed).
Proofs 1, 2, 5, 10 are logical; 3, 9 are empirical.
3
Categorize the proofs
Group proofs by type: (a) those showing definition leads to circularity or infinite regress (proofs 2, 10), (b) those showing definitions are unnecessary because we already know things (proofs 3, 6, 7, 8, 9), (c) those showing definitions themselves are unknowable (proofs 4, 5).
4
Understand proof 1: foundation of logic is speaking without knowledge
Ibn Taymiyya argues that the entire enterprise of logic is built on an unjustified claim. This sets the tone: the logicians' own first principle is baseless.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
15 min
Second Maqam: Definition Does Not Convey Knowledge
Second maqam: proofs against definition conveying knowledge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to outline Ibn Taymiyya's reasons for rejecting the claim that definition conveys knowledge, including his engagement with al-Ghazali and Ibn Sina.

Core Idea
Even a correct definition does not guarantee knowledge; it is a conventional tool that can at best prompt understanding.

The second maqam of Ibn Taymiyya's Radd targets the claim that definition (hadd) actually conveys knowledge of the thing defined. The fihris shows that Ibn Taymiyya engages with al-Ghazali and Ibn Sina, who acknowledged the difficulty. He then presents nine proofs against the epistemological utility of definition, culminating in the classic problem of circularity between essence and essential attributes. This lesson unpacks these proofs and their implications for Islamic epistemology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the target claim and references to al-Ghazali and Ibn Sina
Read the heading: 'Refuting their claim that definition conveys knowledge of conceptualizations.' Note the lines about al-Ghazali's view and his acknowledgment of impossibility in Mi'yar al-Ilm, and Ibn Sina's admission that some concepts are self-evident.
Ibn Taymiyya uses their concessions to weaken the logicians' case.
2
Review the nine proofs
Read the numbered proofs (الأول through التاسع). Focus on the logical structure: many proofs show that definition either assumes what it is trying to prove or fails to add new knowledge.
Proofs 3 and 9 involve circularity; proof 1 says definition does not convey knowledge at all.
3
Analyze proof 3: if conceptualization occurs via definition, it must occur before knowing the definition is valid
This is a powerful regress argument: to know the definition is correct, one must already have the concept, undermining the need for definition.
4
Understand proof 6: distinction between essential and accidental is false
Ibn Taymiyya argues that the logicians' division of properties into essential (dhātī) and accidental ('araḍī) is not objective but conventional. This undermines the very structure of definition.
This connects to later discussions on essence vs. existence and the necessary vs. the essential.

Index of the book 'The Refutation of the Logicians'. Topics: Introduction of the reviewer, Introduction of Sayyid Sulayman al-Nadwi, Publisher's introduction, Author's introduction, Summary of the principles of logic and its terminology: discourse in four stations. First station: Refuting their claim that conceptualizations are only attained through definition. Proofs of its falsity: First: The foundation of logic is speaking without knowledge. Second: Defining the defined by another definition entails circularity. Third: The particulars of the sciences are conceptualized without definitions. Fourth: A correct definition is not known according to their principle. Fifth: The real definition is either impossible or difficult. Sixth: Knowing the species without definition is better than knowing that which has no composition. Seventh: The priority of conceptualizing the meaning over knowing the indication of the word upon it. Eighth: The possibility of conceptualizing the meaning without the word. Ninth: All existents are conceptualized by humans only through their senses. Tenth: Refutation and objection cannot occur except after conceptualizing the defined without the definition. Eleventh: Self-evidence and consideration are not necessary attributes of known things. Second station: Refuting their claim that definition conveys knowledge of conceptualizations. The view of Imam al-Ghazali on logic: the benefit of definition according to the theologians. Al-Ghazali's acknowledgment of the impossibility of definition in the Criterion of Knowledge. Refutation of al-Ghazali's statement. The craft of definition is a conventional, non-instinctive postulate. Mixing the articles of the logicians with prophetic sciences. Proofs of its falsity: First: Definition does not convey knowledge of the defined. Innovation of mentioning the (singular) name - digression. Second: A single reporter without evidence does not convey knowledge. Third: If conceptualization of the defined occurred through definition, it would have occurred before knowing the validity of the definition. Fourth: Knowledge of the defined depends on knowledge of the named and its name only. Definition may prompt a prompting. Avicenna's acknowledgment that some matters are intrinsically conceptualized. The sound investigation concerning the issue of definition. The seeker who conceptualizes the meaning but is ignorant of its linguistic indication. Translation and its rulings. Knowledge of legal definitions from religion. Types of verbal definitions. Ijtihad and interpretation. Section: The seeker who has not conceptualized the meaning and is ignorant of its name. Fifth: Individual conceptualizations cannot be sought. Sixth: Distinguishing between essential and accidental is false. Discourse on the difference between essence and existence. Discourse on the distinction between essential and necessary. Seventh: The condition of shared essential attributes is a purely conventional matter. Eighth: The condition of mentioning differentiae along with the distinction between essential and necessary is impossible. Ninth: Knowledge of the essence depends on knowledge of the essential attributes and vice versa, leading to circularity. Investigations concerning the definition of knowledge and report. Third station: Refuting their claim that assents are only attained through syllogism. Confining the attainment of knowledge to syllogism is a statement without knowledge. The difference between self-evident and theoretical is purely relative. The nullity of their prohibition of argumentation by mutawatir and experimental reports. Denial of mutawatir reports is a principle of atheism. The polytheism of the philosophers is more heinous than the polytheism of the pre-Islamic people. The nullity of their claim: In demonstration, a universal proposition is necessary. The corruption of their statement that in every theoretical knowledge two premises are necessary. Universal propositions are learned by analogical reasoning. Their claim that demonstration yields perfectional sciences. Proofs of its falsity: First: Demonstration does not convey knowledge of any existent. Second: The Necessary Existent is not known by demonstration, etc. Third: Their theological science is not knowledge of the Creator nor of the created. Objection by Ibn al-Mutahhar al-Hilli and the author's correction of him. The highest science according to the logicians is not knowledge of an existent. Fourth: Mathematical science does not perfect souls, even if minds are exercised by it; the enticing causes for occupation with mathematical science and the like.
Source pages p. 9

Commentary
This passage is the table of contents (fihris) of Ibn Taymiyya's 'Radd Mantiqiyyin'. It provides an overview of the book's structure, which is organized into three main 'maqamat' (stations) after a summary of the principles of logic. The first maqam refutes the claim that conceptualizations (tasawwurat) are only attained through definition (hadd). It lists eleven proofs of the falsity of this claim, including points about circularity, the possibility of conceiving without definition, and the reliance on senses. The second maqam refutes the claim that definition conveys knowledge of conceptualizations, discussing al-Ghazali's views, Avicenna's admission, and nine proofs against the utility of definition, including arguments about essential vs. accidental attributes and circularity. The third maqam refutes the claim that assents (tasdiqat) are only attained through syllogism (qiyas), discussing the relativity of self-evidence, the rejection of mutawatir reports, and four proofs against demonstration, including the failure of demonstration to yield knowledge of existents. The fihris shows that Ibn Taymiyya's critique is comprehensive, targeting both the epistemological foundations of Greek logic and its specific doctrines on definition and syllogism. The table of contents also indicates that the book engages with other thinkers like al-Ghazali and Avicenna, and includes discussions on translation, legal definitions, and ijtihad. The structure is polemical, systematically dismantling the logicians' claims. The fihris itself is not a logical argument but a roadmap of the book's arguments.

ذاتي
عرضي
دور

Checkpoint
According to the second maqam, what does Ibn Taymiyya say about the distinction between essential (dhātī) and accidental ('araḍī)?
A) It is a useful logical distinction
B) It is based on the nature of things
C) It is false and conventional
D) It is necessary for definition

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya denies that definition conveys knowledge, arguing that it is a conventional construct, not a necessary condition for understanding.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Explain in your own words why Ibn Taymiyya says the distinction between essential and accidental is false. Use one of his proofs as support.
?
How does Ibn Taymiyya's critique of definition affect the way a mutakallim (theologian) might approach defining terms like 'qadim' (pre-eternal) or 'hadith' (temporal)? Provide one specific implication.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
15 min
Third Maqam: Assents Do Not Require Syllogism
Third maqam: proofs against requirement of syllogism for assent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list Ibn Taymiyya's arguments against the claim that all assents (tasdiqat) depend on syllogism (qiyas), including his defense of other sources of knowledge like mutawatir reports.

Core Idea
Knowledge comes through senses, testimony, and analogical reasoning, not just syllogism.

In the third maqam of his Radd, Ibn Taymiyya takes on the logicians' claim that all assents (tasdiqat) require syllogism (qiyas iqtirani). The fihris indicates that he argues this claim is itself a groundless assertion. He then criticizes the logicians' rejection of other valid sources of knowledge, such as mutawatir (mass-transmitted) and experimental reports, and highlights the relativity of the self-evident/theoretical distinction. Four explicit proofs against demonstration are listed. This lesson explores this final pillar of Ibn Taymiyya's critique.

Guided Path
1
Identify the target claim and initial objection
Read the heading: 'Refuting their claim that assents are only attained through syllogism.' Note the line 'Confining the attainment of knowledge to syllogism is a statement without knowledge' — Ibn Taymiyya calls the logicians' own principle baseless.
2
Analyze the rejection of mutawatir and experimental reports
Read the lines: 'The nullity of their prohibition of argumentation by mutawatir and experimental reports. Denial of mutawatir reports is a principle of atheism.' Ibn Taymiyya emphasizes that rejecting these common sources of knowledge leads to skepticism and ultimately irreligion.
In Islamic tradition, mutawatir hadith provides certain knowledge. By denying it, the logicians cut off a key source of religious knowledge.
3
Review the four proofs against demonstration
Locate the numbered proofs (الأول through الرابع) under the third maqam. Note that the first says 'Demonstration does not convey knowledge of any existent' — a sweeping claim. The second says the Necessary Existent (God) is not known through demonstration. The third says their theological science is not knowledge of God or creation. The fourth criticizes mathematical science for not perfecting souls.
These proofs go beyond logic to challenge the metaphysical and spiritual claims of the logicians.
4
Understand the alternative: analogical reasoning (qiyas al-tamthil)
The fihris states 'Universal propositions are learned by analogical reasoning' (القضايا الكلية تعلم بقياس التمثيل). This indicates that Ibn Taymiyya sees analogy (the type used in fiqh) as more foundational than Aristotelian syllogism.
This connects to his broader project: Islamic reasoning is superior to Greek logic.

Commentary
This passage is the table of contents (fihris) of Ibn Taymiyya's 'Radd Mantiqiyyin'. It provides an overview of the book's structure, which is organized into three main 'maqamat' (stations) after a summary of the principles of logic. The first maqam refutes the claim that conceptualizations (tasawwurat) are only attained through definition (hadd). It lists eleven proofs of the falsity of this claim, including points about circularity, the possibility of conceiving without definition, and the reliance on senses. The second maqam refutes the claim that definition conveys knowledge of conceptualizations, discussing al-Ghazali's views, Avicenna's admission, and nine proofs against the utility of definition, including arguments about essential vs. accidental attributes and circularity. The third maqam refutes the claim that assents (tasdiqat) are only attained through syllogism (qiyas), discussing the relativity of self-evidence, the rejection of mutawatir reports, and four proofs against demonstration, including the failure of demonstration to yield knowledge of existents. The fihris shows that Ibn Taymiyya's critique is comprehensive, targeting both the epistemological foundations of Greek logic and its specific doctrines on definition and syllogism. The table of contents also indicates that the book engages with other thinkers like al-Ghazali and Avicenna, and includes discussions on translation, legal definitions, and ijtihad. The structure is polemical, systematically dismantling the logicians' claims. The fihris itself is not a logical argument but a roadmap of the book's arguments.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Navigating the Fihris: Structure of Ibn Taymiyya's Critique
Table of contents listing topics and pages

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three maqamat of Ibn Taymiyya's critique from the fihris and state the main target of each.

Core Idea
The fihris is a battlefield map: it shows where Ibn Taymiyya attacks Greek logic.

This table of contents is not just a list—it is a strategic outline of Ibn Taymiyya's systematic refutation of Greek logic. By learning to read this fihris, you will grasp the architecture of his argument before diving into the details.

Guided Path
1
Locate the three maqamat (stations)
Scan the fihris for the word 'المقام' (al-maqam). You will find three: al-maqam al-thalith (third station), al-maqam al-rabi' (fourth station). Note that the first and second are not explicitly listed; they may be earlier in the book.
Each maqam is a major division focusing on a key aspect of the critique.
2
Identify the main target of each maqam
From the fihris headings: al-maqam al-thalith targets the claim that assents (tasdiqat) are only attained through syllogism. Al-maqam al-rabi' targets the claim that syllogism yields knowledge of assents.
This shows Ibn Taymiyya's progressive attack: first on syllogism as necessary, then on its sufficiency.
3
Examine the subdivisions within each maqam
Look for sections (فصل) and subheadings. For example, under al-maqam al-thalith, you see 'بطلان حصر الأدلة في القياس والاستقراء والتمثيل' (invalidity of restricting proofs to syllogism, induction, and analogy). This reveals his broader target: the logicians' classification of inference.
The subdivisions show the logical structure of his refutation.
4
Relate the fihris to the author's overall argument
Notice how Islamic legal concepts appear: 'قياس التمثيل' (analogical reasoning) and 'الاجتهاد والتأويل' (ijtihad and interpretation). This reflects Ibn Taymiyya's alternative: he proposes that Islamic legal reasoning (like qiyas al-tamthil) is epistemically sound and not dependent on Greek logic.
The fihris thus previews his constructive position.

Ninth: Dependence of knowledge of the essence on knowledge of the essentials and vice versa entails circularity... Investigations into the definition of knowledge and report. Fourth station: In refuting their saying that syllogism yields knowledge of assents. That the logical syllogism is ineffective for knowledge, existence and non-existence. The Sharia of Islam is not dependent on any of their sciences. 290, 292, 302. God. Sixth: Demonstration does not yield universal matters that must endure in contingent things.
