Source pages p. 10

Commentary
This passage is the table of contents (fihris) for Ibn Taymiyya's 'Refutation of the Logicians' (Radd al-Mantiqiyyin). It lists the major topics covered in the book along with their page numbers. The structure shows that the work is divided into several 'stations' (maqamat) and sections (fusul) that systematically critique Greek logic, especially the theories of definition (hadd), syllogism (qiyas), and the claim that certain knowledge is only attained through demonstration. Key themes include the distinction between essential and accidental, the nature of definition, the inadequacy of syllogism as the sole method of knowledge, the criticism of the philosophers' theology (e.g., that God's knowledge is via syllogism), and the defense of analogical reasoning (qiyas al-tamthil) used in Islamic jurisprudence. The table also mentions specific figures like Ibn Sina, al-Ghazali, and Aristotle. This fihris serves as a roadmap for the book's argument, showing the breadth of Ibn Taymiyya's critique.

Key Takeaway
The fihris reveals that Ibn Taymiyya's critique is organized into thematic stations, targeting first the necessity of syllogism for assents, then its sufficiency, while defending Islamic analogical reasoning.

?

?

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Navigating Ibn Taymiyya's Refutation through its Table of Contents
Table of contents listing topics and page numbers for the entire book.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to use the table of contents of Ibn Taymiyya's Radd al-Mantiqiyyin to identify major logical arguments and the author's strategy.

Core Idea
The table of contents reveals the battlefield: logic, demonstration, and divine knowledge.

A table of contents (fihrist) is not just a list of pages; it is a map of the author's intellectual attack. In Ibn Taymiyya's Radd al-Mantiqiyyin, the fihrist shows the progression from critiquing the philosophers' concept of divine science to affirming the sufficiency of innate knowledge and revelation. In this lesson, you will learn to extract the book's logical argumentative structure from its fihrist.

Guided Path
1
Scan the fihrist for major headings
Look for the words 'المقام' (station) and 'فصل' (chapter). These indicate major divisions of the book and show how Ibn Taymiyya organized his refutation.
The first station is about the philosophers' divine science; the second about syllogism and demonstration.
2
Identify key topics of refutation
Note page references for terms like 'قياس الشمول والتمثيل' (universal and analogical syllogism) and 'البرهان' (demonstration). These are central to Ibn Taymiyya's critique.
For example, page 409 discusses the equivalence of universal and analogical syllogism.
3
Map the sequence of arguments
Notice that the fihrist moves from negative critiques (e.g., 'The divine science has no external reality') to positive affirmations (e.g., 'The balance sent from God is the correct syllogism'). This sequence reflects Ibn Taymiyya's method of deconstruction followed by reconstruction.
The page numbers help trace the argument's flow.
4
Relate structure to Ibn Taymiyya's project
The organization reveals his overall strategy: first dismantling Greek logical foundations, then asserting Islamic epistemic principles. The fihrist entries on 'The Islamic Sharia is not dependent on their sciences' and 'Mutawatir from the prophets is greater' show the ultimate reliance on revelation.
This structure is itself a critique of the claim that logic is necessary for knowledge.

Fallacies of the theologians and philosophers
The monotheism of the Necessary Being according to the philosophers
Second: The specific thing sought to be known through universal propositions is known before and without them 352
The Quranic method in explaining the possibility of resurrection 356
Their attempt to oppose innate nature and the teachings of messengers 361
Hidden premises may benefit some people in debate. 364
Disagreement among philosophers. 368
Al-Nawbakhti's speech in refutation of logic. 373
The book 'Opinions and Religions' 377
The intellectual balance is the innate knowledge of similarity and difference 383
Eighth: They have no proof for their philosophical sciences 420
That the science of astronomy is from experiential things 422
If it is God's unchangeable custom 426
Mutawatir from the prophets is greater than mutawatir from philosophers 429
That the philosophers are among the most ignorant of creation about the Lord of the worlds 432
Then index of subjects 434
Bibliography 436
General indices 438
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This passage is the table of contents (fihrist) of Ibn Taymiyya's book 'Refutation of the Logicians'. It lists the major topics covered in the book along with their page numbers. The table of contents gives a comprehensive overview of the refutation's structure. It begins with a critique of the philosophers' concept of divine science, then moves to discussions on the perfection of the soul, the personalities of Aristotle and others, and the restriction of inference to two premises. It includes chapters on Imam al-Ghazali's relationship with logic, the correlation between universal and analogical syllogism, and the reduction of conjunctive and disjunctive syllogisms to one meaning. The author also addresses Ibn Sina's sciences, falsifies the claim that faith is mere knowledge, and provides a chapter on analogical syllogism yielding only probability. There are sections on objections by Muslim thinkers, refutations, and discussions on monotheism, attributes, and exhaustive division. Further topics include the fourth station on syllogism's role in knowledge, the sixth station on demonstration not yielding universal eternal matters, and refutations of restrictions on evidence types. The table also covers the conventional nature of logic, silly statements of philosophers and Sufis about prophets, and critiques of theologians and philosophers. Later entries discuss the inability of demonstrative syllogism to prove the Maker, the sufficiency of conceptualization of the middle term, and the equivalence of universal and analogical syllogism. It ends with topics on the balance sent from God, reduction to conjunctive syllogism, refutations on cause and effect, and comparisons between prophetic and philosophical knowledge. The table of contents shows the breadth of Ibn Taymiyya's attack on Aristotelian logic and Greek philosophy, emphasizing the supremacy of innate knowledge and divine revelation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) 416
D) 401

Key Takeaway
The fihrist of Radd al-Mantiqiyyin maps Ibn Taymiyya's systematic refutation, from critiquing the foundations of Greek logic to asserting the primacy of innate knowledge and revelation.

?

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Mapping Ibn Taymiyya's Critique of Logic
Table of contents listing topics and page numbers of the book.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to outline the main sections of Ibn Taymiyya's 'Radd Mantiqiyyin' from its table of contents.

Core Idea
The table of contents reveals Ibn Taymiyya's systematic dismantling of logical certainty.

The table of contents of a scholarly work is not just a list; it is a roadmap of the author's argument. In Ibn Taymiyya's 'Refutation of the Logicians', the entries preview his comprehensive critique of Aristotelian logic as used by Muslim philosophers. This lesson helps you navigate this roadmap to understand the flow of his critique.

Guided Path
1
Scan the major headings
Look for numbered sections (third, fourth, fifth, etc.) to see the sequence of arguments.
2
Identify the key targets
Note names like Ibn Sina, al-Razi, and topics like syllogism, well-known propositions.
3
Observe the progression from theoretical to applied
Early entries deal with demonstrative syllogism and proof; later ones address prophethood and revelation.
4
Note the recurring themes
The balance of syllogism, the role of innate nature, and the critique of philosophical epistemology.

برهان للرازي على هذا التفريق وبيان تناقضه من ثلاثة عشر طريقاً
فصل برهان آخر للرازي على هذا التفريق
الثاني: لا دليل على دعواهم أن المشهورات ليست من اليقينيات. بيان أن قضايا التحسين والتقبيح من أعظم اليقينيات
الثالث : في بيان كون المشهورات من جملة القضايا الواجب قبولها

الفناء المذموم والفناء المحمود
From the innovations of the theologians: their rejection of what is sound from philosophy. Third: The lack of demonstrative syllogism's indication for proving the Creator. Discourse on the cause of the need for the Creator. Discourse on the genus of syllogism and proof absolutely. Fourth: Complete conceptualization of the middle term suffices over logical syllogism. Chapter: The syllogism, even if sound, does not yield knowledge of existents. First: Explanation of the categories of certainties according to them that contain no universal proposition. Discourse on the saying of al-Khalil (peace be upon him): 'This is my Lord'. Every conceptualization can be turned into an assent and vice versa. Fifth: Among syllogisms are those whose premises are self-evident. Sixth: Among universal propositions are those that can be known without mediation of syllogism. Seventh: Decisive proofs for the equivalence of comprehensive syllogism and analogical syllogism. The balance sent down from God is the correct syllogism. Every syllogism in the world can be reduced to conjunctive syllogism. Invalidation of the claim of conjunction of cause and effect. Refutation of the claim that the unseen world is the intellectual world. The oneness of the Necessary Existence according to the philosophers. The method of the Qur'an in explaining the possibility of resurrection. Their attempt to oppose innate disposition and the teachings of the messengers. Hidden premises may benefit some people and in debate. Disagreement among the philosophers themselves. The statement of al-Nawbakhti in refutation of logic. The book 'Al-Ara' wa al-Diyanat'. Concerning time. The intellectual balance is the innate knowledge of similarity and difference. Eighth: They have no proof for their philosophical sciences. The science of astronomy being among the empirical matters. The sunna of God that never changes. The mutawatir from the prophets is greater than the mutawatir from the philosophers. The philosophers are among the most ignorant of creation concerning the Lord of the worlds. Ninth: Refutation of Ibn Sina and al-Razi in their discussion of well-known propositions – and it contains eight types. First: Discourse on their differentiation between primary and well-known propositions. A proof by al-Razi for this differentiation and explanation of its contradiction in thirteen ways. Chapter: Another proof by al-Razi for this differentiation. Second: No evidence for their claim that well-known propositions are not certainties. Explanation that propositions of good and evil are among the greatest certainties. Third: Explanation that well-known propositions are among the propositions that must be accepted. Fourth: The property of intellect and innate nature: approval of good and disapproval of evil. Fifth: Concerning these well-known propositions being known by innate nature. Sixth: Concerning that which necessitates belief in these well-known propositions being among the necessities of humanity. Seventh: Ibn Sina's refutation of himself in his statement that well-known propositions are not perceived by the powers of the soul. Eighth: Refutation of their statement that intellect alone does not judge anything in well-known propositions. Tenth: No argument for their denial of reports of prophets that fall outside their syllogism. Eleventh: Invalidity of their statement that demonstrative, rhetorical, and dialectical syllogisms are those mentioned in Surat al-Nahl. The statement of the philosophers concerning the prophets (peace be upon them). Their attempt to couple philosophy with the teachings of the prophets. Reason for revelation of the verse: 'Indeed, those who have believed and those who were Jews' – the verse. Discourse on God taking the covenant of the prophets to believe in Muhammad. The Sabians – and the correct investigation concerning them. The Last Day as mentioned in the Qur'an. Their error in denying God's knowledge and other attributes, and its refutation. Discourse on their making the three syllogisms from the Qur'an. Twelfth: Their denial of the existence of jinn, angels, and revelation is a statement without knowledge. Thirteenth: Their way does not distinguish between truth and falsehood, unlike the way of the prophets. Fourteenth: Corruption of their claim that the sciences of the prophets are obtained through logical syllogism. Their claim that the prophet's knowledge of the unseen is derived from the celestial soul, and explanation of its corruption in ten aspects. Tenth: The angels are living, rational beings, not imaginary forms. That the acquisition of knowledge in the hearts of prophets is through angels. The difference between the ways of Muslim theologians and the ways of the philosophers. The blameworthy annihilation and the praiseworthy annihilation.
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This passage is the table of contents of Ibn Taymiyya's 'Radd Mantiqiyyin' (Refutation of the Logicians). It lists the topics covered in the book, providing an overview of the main arguments. The table is divided into two pages: page 12 covers early topics up to 'the philosophers are the most ignorant of creation about the Lord', and page 13 continues with more detailed headings on well-known propositions, prophethood, and related subjects. The structure reveals Ibn Taymiyya's critical approach: he begins by attacking the claims of logicians regarding demonstration and certainty, then moves to discussions on innate knowledge, the role of syllogism, and finally a refutation of specific philosophers like Ibn Sina and al-Razi. The table also includes topics on the prophets, the angels, and the comparison between Islamic theology and philosophy. Each heading indicates a distinct argument or set of arguments. The overall purpose is to systematically dismantle the epistemological foundations of Greek logic as adopted by Muslim philosophers, asserting the superiority of prophetic knowledge and sound innate reasoning.

المشهورات
القياس الاقتراني

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Key Concepts: Burhani, Mashhurat, Iqtirani
Table of contents listing topics and page numbers of the book.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the three key terms that appear prominently in the table of contents.

Core Idea
Three terms structure Ibn Taymiyya's critique: demonstrative syllogism, well-known propositions, and conjunctive syllogism.

In the table of contents, three Arabic terms stand out: 'al-qiyas al-burhani' (demonstrative syllogism), 'al-mashhurat' (well-known propositions), and 'al-qiyas al-iqtirani' (conjunctive syllogism). Understanding these terms is essential to follow Ibn Taymiyya's arguments. This lesson introduces them and previews his critical stance.

Guided Path
1
Locate each term in the table
Find where 'برهاني', 'مشهورات', and 'اقتراني' appear and note the context.
2
Understand the standard logical meaning
Read the definitions provided in key terms.
3
Recognize Ibn Taymiyya's shift
Note the shift_alert: he challenges the exclusivity of burhani, blurs mashhurat with certainties, and reduces all syllogisms to iqtirani.
4
Preview the critique
The table shows that whole sections are devoted to refuting claims about each term.

Reason for revelation of the verse: 'Indeed, those who have believed and those who were Jews' – the verse. Discourse on God taking the covenant of the prophets to believe in Muhammad. The Sabians – and the correct investigation concerning them. The Last Day as mentioned in the Qur'an. Their error in denying God's knowledge and other attributes, and its refutation. Discourse on their making the three syllogisms from the Qur'an. Twelfth: Their denial of the existence of jinn, angels, and revelation is a statement without knowledge. Thirteenth: Their way does not distinguish between truth and falsehood, unlike the way of the prophets. Fourteenth: Corruption of their claim that the sciences of the prophets are obtained through logical syllogism. Their claim that the prophet's knowledge of the unseen is derived from the celestial soul, and explanation of its corruption in ten aspects. Tenth: The angels are living, rational beings, not imaginary forms. That the acquisition of knowledge in the hearts of prophets is through angels. The difference between the ways of Muslim theologians and the ways of the philosophers. The blameworthy annihilation and the praiseworthy annihilation.
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This passage is the table of contents of Ibn Taymiyya's 'Radd Mantiqiyyin' (Refutation of the Logicians). It lists the topics covered in the book, providing an overview of the main arguments. The table is divided into two pages: page 12 covers early topics up to 'the philosophers are the most ignorant of creation about the Lord', and page 13 continues with more detailed headings on well-known propositions, prophethood, and related subjects. The structure reveals Ibn Taymiyya's critical approach: he begins by attacking the claims of logicians regarding demonstration and certainty, then moves to discussions on innate knowledge, the role of syllogism, and finally a refutation of specific philosophers like Ibn Sina and al-Razi. The table also includes topics on the prophets, the angels, and the comparison between Islamic theology and philosophy. Each heading indicates a distinct argument or set of arguments. The overall purpose is to systematically dismantle the epistemological foundations of Greek logic as adopted by Muslim philosophers, asserting the superiority of prophetic knowledge and sound innate reasoning.

القياس البرهاني
المشهورات
القياس الاقتراني

Introduction and Front Matter
advanced
5 min
Mapping Ibn Taymiyya's Critique of Logicians on Famous Premises
Index listing topics of Ibn Taymiyya's refutation of logicians.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the main topics of Ibn Taymiyya's critique in the Ninth Topic of Radd Mantiqiyyin and explain his central objections to the logicians' treatment of famous premises.

Core Idea
Ibn Taymiyya overturns the logicians' dismissal of famous premises as certain: moral truths are rationally self-evident.

This lesson unpacks the table of contents of Ibn Taymiyya's Radd Mantiqiyyin, specifically the Ninth Topic. By examining the fihris, you will see the structure of his refutation of Ibn Sina and al-Razi on the status of 'famous premises' (mashhurat). You will learn how Ibn Taymiyya argues that judgments of good and evil are certain and that the logicians' distinction between primary and famous premises is flawed. This map will guide your understanding of the book's overall argumentative strategy.

Guided Path
1
Locate the Ninth Topic and its eight types
Find the heading 'الموضوع التاسع : الرد على ابن سينا والرازي في كلامهما في القضايا المشهورة' and the eight numbered items that follow. Note how each type addresses a different aspect of the logicians' position.
The eight types are listed from 'الأول' to 'الثامن'.
2
Identify the three main arguments against the logicians' treatment of mashhurat
From the types, extract Ibn Taymiyya's core objections: (1) The logicians have no proof that mashhurat are not certain; (2) The judgments of good and evil (tahsin wa taqbih) are among the greatest certainties; (3) The logicians' claim that reason alone does not decide regarding mashhurat is false.
These appear in types الثاني, الثالث, and الثامن.
3
Observe the broader claims beyond the eight types
Note the subsequent topics: the invalidity of limiting syllogistic reasoning, the logicians' failure to distinguish truth from falsehood, and their denial of prophetic knowledge. This shows Ibn Taymiyya's comprehensive critique.
These topics bridge to the discussion of prophecy and the superiority of the prophetic method.
4
Understand the significance of the fihris as a map
The fihris reveals that Ibn Taymiyya systematically attacks both the epistemological and methodological foundations of logic, and contrasts the philosophers' approach with that of the prophets and Muslim theologians.
Use this map to navigate the full text of the Radd.

Index of the book against the logicians
Ninth Topic: Refutation of Ibn Sina and al-Razi regarding their statements about famous premises (al-mashhurat).
And it contains eight types:
First: Discussion of their distinction between primary premises and famous premises.
Proof by al-Razi for this distinction and an exposition of its contradiction from thirteen ways.
Section: Another proof by al-Razi for this distinction.
Second: No evidence for their claim that famous premises are not among certainties. An exposition that judgments of good and evil are among the greatest certainties.
Third: On the exposition that famous premises are among the classes of premises that must be accepted.
Fourth: The special quality of reason and innate disposition is the approval of good and disapproval of evil.
Fifth: On these famous premises being known by innate disposition.
Sixth: On the cause that necessitates belief in these famous premises being among the requisites of humanity.
Seventh: Ibn Sina's self-refutation in his statement that famous premises are not perceived by the powers of the soul.
Eighth: Refutation of their statement that reason alone does not decide anything regarding famous premises.
Tenth: No proof for their discrediting of reports of prophets that fall outside their syllogism.
Eleventh: Invalidity of their statement that the demonstrative, rhetorical, and dialectical syllogisms are those mentioned in Surah al-Nahl.
The statements of philosophers regarding prophets, peace be upon them.
Their attempt to join philosophy with the teachings of the prophets.
Reason for the revelation of the verse: 'Indeed, those who have believed and those who were Jews...' (al-Baqarah 2:62).
Discussion of God's taking of the covenant of the prophets to believe in Muhammad.
The Sabians - and the correct investigation about them.
The Last Day as mentioned in the Quran.
Their misguidance in denying God's knowledge and other attributes, and its refutation.
Discussion of their making the three syllogisms from the Quran.
Twelfth: Their denial of the existence of jinn, angels, and revelation is a statement without knowledge.
Thirteenth: Their method does not distinguish between truth and falsehood, unlike the method of the prophets.
Fourteenth: The corruption of their making the sciences of the prophets obtained through logical syllogism.
Their making the prophet's knowledge of the unseen derived from the celestial soul, and an exposition of its corruption from ten aspects.
Tenth: The angels are living, rational beings, not imaginary forms.
The obtaining of knowledge in the hearts of prophets through the agency of angels.
The difference between the methods of the Muslim theologians and the methods of the philosophers.
Blameworthy annihilation and praiseworthy annihilation.
Statements of philosophers that no one among the Muslims has adopted, and the negation of each of them by the Muslims.
The shirk-based intercession that is denied and the shari'a-based intercession that is affirmed.
Enumeration of categories of those called upon besides God.
The statement of philosophers regarding intercession is greater shirk than the statement of others.
The mediation of humans for the Hanifs is not like the mediation of celestial beings for the philosophers.
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage is a table of contents (fihris) for Ibn Taymiyya's work 'Radd Mantiqiyyin' (Refutation of the Logicians). It lists the topics covered in the book, particularly the ninth major theme which is a refutation of Avicenna (Ibn Sina) and Fakhr al-Din al-Razi regarding their treatment of 'famous premises' (mashhurat). The fihris shows that the author methodically addresses the logicians' distinctions, arguments, and contradictions. It also indicates broader discussions on prophecy, angels, jinn, and the superiority of prophetic methods over syllogistic reasoning. The index gives a clear overview of the book's structure and main arguments, serving as a roadmap for the reader.

Key Terms
المشهورات (al-mashhurat): Premises that are widely accepted but not necessarily certain; according to logicians, they are not among the certainties (yaqiniyyat). [Note: Ibn Taymiyya redefines al-mashhurat as often carrying certainty, especially in ethical judgments, contra the standard logical tradition.]
الأوليات (al-awwaliyyat): Primary premises that are self-evidently true, such as 'the whole is greater than the part'. [Note: Standard term in logic; no significant shift.]
اليقينيات (al-yaqiniyyat): Certain premises that are indubitable. [Note: Stable term across Islamic logic.]
القياس البرهاني (al-qiyas al-burhani): Demonstrative syllogism that yields certain knowledge from true premises. [Note: Standard term in Aristotelian and Islamic logic.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Navigating the Fihris of Radd al-Mantiqiyyin
List of topics and page numbers for the book.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the structure and key topics of Ibn Taymiyya's Radd al-Mantiqiyyin by reading its table of contents.

Core Idea
A fihris reveals the author's argumentative structure and priorities.

This lesson walks you through the table of contents of Ibn Taymiyya's Radd al-Mantiqiyyin. You will learn to parse the page references and topic descriptions, giving you a roadmap to the book's major arguments and showing how Ibn Taymiyya organizes his critique of Aristotelian logic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the page numbers
The numbers (e.g., ٥٦٨, ٥٧٠) are page references. They appear before each topic. Note that OCR errors may occur (e.g., ۵۷۳ vs ٥٧٣).
Compare with original if possible.
2
Parse the topic descriptions
Each line after the page number gives a theme. For example, 'الشفاعة الشركية المنفية والشفاعة الشرعية الثابتة' means 'The polytheistic intercession denied and the legal intercession established.'
Look for contrasts or key phrases.
3
Relate topics to the book's overall argument
Topics like 'مقالات للفلاسفة لم يذهب إليها أحد من المسلمين' reveal Ibn Taymiyya's critical stance against philosophers.
Consider how each topic supports his refutation.
4
Use the fihris as a navigation tool
When studying the book, locate specific arguments by page. For instance, to find his discussion of lawful intercession, turn to page 570.
Keep the fihris handy while reading.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate

The Uniqueness of Ibn Taymiyya's Refutation of the Logicians
Author introduces the book's uniqueness and historical context of logic's translation and reception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how Ibn Taymiyya's Radd al-Mantiqiyyin is distinct from previous works on logic in the Islamic tradition.

Core Idea
Ibn Taymiyya's refutation of logic is unprecedented in its thorough critique of Aristotelian foundations.

This introduction by Dr. Sulayman Nadwi sets the stage for Ibn Taymiyya's monumental critique. The passage declares that no book like this had been composed before. It targets the very foundations of Aristotelian logic, which had been transmitted into Islamic civilization. Understanding its uniqueness helps you appreciate why this work is central to the Islamic intellectual tradition's engagement with logic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the book's claim to uniqueness
The passage says it is 'a book unlike any other and without precedent.' This claim points to its role as a direct critique of Aristotle's foundations, not just a commentary or adaptation.
2
Understand the Aristotelian definition of logic
The passage defines logic as 'rules whose observance protects the mind from error in thought and the arrangement of known things to obtain the unknown.' This is Aristotle's conception, which Ibn Taymiyya challenges.
Compare this to later Islamic definitions that integrated it with fiqh and kalam.
3
Trace the transmission of logic into Arabic
Logic was translated from Greek into Arabic during the Abbasid period by Syriac and Hebrew translators, as recorded in Ibn al-Nadim's 'al-Fihrist'. This shows it was a foreign import.
The translation process was gradual, 'chapter by chapter and discipline by discipline.'
4
Recognize the rejection of logic by some scholars
Many religious scholars (mufassirun, muhaddithun, fuqaha) kept aloof from logic; some declared it forbidden and accused its practitioners of heresy, as al-Suyuti's treatise shows.
This sets up the conflict that Ibn Taymiyya enters.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم مقدمة العلامة الدكتور السيد سليمان النذوى، مدير مجلة «معارف»، أعظم كره، الهند. كتاب الرد على المنطقيين هذا كتاب لم يُنسَج على منواله ولم يسبق له نظير . فهو نقد ما قاله وأصله وأسسه أرسطو حكيم اليونانيين في نقد أدلة العقل وترجيح بعضها على بعض بأصول وقواعد وقوانينَ تَعْصِمُ مراعاتها الذهنَ عن الخطأ في الفكر وترتيب المعلوم لتحصيل المجهول، وسماها «علم المنطق». نقل هذا العلم في جملة ما نقل من العلوم اليونانية إلى العربية أيام حضارة العباسيين في القرن الثالث للهجرة، بأيدي نَقَلة السُّريانيين والعبرانيين كما نعرفُ خبره في كتاب «الفهرست» لابن النديم البغدادي الموجود في آخر القرن الرابع. فنقل هذا العلم باباً باباً وفنا فنا حتى تم كله وحَصَل جُلّه عند عارفي اللغة العربية . ولم يزل علماء المنقول من أئمة الدين من المفسرين والمحدثين والفقهاء في مَعْزِلٍ منه حتى حَرَّم منهم من حَرَّمه ونسب إلى الزندقة مَنْ نَظَر فيه، حتى إن جلال الدين السيوطي المتوفى سنة ٩١١ هـ ـ وقد كان علماء المسلمين تبقروا في هذه العلوم وتوسعوا في معرفة حقهم من باطلهم - وَضَع رسالة في تحريم علم المنطق . وقد كان علماء الإسلام قبل أبي حامد الغزالي على فرقتين: فرقة اعتكفوا للمنقول من التفسير والفقه والحديث، وأخرى للمعقول من العلوم الطبيعية والإلهية والرياضية وغيرها. وقد كانت بينهم حرب عوان يَشُنُّ بعضهم على بعض غارة شعواء،
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Introduction of the distinguished scholar Dr. Sayyid Sulayman Nadwi, director of the journal 'Ma'arif', Azamgarh, India. The book 'The Refutation of the Logicians'. This is a book unlike any other and without precedent. It is a critique of what Aristotle, the philosopher of the Greeks, said and established in criticism of the proofs of the intellect and preferring some over others with principles, rules, and laws whose observance protects the mind from error in thought and the arrangement of known things to obtain the unknown, and he called it 'The science of logic'. This science was transmitted along with what was transmitted from Greek sciences into Arabic during the Abbasid civilization in the third century AH, by the hands of Syriac and Hebrew translators, as we know its account in the book 'al-Fihrist' by Ibn al-Nadim al-Baghdadi from the end of the fourth century. So this science was transmitted chapter by chapter and discipline by discipline until it was completed and most of it was obtained by those knowledgeable in Arabic. And the scholars of transmitted sciences from the religious leaders – exegetes, hadith scholars, and jurists – kept aloof from it until some of them declared it forbidden and accused those who looked into it of heresy, even that Jalal al-Din al-Suyuti, who died in 911 AH – while Muslim scholars had become thorough in these sciences and expanded in knowledge of their truth from falsehood – wrote a treatise on the prohibition of logic. And before Abu Hamid al-Ghazali, the scholars of Islam were divided into two groups: a group devoted to transmitted sciences: exegesis, fiqh, and hadith; and another to rational sciences: natural, divine, mathematical, and others. And between them was a fierce war in which one group launched a fierce attack on the other.
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage is the introduction by Dr. Sulayman Nadwi to Ibn Taymiyya's 'Radd al-Mantiqiyyin'. It begins with the basmala and identifies the author of the introduction. Then it asserts the uniqueness of Ibn Taymiyya's work as an unprecedented critique of Aristotelian logic. Nadwi explains that logic was translated from Greek into Arabic during the Abbasid era by Syriac and Hebrew translators, as recorded by Ibn al-Nadim. He notes that many traditional religious scholars (mufassirun, muhaddithun, fuqaha) initially kept away from logic, some even declaring it forbidden and accusing its practitioners of heresy, such as al-Suyuti's treatise. Before al-Ghazali, scholars were split between those focused on transmitted sciences (naql) and those focused on rational sciences ('aql). There was a fierce conflict between these two camps.

نَقَلة
الفهرست
الغزالي

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya's Radd al-Mantiqiyyin is a unique critique of Aristotelian logic, which was imported into Islamic civilization and met with both acceptance and rejection among scholars.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate

The Historical Division Between Transmitted and Rational Sciences
Author introduces the book's uniqueness and historical context of logic's translation and reception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the two scholarly camps before al-Ghazali and their conflict over logic.

Core Idea
Before al-Ghazali, Islamic scholars were sharply divided between transmitted sciences and rational sciences, with logic as a battlefield.

This passage reveals a crucial historical context: before al-Ghazali, the Islamic intellectual landscape was polarized. One camp focused exclusively on transmitted sciences like tafsir, fiqh, and hadith; the other camp engaged with rational sciences including logic, natural philosophy, and metaphysics. This division led to a fierce war of words. Understanding this helps you see why Ibn Taymiyya's project was so groundbreaking.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two camps of scholars
The passage mentions 'a group devoted to transmitted sciences: exegesis, fiqh, and hadith' and 'another to rational sciences: natural, divine, mathematical, and others.' These are the naqli and 'aqli camps.
Note that logic is considered part of the rational sciences.
2
Describe their relationship
The passage says 'between them was a fierce war in which one group launched a fierce attack on the other.' This indicates open hostility and mutual accusations.
This conflict is part of the backdrop for Ibn Taymiyya's work.
3
Locate al-Ghazali's role
Al-Ghazali is mentioned as a pivotal figure before whom the division existed. The implication is that after him, there was some integration or change.
Al-Ghazali himself wrote on logic in works like 'al-Mustasfa' and 'Mihakk al-Nazar'.
4
Connect to Ibn Taymiyya's critique
Ibn Taymiyya's Radd al-Mantiqiyyin enters this battlefield by critiquing the very foundations of rational sciences, particularly logic.
His critique aims to resolve or reframe the conflict.

بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم مقدمة العلامة الدكتور السيد سليمان النذوى، مدير مجلة «معارف»، أعظم كره، الهند. كتاب الرد على المنطقيين هذا كتاب لم يُنسَج على منواله ولم يسبق له نظير . فهو نقد ما قاله وأصله وأسسه أرسطو حكيم اليونانيين في نقد أدلة العقل وترجيح بعضها على بعض بأصول وقواعد وقوانينَ تَعْصِمُ مراعاتها الذهنَ عن الخطأ في الفكر وترتيب المعلوم لتحصيل المجهول، وسماها «علم المنطق». نقل هذا العلم في جملة ما نقل من العلوم اليونانية إلى العربية أيام حضارة العباسيين في القرن الثالث للهجرة، بأيدي نَقَلة السُّريانيين والعبرانيين كما نعرفُ خبره في كتاب «الفهرست» لابن النديم البغدادي الموجود في آخر القرن الرابع. فنقل هذا العلم باباً باباً وفنا فنا حتى تم كله وحَصَل جُلّه عند عارفي اللغة العربية . ولم يزل علماء المنقول من أئمة الدين من المفسرين والمحدثين والفقهاء في مَعْزِلٍ منه حتى حَرَّم منهم من حَرَّمه ونسب إلى الزندقة مَنْ نَظَر فيه، حتى إن جلال الدين السيوطي المتوفى سنة ٩١١ هـ ـ وقد كان علماء المسلمين تبقروا في هذه العلوم وتوسعوا في معرفة حقهم من باطلهم - وَضَع رسالة في تحريم علم المنطق . وقد كان علماء الإسلام قبل أبي حامد الغزالي على فرقتين: فرقة اعتكفوا للمنقول من التفسير والفقه والحديث، وأخرى للمعقول من العلوم الطبيعية والإلهية والرياضية وغيرها. وقد كانت بينهم حرب عوان يَشُنُّ بعضهم على بعض غارة شعواء،
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Introduction of the distinguished scholar Dr. Sayyid Sulayman Nadwi, director of the journal 'Ma'arif', Azamgarh, India. The book 'The Refutation of the Logicians'. This is a book unlike any other and without precedent. It is a critique of what Aristotle, the philosopher of the Greeks, said and established in criticism of the proofs of the intellect and preferring some over others with principles, rules, and laws whose observance protects the mind from error in thought and the arrangement of known things to obtain the unknown, and he called it 'The science of logic'. This science was transmitted along with what was transmitted from Greek sciences into Arabic during the Abbasid civilization in the third century AH, by the hands of Syriac and Hebrew translators, as we know its account in the book 'al-Fihrist' by Ibn al-Nadim al-Baghdadi from the end of the fourth century. So this science was transmitted chapter by chapter and discipline by discipline until it was completed and most of it was obtained by those knowledgeable in Arabic. And the scholars of transmitted sciences from the religious leaders – exegetes, hadith scholars, and jurists – kept aloof from it until some of them declared it forbidden and accused those who looked into it of heresy, even that Jalal al-Din al-Suyuti, who died in 911 AH – while Muslim scholars had become thorough in these sciences and expanded in knowledge of their truth from falsehood – wrote a treatise on the prohibition of logic. And before Abu Hamid al-Ghazali, the scholars of Islam were divided into two groups: a group devoted to transmitted sciences: exegesis, fiqh, and hadith; and another to rational sciences: natural, divine, mathematical, and others. And between them was a fierce war in which one group launched a fierce attack on the other.
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage is the introduction by Dr. Sulayman Nadwi to Ibn Taymiyya's 'Radd al-Mantiqiyyin'. It begins with the basmala and identifies the author of the introduction. Then it asserts the uniqueness of Ibn Taymiyya's work as an unprecedented critique of Aristotelian logic. Nadwi explains that logic was translated from Greek into Arabic during the Abbasid era by Syriac and Hebrew translators, as recorded by Ibn al-Nadim. He notes that many traditional religious scholars (mufassirun, muhaddithun, fuqaha) initially kept away from logic, some even declaring it forbidden and accusing its practitioners of heresy, such as al-Suyuti's treatise. Before al-Ghazali, scholars were split between those focused on transmitted sciences (naql) and those focused on rational sciences ('aql). There was a fierce conflict between these two camps.

Before al-Ghazali, Islamic scholars were divided into two hostile camps: one focusing on transmitted sciences and the other on rational sciences, with logic at the center of the conflict.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Definition and Translation of Greek Logic
Nadwi defines logic and describes its translation into Arabic.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Aristotelian definition of logic and describe how it was transmitted into Islamic civilization.

Core Idea
Aristotle's logic entered Islam as a foreign science, transmitted by Syriac and Hebrew translators.

Dr. al-Nadwi begins his introduction by defining logic as Aristotle's system for critiquing proofs and safeguarding the mind. He then explains how this science was translated into Arabic during the Abbasid era. Understanding this origin is essential for grasping why later scholars like Ibn Taymiyya engaged with it critically.

Guided Path
1
Locate Aristotle's definition of logic in the Arabic text
Find the sentence beginning with 'نقد ما قاله وأصله...' and identify the key components: critique of proofs, rules to preserve the mind from error.
The definition is presented as the foundation of 'ilm al-mantiq.
2
Trace the translation chain
Note the mention of Syriac and Hebrew intermediaries and the reference to Ibn al-Nadim's 'Al-Fihrist'. This shows the historical path of transmission.
3
Observe the attitude of early transmitted scholars
Identify the sentence stating that exegetes, hadith scholars, and jurists kept aloof from logic. Some declared it forbidden and accused its students of heresy.
This sets the stage for the later conflict.

مقدمة العلامة الدكتور السيد سليمان النذوى، مدير مجلة «معارف»، أعظم كره، الهند. كتاب الرد على المنطقيين هذا كتاب لم يُنسَج على منواله ولم يسبق له نظير . فهو نقد ما قاله وأصله وأسسه أرسطو حكيم اليونانيين في نقد أدلة العقل وترجيح بعضها على بعض بأصول وقواعد وقوانينَ تَعْصِمُ مراعاتها الذهنَ عن الخطأ في الفكر وترتيب المعلوم لتحصيل المجهول، وسماها «علم المنطق». نقل هذا العلم في جملة ما نقل من العلوم اليونانية إلى العربية أيام حضارة العباسيين في القرن الثالث للهجرة، بأيدي نَقَلة السُّريانيين والعبرانيين كما نعرفُ خبره في كتاب الفهرست» لابن النديم البغدادي الموجود في آخر القرن الرابع. فنقل هذا العلم باباً باباً وفنا فنا حتى تم كله وحَصَل جُلّه عند عارفي اللغة العربية . ولم يزل علماء المنقول من أئمة الدين من المفسرين والمحدثين والفقهاء في مَعْزِلٍ منه حتى حَرَّم منهم من حَرَّمه ونسب إلى الزندقة مَنْ نَظَر فيه، حتى إن جلال الدين السيوطي المتوفى سنة ٩١١ هـ ـ وقد كان علماء المسلمين تبقروا في هذه العلوم وتوسعوا في معرفة حقهم من باطلهم - وَضَع رسالة في تحريم علم المنطق . وقد كان علماء الإسلام قبل أبي حامد الغزالي على فرقتين: فرقة اعتكفوا للمنقول من التفسير والفقه والحديث، وأخرى للمعقول من العلوم الطبيعية والإلهية والرياضية وغيرها. وقد كانت بينهم حرب عوان يَشُنُّ بعضهم على بعض غارة شعواء، وبينهما عداوة وشحناء فيحسب علماء المنقول حكماء المعقول ملاحدة وزنادقة وينسب الحكماء إليهم من الجهل بالحقيقة والجحود بما يثبت عند العقل من الحق . فقام ناس زمن الديالمة وأرادوا التوفيق بين الفرقتين والتطبيق بين العلمين، وهم مؤلفو رسائل إخوان الصفاء وأمثالهم . فقالوا ما جاد به الحكماء وما جاء به الأنبياء دين واحد وكلاهما حق فأصَّلوا ما قال الحكماء وأوَّلوا ما جاء به الأنبياء وردُّوه إلى أقوالهم وتعاليمهم، وهم الباطنية والإسماعيلية. وفي آخرهم أبو علي ابن سينا الذي وَلَده الإسماعيلية وتربَّى وترعرع في حُجورهم، كما قال ابن سينا عن نفسه (راجع ترجمته في طبقات «الأطباء» لابن أبي أصيبعة وانظر في هذا الكتاب في صحيفة ١٨٣). ثم جاء الغزالي من فقهاء الشافعية زمن ملوك السَّلاجقة من أهل السنة، والباطنية في جبالهم يحملون على شيوخ أهل السنة بشككهم وخناجرهم وعلى شبيبتهم بشكوكهم ودفاترهم، فتزلزل عالم الإسلام وزلت أقدامُ الأفهام وضلت آراء حملة الأقلام . فقام الغزالي أحسن قيام وتسلّح بسلاحهم وتدرع بدروعهم، واختار حقهم وردَّ باطِلَهم، فمنع ثغور الدين عن غاراتهم وكتب وألف ووضع كتباً ورسائل و مجلدات في توفيق الرأيين، فخلط بين العلمين وآخى بين الحزبين (راجع الكتاب، صفحة ۲۳۸ و ۲۳۹). فنشأ به متكلّمون غَرَّهم زَخْرَفة القول ومموّهات العقول، فتفرقوا فرَقاً واختلقوا أقوالاً وهم يَحْسَبون أنهم يُحسنون صُنْعا (راجع هذا الكتاب، صفحة ۱۸۹ - ۱۸۳). ثم قدر الله تعالى لهذه الأمة المرحومة من علماء الدين رجلاً نافذ البصيرة غيوراً على الدين عارفاً بكتاب الله وسنة رسوله وعالماً بأقوال الحكماء ومميّزاً بين حقهم وباطلهم وعارفاً بفنون الحكمة كلها وآراء عقلائهم كلهم ولم يقصر علمه على أرسطاليس وشارحه ابن سينا بل نظر في علوم جميع طبقاتهم وعرف أفكار فرقهم وطوائفهم وأساكلهم، فرد هذا بهذا ورَجّح ذاك بذاك . وهو العلامة الإمام الحافظ ابن تيمية صاحب هذا الكتاب.
Introduction of the eminent scholar Dr. Sayyid Sulayman al-Nadwi, director of the magazine 'Ma'arif', Azamgarh, India. The book 'Al-Radd 'ala al-Mantiqiyyin' (Refutation of the Logicians) is a book unparalleled in its style, without precedent. It is a critique of what was said and originated and founded by Aristotle, the philosopher of the Greeks, regarding the critique of intellectual proofs and weighing some over others by principles, rules, and laws whose observance preserves the mind from error in thought and the arrangement of known information to acquire the unknown, which he called 'the science of logic'. This science was transmitted among what was transmitted from Greek sciences into Arabic during the Abbasid civilization in the third century AH, by the hands of Syriac and Hebrew translators, as we know its account in the book 'Al-Fihrist' by Ibn al-Nadim al-Baghdadi, who lived at the end of the fourth century. So this science was transmitted chapter by chapter and discipline by discipline until it was completed and most of it was obtained by those familiar with the Arabic language. And the scholars of transmitted sciences among the religious leaders—exegetes, hadith scholars, and jurists—continued to keep aloof from it, until some of them declared it forbidden and accused of heresy whoever studied it. So much so that Jalal al-Din al-Suyuti (d. 911 AH)—and Muslim scholars had delved into these sciences and expanded in knowledge of their truth from their falsehood—wrote a treatise on the prohibition of the science of logic. Before Abu Hamid al-Ghazali, Muslim scholars were divided into two groups: a group that secluded themselves for the transmitted sciences of tafsir, fiqh, and hadith, and another group for the rational sciences of natural philosophy, theology, mathematics, etc. Between them was a relentless war, each launching a fierce attack on the other, with enmity and hatred. The transmitted scholars considered the rational philosophers heretics and infidels, while the philosophers attributed to them ignorance of reality and denial of truth established by reason. Then some people during the time of the Daylamites arose and sought reconciliation between the two groups and integration of the two sciences. They were the authors of the Epistles of the Brethren of Purity and their likes. They said that what the philosophers produced and what the prophets brought are one religion, both truth, so they grounded what the philosophers said and interpreted what the prophets brought, reducing it to their own sayings and teachings. They were the Batinis and Isma'ilis. And among the last of them was Abu 'Ali Ibn Sina, whom the Isma'ilis sired and who was raised and grew up in their care, as Ibn Sina said of himself (see his biography in 'Tabaqat al-Atibba' by Ibn Abi Usaybi'a and see in this book on page 183). Then came al-Ghazali, one of the Shafi'i jurists during the time of the Seljuk sultans from Ahl al-Sunnah, while the Batinis were in their mountains attacking the Sunni scholars with their doubts and daggers, and their youth with their suspicions and books. So the world of Islam was shaken, the feet of understanding slipped, and the opinions of those who held pens went astray. Then al-Ghazali stood up excellently, armed himself with their weapons, donned their armor, selected their truth and rejected their falsehood, thus defending the frontiers of religion from their attacks. He wrote and composed books, treatises, and volumes on reconciling the two views, mixing the two sciences and making brotherhood between the two parties (see the book, pages 238 and 239). Consequently, there arose theologians who were deceived by the embellishment of speech and the delusions of intellects, so they split into sects and invented doctrines, thinking that they were doing good (see this book, pages 183-189). Then Allah decreed for this blessed community among the religious scholars a man of penetrating insight, zealous for religion, knowledgeable in the Book of Allah and the Sunnah of His Messenger, well-versed in the sayings of the philosophers, distinguishing between their truth and falsehood, knowledgeable in all the arts of wisdom and the opinions of all their intellectuals. He did not limit his knowledge to Aristotle and his commentator Ibn Sina, but rather examined the sciences of all their classes and knew the thoughts of their sects, groups, and methods, thus refuting some by others and preferring some over others. He is the eminent Imam, the memorizer, Ibn Taymiyya, the author of this book.
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage is the introduction by Dr. Sulayman al-Nadwi to Ibn Taymiyya's 'Al-Radd 'ala al-Mantiqiyyin'. It sets the historical stage for why the book is significant. The introduction begins by describing Ibn Taymiyya's work as unique and unprecedented, a critique of Aristotle's logic. It then recounts how Greek logic was translated into Arabic during the Abbasid period via Syriac and Hebrew intermediaries, as recorded in Ibn al-Nadim's 'Al-Fihrist'. The passage notes that early Muslim scholars of transmitted sciences (exegesis, hadith, fiqh) kept aloof from logic, and some declared it forbidden, even accusing its practitioners of heresy. Al-Suyuti authored a treatise prohibiting logic. This period was marked by a sharp divide between scholars of transmitted sciences and those of rational sciences (natural philosophy, theology, mathematics). The 'Brethren of Purity' and others, identified as Batinis and Isma'ilis, sought to reconcile the two but ended up subordinating revelation to philosophy. Ibn Sina is mentioned as a product of this milieu. Then the passage describes the threat posed by the Batinis during Ghazali's time, and how Ghazali defended Sunni orthodoxy by engaging with their arguments, writing works that mixed the two sciences. This led to later theologians being deceived by sophistry. Finally, the introduction culminates with Allah sending Ibn Taymiyya, a scholar with deep knowledge of both scripture and philosophy, capable of distinguishing truth from falsehood and refuting the logicians. This historical account frames Ibn Taymiyya's work as a necessary corrective to the errors introduced by Greek logic and its Islamic proponents.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
6 min
The Conflict Between Transmitted and Rational Sciences
Nadwi describes the pre-Ghazali divide and the rise of reconciliation movements.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the divide between scholars of transmitted sciences and rational sciences, and identify the groups that attempted reconciliation.

Core Idea
The conflict between manqul and ma'qul split the Ummah, and esoteric groups tried to merge them.

Before al-Ghazali, Muslim scholars were sharply divided: one group focused solely on transmitted sciences (tafsir, fiqh, hadith), the other on rational sciences (natural philosophy, theology). Nadwi describes this as a 'relentless war'. He then introduces the Brethren of Purity, the Batinis, and the Isma'ilis as those who sought to reconcile the two—but at the cost of subordinating revelation to philosophy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two opposing groups
Find the sentences that begin with 'فرقة اعتكفوا للمنقول' and 'وأخرى للمعقول'. These describe the transmitted scholars and the rational scholars.
Notice the strong language: 'حرب عوان' (relentless war).
2
Examine the accusations each group made against the other
The transmitted scholars called the rational scholars heretics; the rational scholars accused the transmitted scholars of ignorance and denial.
This mutual hostility is key to understanding the context.
3
Analyze the attempted reconciliation by the Brethren of Purity and the Batinis
They claimed that philosophy and prophecy are one religion. They grounded philosophy and interpreted revelation to align with it.
Nadwi presents this as a distortion of revelation.

مقدمة العلامة الدكتور السيد سليمان النذوى، مدير مجلة «معارف»، أعظم كره، الهند. كتاب الرد على المنطقيين هذا كتاب لم يُنسَج على منواله ولم يسبق له نظير . فهو نقد ما قاله وأصله وأسسه أرسطو حكيم اليونانيين في نقد أدلة العقل وترجيح بعضها على بعض بأصول وقواعد وقوانينَ تَعْصِمُ مراعاتها الذهنَ عن الخطأ في الفكر وترتيب المعلوم لتحصيل المجهول، وسماها «علم المنطق». نقل هذا العلم في جملة ما نقل من العلوم اليونانية إلى العربية أيام حضارة العباسيين في القرن الثالث للهجرة، بأيدي نَقَلة السُّريانيين والعبرانيين كما نعرفُ خبره في كتاب الفهرست» لابن النديم البغدادي الموجود في آخر القرن الرابع. فنقل هذا العلم باباً باباً وفنا فنا حتى تم كله وحَصَل جُلّه عند عارفي اللغة العربية . ولم يزل علماء المنقول من أئمة الدين من المفسرين والمحدثين والفقهاء في مَعْزِلٍ منه حتى حَرَّم منهم من حَرَّمه ونسب إلى الزندقة مَنْ نَظَر فيه، حتى إن جلال الدين السيوطي المتوفى سنة ٩١١ هـ ـ وقد كان علماء المسلمين تبقروا في هذه العلوم وتوسعوا في معرفة حقهم من باطلهم - وَضَع رسالة في تحريم علم المنطق . وقد كان علماء الإسلام قبل أبي حامد الغزالي على فرقتين: فرقة اعتكفوا للمنقول من التفسير والفقه والحديث، وأخرى للمعقول من العلوم الطبيعية والإلهية والرياضية وغيرها. وقد كانت بينهم حرب عوان يَشُنُّ بعضهم على بعض غارة شعواء، وبينهما عداوة وشحناء فيحسب علماء المنقول حكماء المعقول ملاحدة وزنادقة وينسب الحكماء إليهم من الجهل بالحقيقة والجحود بما يثبت عند العقل من الحق . فقام ناس زمن الديالمة وأرادوا التوفيق بين الفرقتين والتطبيق بين العلمين، وهم مؤلفو رسائل إخوان الصفاء وأمثالهم . فقالوا ما جاد به الحكماء وما جاء به الأنبياء دين واحد وكلاهما حق فأصَّلوا ما قال الحكماء وأوَّلوا ما جاء به الأنبياء وردُّوه إلى أقوالهم وتعاليمهم، وهم الباطنية والإسماعيلية. وفي آخرهم أبو علي ابن سينا الذي وَلَده الإسماعيلية وتربَّى وترعرع في حُجورهم، كما قال ابن سينا عن نفسه (راجع ترجمته في طبقات «الأطباء» لابن أبي أصيبعة وانظر في هذا الكتاب في صحيفة ١٨٣). ثم جاء الغزالي من فقهاء الشافعية زمن ملوك السَّلاجقة من أهل السنة، والباطنية في جبالهم يحملون على شيوخ أهل السنة بشككهم وخناجرهم وعلى شبيبتهم بشكوكهم ودفاترهم، فتزلزل عالم الإسلام وزلت أقدامُ الأفهام وضلت آراء حملة الأقلام . فقام الغزالي أحسن قيام وتسلّح بسلاحهم وتدرع بدروعهم، واختار حقهم وردَّ باطِلَهم، فمنع ثغور الدين عن غاراتهم وكتب وألف ووضع كتباً ورسائل و مجلدات في توفيق الرأيين، فخلط بين العلمين وآخى بين الحزبين (راجع الكتاب، صفحة ۲۳۸ و ۲۳۹). فنشأ به متكلّمون غَرَّهم زَخْرَفة القول ومموّهات العقول، فتفرقوا فرَقاً واختلقوا أقوالاً وهم يَحْسَبون أنهم يُحسنون صُنْعا (راجع هذا الكتاب، صفحة ۱۸۹ - ۱۸۳). ثم قدر الله تعالى لهذه الأمة المرحومة من علماء الدين رجلاً نافذ البصيرة غيوراً على الدين عارفاً بكتاب الله وسنة رسوله وعالماً بأقوال الحكماء ومميّزاً بين حقهم وباطلهم وعارفاً بفنون الحكمة كلها وآراء عقلائهم كلهم ولم يقصر علمه على أرسطاليس وشارحه ابن سينا بل نظر في علوم جميع طبقاتهم وعرف أفكار فرقهم وطوائفهم وأساكلهم، فرد هذا بهذا ورَجّح ذاك بذاك . وهو العلامة الإمام الحافظ ابن تيمية صاحب هذا الكتاب.
Introduction of the eminent scholar Dr. Sayyid Sulayman al-Nadwi, director of the magazine 'Ma'arif', Azamgarh, India. The book 'Al-Radd 'ala al-Mantiqiyyin' (Refutation of the Logicians) is a book unparalleled in its style, without precedent. It is a critique of what was said and originated and founded by Aristotle, the philosopher of the Greeks, regarding the critique of intellectual proofs and weighing some over others by principles, rules, and laws whose observance preserves the mind from error in thought and the arrangement of known information to acquire the unknown, which he called 'the science of logic'. This science was transmitted among what was transmitted from Greek sciences into Arabic during the Abbasid civilization in the third century AH, by the hands of Syriac and Hebrew translators, as we know its account in the book 'Al-Fihrist' by Ibn al-Nadim al-Baghdadi, who lived at the end of the fourth century. So this science was transmitted chapter by chapter and discipline by discipline until it was completed and most of it was obtained by those familiar with the Arabic language. And the scholars of transmitted sciences among the religious leaders—exegetes, hadith scholars, and jurists—continued to keep aloof from it, until some of them declared it forbidden and accused of heresy whoever studied it. So much so that Jalal al-Din al-Suyuti (d. 911 AH)—and Muslim scholars had delved into these sciences and expanded in knowledge of their truth from their falsehood—wrote a treatise on the prohibition of the science of logic. Before Abu Hamid al-Ghazali, Muslim scholars were divided into two groups: a group that secluded themselves for the transmitted sciences of tafsir, fiqh, and hadith, and another group for the rational sciences of natural philosophy, theology, mathematics, etc. Between them was a relentless war, each launching a fierce attack on the other, with enmity and hatred. The transmitted scholars considered the rational philosophers heretics and infidels, while the philosophers attributed to them ignorance of reality and denial of truth established by reason. Then some people during the time of the Daylamites arose and sought reconciliation between the two groups and integration of the two sciences. They were the authors of the Epistles of the Brethren of Purity and their likes. They said that what the philosophers produced and what the prophets brought are one religion, both truth, so they grounded what the philosophers said and interpreted what the prophets brought, reducing it to their own sayings and teachings. They were the Batinis and Isma'ilis. And among the last of them was Abu 'Ali Ibn Sina, whom the Isma'ilis sired and who was raised and grew up in their care, as Ibn Sina said of himself (see his biography in 'Tabaqat al-Atibba' by Ibn Abi Usaybi'a and see in this book on page 183). Then came al-Ghazali, one of the Shafi'i jurists during the time of the Seljuk sultans from Ahl al-Sunnah, while the Batinis were in their mountains attacking the Sunni scholars with their doubts and daggers, and their youth with their suspicions and books. So the world of Islam was shaken, the feet of understanding slipped, and the opinions of those who held pens went astray. Then al-Ghazali stood up excellently, armed himself with their weapons, donned their armor, selected their truth and rejected their falsehood, thus defending the frontiers of religion from their attacks. He wrote and composed books, treatises, and volumes on reconciling the two views, mixing the two sciences and making brotherhood between the two parties (see the book, pages 238 and 239). Consequently, there arose theologians who were deceived by the embellishment of speech and the delusions of intellects, so they split into sects and invented doctrines, thinking that they were doing good (see this book, pages 183-189). Then Allah decreed for this blessed community among the religious scholars a man of penetrating insight, zealous for religion, knowledgeable in the Book of Allah and the Sunnah of His Messenger, well-versed in the sayings of the philosophers, distinguishing between their truth and falsehood, knowledgeable in all the arts of wisdom and the opinions of all their intellectuals. He did not limit his knowledge to Aristotle and his commentator Ibn Sina, but rather examined the sciences of all their classes and knew the thoughts of their sects, groups, and methods, thus refuting some by others and preferring some over others. He is the eminent Imam, the memorizer, Ibn Taymiyya, the author of this book.
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage is the introduction by Dr. Sulayman al-Nadwi to Ibn Taymiyya's 'Al-Radd 'ala al-Mantiqiyyin'. It sets the historical stage for why the book is significant. The introduction begins by describing Ibn Taymiyya's work as unique and unprecedented, a critique of Aristotle's logic. It then recounts how Greek logic was translated into Arabic during the Abbasid period via Syriac and Hebrew intermediaries, as recorded in Ibn al-Nadim's 'Al-Fihrist'. The passage notes that early Muslim scholars of transmitted sciences (exegesis, hadith, fiqh) kept aloof from logic, and some declared it forbidden, even accusing its practitioners of heresy. Al-Suyuti authored a treatise prohibiting logic. This period was marked by a sharp divide between scholars of transmitted sciences and those of rational sciences (natural philosophy, theology, mathematics). The 'Brethren of Purity' and others, identified as Batinis and Isma'ilis, sought to reconcile the two but ended up subordinating revelation to philosophy. Ibn Sina is mentioned as a product of this milieu. Then the passage describes the threat posed by the Batinis during Ghazali's time, and how Ghazali defended Sunni orthodoxy by engaging with their arguments, writing works that mixed the two sciences. This led to later theologians being deceived by sophistry. Finally, the introduction culminates with Allah sending Ibn Taymiyya, a scholar with deep knowledge of both scripture and philosophy, capable of distinguishing truth from falsehood and refuting the logicians. This historical account frames Ibn Taymiyya's work as a necessary corrective to the errors introduced by Greek logic and its Islamic proponents.

المعقول

Checkpoint
According to Nadwi, what was the main error of the Brethren of Purity and the Batinis in their attempt to reconcile sciences?
A) They rejected philosophy entirely.
B) They subordinated revelation to philosophy by interpreting prophecy to fit philosophical doctrines.
C) They denied both revelation and reason.
D) They focused only on the transmitted sciences.

Key Takeaway
The pre-Ghazali divide between transmitted and rational sciences was deep, and early reconciliation attempts by groups like the Brethren of Purity distorted revelation to fit philosophy.

List three key differences between the transmitted and rational approaches to knowledge as described by Nadwi.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
7 min
Ghazali's Synthesis and Ibn Taymiyya's Critical Response
Nadwi describes Ghazali's synthesis, its negative aftermath, and Ibn Taymiyya's emergence as a corrective.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the consequences of al-Ghazali's integration of logic into Sunni theology and how Ibn Taymiyya's critique addressed the resulting confusion.

Core Idea
Ghazali's mixing of sciences gave rise to confused theologians; Ibn Taymiyya's penetrating critique restored clarity.

Nadwi narrates how al-Ghazali, in defense against the Batinis, adopted their weapons and produced works mixing logic with theology. This led to a generation of theologians deceived by sophistry. Then Allah raised Ibn Taymiyya, a scholar uniquely qualified to distinguish truth from falsehood in both transmitted and rational sciences. This sets the stage for the book's critical evaluation of logic.

Guided Path
1
Understand Ghazali's motive and method
The Batinis were attacking Sunni scholars. Ghazali armed himself with their weapons and selected their truth while rejecting falsehood, but in the process he mixed the two sciences.
Nadwi uses the phrase 'خلط بين العلمين' (mixed the two sciences).
2
Identify the unintended consequence
Find the sentence that states that theologians arose who were deceived by embellished speech and delusions, leading to division and false doctrines.
This consequence is presented as negative.
3
Recognize Ibn Taymiyya's qualifications
Nadwi describes Ibn Taymiyya as having penetrating insight, knowledge of scripture, and comprehensive understanding of philosophical schools—able to distinguish truth from falsehood.
Note that he did not limit himself to Aristotle and Ibn Sina but studied all sects.

Commentary
This passage is the introduction by Dr. Sulayman al-Nadwi to Ibn Taymiyya's 'Al-Radd 'ala al-Mantiqiyyin'. It sets the historical stage for why the book is significant. The introduction begins by describing Ibn Taymiyya's work as unique and unprecedented, a critique of Aristotle's logic. It then recounts how Greek logic was translated into Arabic during the Abbasid period via Syriac and Hebrew intermediaries, as recorded in Ibn al-Nadim's 'Al-Fihrist'. Ibn Sina is mentioned as a product of this milieu. Then the passage describes the threat posed by the Batinis during Ghazali's time, and how Ghazali defended Sunni orthodoxy by engaging with their arguments, writing works that mixed the two sciences. Checkpoint
According to Nadwi, what was the main negative consequence of al-Ghazali's mixing of sciences?
A) It united all scholars under one methodology.
B) It led to the rise of theologians deceived by sophistry who split into sects.
C) It permanently ended the Batini threat.
D) It caused the fall of the Seljuk Empire.

Key Takeaway
Ghazali's integration of logic into Sunni theology had unintended consequences that Ibn Taymiyya sought to correct by returning to a scripture-based methodology while critically engaging philosophical arguments.

Read the passage where Nadwi describes the theologians deceived by Ghazali's synthesis. Identify one example of a theological doctrine that might have been influenced by logical sophistry (e.g., from later Ash'ari or Maturidi texts).
?
Write a short essay arguing whether Ibn Taymiyya's approach—using philosophy against itself—is a valid method of refutation. Support your argument with examples from this introduction.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
5 min
The Historic Tension between Transmitted and Rational Sciences
Introduction describes the enmity between naql and aql and the first reconciliation attempts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two main camps in the classical Islamic intellectual tradition and describe their mutual accusations.

Core Idea
The conflict between naql and aql defined Islamic intellectual history.

In this lesson, we examine the deep-rooted enmity between scholars of transmitted knowledge and philosophers, as described in Nadwi's introduction. Understanding this tension is crucial for grasping Ibn Taymiyya's later critique.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two camps
Find the terms 'ulamā' al-manqūl' and 'ḥukamā' al-maʿqūl' in the Arabic. What does each camp accuse the other of?
2
Trace the reconciliation attempt
Who were the Brethren of Purity? What was their approach to harmonizing philosophy and revelation?
3
Recognize the Ismaili connection
How does the passage link Ibn Sina to the Ismailis? Why is this relevant to understanding the tension?

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مقدمة الدكتور الندوي وبينهما عداوة وشحناء فيحسب علماء المنقول حكماء المعقول ملاحدة وزنادقة وينسب الحكماء إليهم من الجهل بالحقيقة والجحود بما يثبت عند العقل من الحق . فقام ناس زمن الديالمة وأرادوا التوفيق بين الفرقتين والتطبيق بين العلمين، وهم مؤلفو رسائل إخوان الصفاء وأمثالهم . فقالوا ما جاد به الحكماء وما جاء به الأنبياء دين واحد وكلاهما حق فأصَّلوا ما قال الحكماء وأوَّلوا ما جاء به الأنبياء وردُّوه إلى أقوالهم وتعاليمهم، وهم الباطنية والإسماعيلية. وفي آخرهم أبو علي ابن سينا الذي وَلَده الإسماعيلية وتربَّى وترعرع في حُجورهم، كما قال ابن سينا عن نفسه (راجع ترجمته في طبقات «الأطباء» لابن أبي أصيبعة وانظر في هذا الكتاب في صحيفة ١٨٣). ثم جاء الغزالي من فقهاء الشافعية زمن ملوك السَّلاجقة من أهل السنة، والباطنية في جبالهم يحملون على شيوخ أهل السنة بشككهم وخناجرهم وعلى شبيبتهم بشكوكهم ودفاترهم، فتزلزل عالم الإسلام وزلت أقدامُ الأفهام وضلت آراء حملة الأقلام . فقام الغزالي أحسن قيام وتسلّح بسلاحهم وتدرع بدروعهم، واختار حقهم وردَّ باطِلَهم، فمنع ثغور الدين عن غاراتهم وكتب وألف ووضع كتباً ورسائل و مجلدات في توفيق الرأيين، فخلط بين العلمين وآخى بين الحزبين (راجع الكتاب، صفحة ٢٣٨ و ٢٣٩). فنشأ به متكلّمون غَرَّهم زَخْرَفة القول ومموّهات العقول، فتفرقوا فرَقاً واختلقوا أقوالاً وهم يَحْسَبون أنهم يُحسنون صُنْعا (راجع هذا الكتاب، صفحة ١٨٩ - ١٨٣). ثم قدر الله تعالى لهذه الأمة المرحومة من علماء الدين رجلاً نافذ البصيرة غيوراً على الدين عارفاً بكتاب الله وسنة رسوله وعالماً بأقوال الحكماء ومميّزاً بين حقهم وباطلهم وعارفاً بفنون الحكمة كلها وآراء عقلائهم كلهم ولم يقصر علمه على أرسطاليس وشارحه ابن سينا بل نظر في علوم جميع طبقاتهم وعرف أفكار فرقهم وطوائفهم وأساكلهم، فرد هذا بهذا ورَجّح ذاك بذاك . وهو العلامة الإمام الحافظ ابن تيمية صاحب هذا الكتاب. (صفحة ١٧) قد بسطتُ في مقالتي في رد مَنْ قال إن حكماء المسلمين لم يكونوا إلا خَدَمة لأرسطو التي ظهرت في مجلة «الثقافة الإسلامية الصادرة في حيدرآباد الدكن بالإنكليزية، المجلد الأول سنة ١٩٢٧ م . فعدّدت مواضع ذكر فيها ابن تيمية فلاسفة اليونانيين وآراءهم وفند آراء ابن سينا وجَهله وقال فيه : إنه لا يعرف غير أرسطو . وقد أكثر هذا المعنى في كتابه . وترى في هذا الكتاب ما يدل على أن ابن تيمية له ولوع بكتاب «المعتبر» لأبي البركات البغدادي وجمعت فيما كتبتُ في آخر كتاب «المعتبر» الذي طبعته دائرة المعارف العثمانية أقوال الإمام فيه وفي كتابه في هذا الكتاب وكتابه المعبر «ببيان موافقة صريح المعقول الصحيح المنقول»، و«منهاج السنة». فأكثر الثناء عليه، وأخذ منه مسائل استحسنها والقول بتسلسل حوادث لا أول لها فأول من قال بهذا أبو البركات في معتبره»، واتبعه فيه ابن تيمية، فقلَّ من كتبه ومقالاته إلا وفيه تصريح بهذه المسئلة، وقد عابه معاصره الأستاذ الإمام السبكي في قصيدته بقوله بهذه المسئلة (1) . وأبو البركات هذا لم يقلد أرسطو تقليد ابن سينا فقال ابن تيمية في هذا الكتاب : وأبو البركات وأمثاله قد رَدّوا على أرسطو ما شاء الله». والجزء الأول من (۱) هذا ما قال السبكي في قصيدته : الله ، سبحـانـه عمـا يَظُـن بـه يَرَى حوادث لا مبدا لأولهــــا في وهذا ما رده به الشيخ محمد اليافعي الشافعي اليمني : وخالق قبل مخلوق يكونـه وقاهر قبل مقهور یکون به وراحـــم قبـــل مـــرحـــــوم فيــــرحمـــــه ورازق قبل مرزوق بأضربه عن أمره صَدّر المخلوق أجمعه والأمر - ويحك ـ لا شك يقوم به وقد تكلم ربُّ العرش بالكتـب الـ منزلات کلاماً لا شبیه به ولم يزل فاعلاً أو قائلاً أزلاً إذا يشاء، فارض بــــــه هذى حوادث لا مبدا لأولها بالنص فافهمـه یـا نـومـان! فانتبه الناشر
Introduction by Dr. Nadwi: And between them there was enmity and hostility, so the scholars of transmitted knowledge consider the philosophers of intellectual knowledge to be heretics and atheists, and the philosophers attribute to them ignorance of truth and rejection of what is established by reason as truth. Then some people arose in the time of the Daylamites and wanted to reconcile the two groups and harmonize the two sciences, and they are the authors of the Epistles of the Brethren of Purity and their likes. They said: What the philosophers produced and what the prophets brought is one religion, and both are true. So they established what the philosophers said and interpreted what the prophets brought, and reduced it to their own sayings and teachings. They are the Batinis and Ismailis. And the last of them was Abu Ali Ibn Sina, whom the Ismailis fathered and he was raised and grew up in their care, as Ibn Sina said about himself (see his biography in the Generations of Physicians by Ibn Abi Usaybi'a, and see in this book on page 183). Then came al-Ghazali from the Shafi'i jurists in the time of the Saljuq kings from the Sunnis, while the Batinis were in their mountains attacking the Sunni elders with their doubts and daggers, and their youth with their doubts and notebooks. So the world of Islam was shaken, the feet of understandings slipped, and the opinions of those who carried pens went astray. So al-Ghazali arose in the best manner, armed himself with their weapons, donned their armor, chose their truth, and refuted their falsehood. He defended the frontiers of the religion against their raids, and wrote, authored, and composed books, treatises, and volumes in reconciling the two views. So he mixed the two sciences and fraternized between the two parties (see the book, pages 238 and 239). There arose from him theologians whom the ornamentation of speech and the deceptions of the intellects deluded, so they split into groups and invented sayings, thinking that they were doing well (see this book, pages 183-189). Then Allah Almighty destined for this mercy-covered nation a man from the religious scholars, penetrating in insight, jealous for the religion, knowledgeable of Allah's Book and the Sunna of His Messenger, knowledgeable of the sayings of the philosophers and discerning between their truth and falsehood, knowledgeable of all the arts of philosophy and all the opinions of their rationalists, and he did not limit his knowledge to Aristotle and his commentator Ibn Sina, but rather looked into the sciences of all their classes and knew the ideas of their groups, sects, and schools. He refuted one with another and weighed one against another. He is the great scholar, the Imam, the Hafiz, Ibn Taymiyya, the author of this book. (Page 17) I have elaborated in my article refuting those who said that the Muslim philosophers were only servants of Aristotle, which appeared in the magazine 'Islamic Culture' published in Hyderabad Deccan in English, Volume 1, 1927 CE. I listed the places where Ibn Taymiyya mentioned the Greek philosophers and their opinions, and he criticized Ibn Sina's opinions and his ignorance, and said of him: He knows nothing besides Aristotle. And he repeated this meaning in his book. And you see in this book what indicates that Ibn Taymiyya was fond of the book 'al-Mu'tabar' by Abu al-Barakat al-Baghdadi, and I collected in what I wrote at the end of the book 'al-Mu'tabar' (published by the Ottoman Knowledge Circle) the Imam's statements about him and in his book in this book and his book 'Bayān Muwāfaqat Ṣarīḥ al-Maʿqūl al-Ṣaḥīḥ al-Manqūl' and 'Minhāj al-Sunna'. So he praised him abundantly, and took from him issues that he approved of, such as the statement of the sequence of events without a beginning. The first to say this was Abu al-Barakat in his 'al-Mu'tabar', and Ibn Taymiyya followed him in it. So rarely do you see any of his books and articles except that there is an explicit mention of this issue. His contemporary, the teacher Imam al-Subki, criticized him in his poem for holding this issue (1). And this Abu al-Barakat did not imitate Aristotle the way Ibn Sina did. So Ibn Taymiyya said in this book: 'Abu al-Barakat and his likes have refuted Aristotle as much as Allah willed.' And the first part of (1) This is what al-Subki said in his poem: 'Allah, glorified be He above what they think of Him... He sees events without a beginning for them in the...' And this is what Shaykh Muhammad al-Yafi'i al-Shafi'i al-Yamani refuted him with: 'And a Creator before a created being exists... And a Subduer before a subdued being exists... And a Merciful before one who is shown mercy... And a Provider before one who is provided for... By His command, every created thing was brought into existence... And the command - woe to you - without doubt, stands by Him... And the Lord of the Throne spoke the revealed Books with speech unlike His... And He did not cease to be a doer or a speaker eternally... When He wills, so be pleased with it... These are events without a beginning from the text, so understand it, O Numan! Wake up.' The publisher.
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage is the introduction by Dr. Nadwi, setting the historical and intellectual context for Ibn Taymiyya's work. The author begins by describing the deep enmity between the scholars of transmitted knowledge (ashab al-naql) and the philosophers (ashab al-aql). Then he narrates the attempt at reconciliation by the Brethren of Purity and the Ismailis, who sought to harmonize philosophy and revelation by reinterpreting religious texts to align with philosophical doctrines. Ibn Sina is presented as the culmination of this trend, having been raised in an Ismaili environment. Next, the author discusses al-Ghazali, who arose to defend Sunni Islam against the Batinis. Al-Ghazali's method, however, was to engage with philosophy using its own tools, mixing the two sciences and ultimately leading to confusion among later theologians who were misled by rhetorical embellishments. Finally, the author introduces Ibn Tayyima as a unique figure: one who was thoroughly grounded in both Islamic sciences and Greek philosophy, yet was able to distinguish truth from falsehood without falling into syncretism. Ibn Taymiyya studied all philosophical schools, not just Aristotle and Ibn Sina, and he refuted them on their own grounds. The passage then discusses Ibn Taymiyya's appreciation for Abu al-Barakat al-Baghdadi's 'al-Mu'tabar', particularly the doctrine of the temporal sequence of events without a first event (a controversial position that denied the temporal origination of the world in a certain sense). Ibn Taymiyya adopted this view, and al-Subki criticized him for it. The introduction concludes by noting that Abu al-Barakat did not blindly imitate Aristotle, and Ibn Taymiyya praised him for refuting Aristotle. This historical background is crucial for understanding Ibn Taymiyya's critical stance toward formal logic and his epistemological project.

Checkpoint
According to the introduction, what did the Brethren of Purity and the Ismailis claim?
A) Philosophy and revelation are irreconcilable.
B) What the philosophers said and what the prophets brought are one religion, both true.
C) Reason must be rejected entirely.
D) Prophecy is superior to philosophy.

Key Takeaway
The early Islamic intellectual landscape was marked by a bitter divide between transmitted and rational sciences, with some groups attempting to harmonize them.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Read the passage again and write a paragraph summarizing the mutual accusations between the scholars of manqul and the philosophers.
?
Find two historical figures from the classical period who represent each camp (e.g., Ibn Hanbal for manqul, Ibn Rushd for ma'qul) and note their core positions.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
5 min
Al-Ghazali’s Reconciliation and Its Aftermath
Introduction describes al-Ghazali's defense and the confusion it later caused.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe al-Ghazali's method of engaging with philosophy and explain why later theologians were misled according to Nadwi.

Core Idea
Al-Ghazali used philosophy's own weapons to defend the faith but ended up mixing the two sciences.

This lesson focuses on al-Ghazali's response to the Batini threat and his method of reconciliation. According to Nadwi, his approach, though successful in its time, led to confusion among later theologians.

Guided Path
1
Identify al-Ghazali's context
What was the Batini threat? How did al-Ghazali respond? Find the description of him arming himself with their weapons.
2
Analyze al-Ghazali's method
What does 'tawfiq bayn al-ra'ayn' mean? How did al-Ghazali mix the two sciences?
3
Evaluate the outcome
What unintended consequence did al-Ghazali's approach produce? How were later theologians misled?
