مقدمة الدكتور الندوي وبينهما عداوة وشحناء فيحسب علماء المنقول حكماء المعقول ملاحدة وزنادقة وينسب الحكماء إليهم من الجهل بالحقيقة والجحود بما يثبت عند العقل من الحق . فقام ناس زمن الديالمة وأرادوا التوفيق بين الفرقتين والتطبيق بين العلمين، وهم مؤلفو رسائل إخوان الصفاء وأمثالهم . فقالوا ما جاد به الحكماء وما جاء به الأنبياء دين واحد وكلاهما حق فأصَّلوا ما قال الحكماء وأوَّلوا ما جاء به الأنبياء وردُّوه إلى أقوالهم وتعاليمهم، وهم الباطنية والإسماعيلية. وفي آخرهم أبو علي ابن سينا الذي وَلَده الإسماعيلية وتربَّى وترعرع في حُجورهم، كما قال ابن سينا عن نفسه (راجع ترجمته في طبقات «الأطباء» لابن أبي أصيبعة وانظر في هذا الكتاب في صحيفة ١٨٣). ثم جاء الغزالي من فقهاء الشافعية زمن ملوك السَّلاجقة من أهل السنة، والباطنية في جبالهم يحملون على شيوخ أهل السنة بشككهم وخناجرهم وعلى شبيبتهم بشكوكهم ودفاترهم، فتزلزل عالم الإسلام وزلت أقدامُ الأفهام وضلت آراء حملة الأقلام . فقام الغزالي أحسن قيام وتسلّح بسلاحهم وتدرع بدروعهم، واختار حقهم وردَّ باطِلَهم، فمنع ثغور الدين عن غاراتهم وكتب وألف ووضع كتباً ورسائل و مجلدات في توفيق الرأيين، فخلط بين العلمين وآخى بين الحزبين (راجع الكتاب، صفحة ٢٣٨ و ٢٣٩). فنشأ به متكلّمون غَرَّهم زَخْرَفة القول ومموّهات العقول، فتفرقوا فرَقاً واختلقوا أقوالاً وهم يَحْسَبون أنهم يُحسنون صُنْعا (راجع هذا الكتاب، صفحة ١٨٩ - ١٨٣). ثم قدر الله تعالى لهذه الأمة المرحومة من علماء الدين رجلاً نافذ البصيرة غيوراً على الدين عارفاً بكتاب الله وسنة رسوله وعالماً بأقوال الحكماء ومميّزاً بين حقهم وباطلهم وعارفاً بفنون الحكمة كلها وآراء عقلائهم كلهم ولم يقصر علمه على أرسطاليس وشارحه ابن سينا بل نظر في علوم جميع طبقاتهم وعرف أفكار فرقهم وطوائفهم وأساكلهم، فرد هذا بهذا ورَجّح ذاك بذاك . وهو العلامة الإمام الحافظ ابن تيمية صاحب هذا الكتاب. (صفحة ١٧) قد بسطتُ في مقالتي في رد مَنْ قال إن حكماء المسلمين لم يكونوا إلا خَدَمة لأرسطو التي ظهرت في مجلة «الثقافة الإسلامية الصادرة في حيدرآباد الدكن بالإنكليزية، المجلد الأول سنة ١٩٢٧ م . فعدّدت مواضع ذكر فيها ابن تيمية فلاسفة اليونانيين وآراءهم وفند آراء ابن سينا وجَهله وقال فيه : إنه لا يعرف غير أرسطو . وقد أكثر هذا المعنى في كتابه . وترى في هذا الكتاب ما يدل على أن ابن تيمية له ولوع بكتاب «المعتبر» لأبي البركات البغدادي وجمعت فيما كتبتُ في آخر كتاب «المعتبر» الذي طبعته دائرة المعارف العثمانية أقوال الإمام فيه وفي كتابه في هذا الكتاب وكتابه المعبر «ببيان موافقة صريح المعقول الصحيح المنقول»، و«منهاج السنة». فأكثر الثناء عليه، وأخذ منه مسائل استحسنها والقول بتسلسل حوادث لا أول لها فأول من قال بهذا أبو البركات في معتبره»، واتبعه فيه ابن تيمية، فقلَّ من كتبه ومقالاته إلا وفيه تصريح بهذه المسئلة، وقد عابه معاصره الأستاذ الإمام السبكي في قصيدته بقوله بهذه المسئلة (1) . وأبو البركات هذا لم يقلد أرسطو تقليد ابن سينا فقال ابن تيمية في هذا الكتاب : وأبو البركات وأمثاله قد رَدّوا على أرسطو ما شاء الله». والجزء الأول من (۱) هذا ما قال السبكي في قصيدته : الله ، سبحـانـه عمـا يَظُـن بـه يَرَى حوادث لا مبدا لأولهــــا في وهذا ما رده به الشيخ محمد اليافعي الشافعي اليمني : وخالق قبل مخلوق يكونـه وقاهر قبل مقهور یکون به وراحـــم قبـــل مـــرحـــــوم فيــــرحمـــــه ورازق قبل مرزوق بأضربه عن أمره صَدّر المخلوق أجمعه والأمر - ويحك ـ لا شك يقوم به وقد تكلم ربُّ العرش بالكتـب الـ منزلات کلاماً لا شبیه به ولم يزل فاعلاً أو قائلاً أزلاً إذا يشاء، فارض بــــــه هذى حوادث لا مبدا لأولها بالنص فافهمـه یـا نـومـان! فانتبه الناشر
Introduction by Dr. Nadwi: And between them there was enmity and hostility, so the scholars of transmitted knowledge consider the philosophers of intellectual knowledge to be heretics and atheists, and the philosophers attribute to them ignorance of truth and rejection of what is established by reason as truth. Then some people arose in the time of the Daylamites and wanted to reconcile the two groups and harmonize the two sciences, and they are the authors of the Epistles of the Brethren of Purity and their likes. They said: What the philosophers produced and what the prophets brought is one religion, and both are true. So they established what the philosophers said and interpreted what the prophets brought, and reduced it to their own sayings and teachings. They are the Batinis and Ismailis. And the last of them was Abu Ali Ibn Sina, whom the Ismailis fathered and he was raised and grew up in their care, as Ibn Sina said about himself (see his biography in the Generations of Physicians by Ibn Abi Usaybi'a, and see in this book on page 183). Then came al-Ghazali from the Shafi'i jurists in the time of the Saljuq kings from the Sunnis, while the Batinis were in their mountains attacking the Sunni elders with their doubts and daggers, and their youth with their doubts and notebooks. So the world of Islam was shaken, the feet of understandings slipped, and the opinions of those who carried pens went astray. So al-Ghazali arose in the best manner, armed himself with their weapons, donned their armor, chose their truth, and refuted their falsehood. He defended the frontiers of the religion against their raids, and wrote, authored, and composed books, treatises, and volumes in reconciling the two views. So he mixed the two sciences and fraternized between the two parties (see the book, pages 238 and 239). There arose from him theologians whom the ornamentation of speech and the deceptions of the intellects deluded, so they split into groups and invented sayings, thinking that they were doing well (see this book, pages 183-189). Then Allah Almighty destined for this mercy-covered nation a man from the religious scholars, penetrating in insight, jealous for the religion, knowledgeable of Allah's Book and the Sunna of His Messenger, knowledgeable of the sayings of the philosophers and discerning between their truth and falsehood, knowledgeable of all the arts of philosophy and all the opinions of their rationalists, and he did not limit his knowledge to Aristotle and his commentator Ibn Sina, but rather looked into the sciences of all their classes and knew the ideas of their groups, sects, and schools. He refuted one with another and weighed one against another. He is the great scholar, the Imam, the Hafiz, Ibn Taymiyya, the author of this book. (Page 17) I have elaborated in my article refuting those who said that the Muslim philosophers were only servants of Aristotle, which appeared in the magazine 'Islamic Culture' published in Hyderabad Deccan in English, Volume 1, 1927 CE. I listed the places where Ibn Taymiyya mentioned the Greek philosophers and their opinions, and he criticized Ibn Sina's opinions and his ignorance, and said of him: He knows nothing besides Aristotle. And he repeated this meaning in his book. And you see in this book what indicates that Ibn Taymiyya was fond of the book 'al-Mu'tabar' by Abu al-Barakat al-Baghdadi, and I collected in what I wrote at the end of the book 'al-Mu'tabar' (published by the Ottoman Knowledge Circle) the Imam's statements about him and in his book in this book and his book 'Bayān Muwāfaqat Ṣarīḥ al-Maʿqūl al-Ṣaḥīḥ al-Manqūl' and 'Minhāj al-Sunna'. So he praised him abundantly, and took from him issues that he approved of, such as the statement of the sequence of events without a beginning. The first to say this was Abu al-Barakat in his 'al-Mu'tabar', and Ibn Taymiyya followed him in it. So rarely do you see any of his books and articles except that there is an explicit mention of this issue. His contemporary, the teacher Imam al-Subki, criticized him in his poem for holding this issue (1). And this Abu al-Barakat did not imitate Aristotle the way Ibn Sina did. So Ibn Taymiyya said in this book: 'Abu al-Barakat and his likes have refuted Aristotle as much as Allah willed.' And the first part of (1) This is what al-Subki said in his poem: 'Allah, glorified be He above what they think of Him... He sees events without a beginning for them in the...' And this is what Shaykh Muhammad al-Yafi'i al-Shafi'i al-Yamani refuted him with: 'And a Creator before a created being exists... And a Subduer before a subdued being exists... And a Merciful before one who is shown mercy... And a Provider before one who is provided for... By His command, every created thing was brought into existence... And the command - woe to you - without doubt, stands by Him... And the Lord of the Throne spoke the revealed Books with speech unlike His... And He did not cease to be a doer or a speaker eternally... When He wills, so be pleased with it... These are events without a beginning from the text, so understand it, O Numan! Wake up.' The publisher.
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage is the introduction by Dr. Nadwi, setting the historical and intellectual context for Ibn Taymiyya's work. The author begins by describing the deep enmity between the scholars of transmitted knowledge (ashab al-naql) and the philosophers (ashab al-aql). Then he narrates the attempt at reconciliation by the Brethren of Purity and the Ismailis, who sought to harmonize philosophy and revelation by reinterpreting religious texts to align with philosophical doctrines. Ibn Sina is presented as the culmination of this trend, having been raised in an Ismaili environment. Next, the author discusses al-Ghazali, who arose to defend Sunni Islam against the Batinis. Al-Ghazali's method, however, was to engage with philosophy using its own tools, mixing the two sciences and ultimately leading to confusion among later theologians who were misled by rhetorical embellishments. Finally, the author introduces Ibn Tayyima as a unique figure: one who was thoroughly grounded in both Islamic sciences and Greek philosophy, yet was able to distinguish truth from falsehood without falling into syncretism. Ibn Taymiyya studied all philosophical schools, not just Aristotle and Ibn Sina, and he refuted them on their own grounds. The passage then discusses Ibn Taymiyya's appreciation for Abu al-Barakat al-Baghdadi's 'al-Mu'tabar', particularly the doctrine of the temporal sequence of events without a first event (a controversial position that denied the temporal origination of the world in a certain sense). Ibn Taymiyya adopted this view, and al-Subki criticized him for it. The introduction concludes by noting that Abu al-Barakat did not blindly imitate Aristotle, and Ibn Taymiyya praised him for refuting Aristotle. This historical background is crucial for understanding Ibn Taymiyya's critical stance toward formal logic and his epistemological project.

Key Takeaway
Al-Ghazali's method, though effective in his time, inadvertently caused confusion among later theologians who could not distinguish the philosophical from the revelatory.

Introduction and Front Matter

Ibn Taymiyya's Comprehensive Critique and His Sources
Introduction presents Ibn Taymiyya as the comprehensive critic and his connection to Abu al-Barakat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain what distinguished Ibn Taymiyya from earlier intellectual critics and identify his admiration for Abu al-Barakat al-Baghdadi.

Core Idea
Ibn Taymiyya studied all philosophies, not just Aristotle, and refuted each on its own grounds.

This lesson introduces Ibn Taymiyya as the unique figure who mastered both Islamic sciences and Greek philosophy, allowing him to critique without syncretism. It also highlights his adoption of Abu al-Barakat's doctrine of temporal sequence without a beginning.

Guided Path
1
List Ibn Taymiyya's qualifications
According to the passage, what made Ibn Taymiyya uniquely qualified to critique the philosophers? Mention his knowledge of Islamic sciences and all philosophical schools.
2
Understand his critical method
What does 'radda hadha bi hadha wa rajjah dhaaka bi dhaak' mean? How did he refute the philosophers?
3
Identify his source of inspiration
Who was Abu al-Barakat al-Baghdadi? What did Ibn Taymiyya admire about him? What controversial doctrine did he adopt from him?
4
Trace the controversy
How did al-Subki respond to Ibn Taymiyya's adoption of the doctrine of hawadith la awwal laha? Why was this doctrine controversial?

مقدمة الدكتور الندوي وبينهما عداوة وشحناء فيحسب علماء المنقول حكماء المعقول ملاحدة وزنادقة وينسب الحكماء إليهم من الجهل بالحقيقة والجحود بما يثبت عند العقل من الحق . فقام ناس زمن الديالمة وأرادوا التوفيق بين الفرقتين والتطبيق بين العلمين، وهم مؤلفو رسائل إخوان الصفاء وأمثالهم . فقالوا ما جاد به الحكماء وما جاء به الأنبياء دين واحد وكلاهما حق فأصَّلوا ما قال الحكماء وأوَّلوا ما جاء به الأنبياء وردُّوه إلى أقوالهم وتعاليمهم، وهم الباطنية والإسماعيلية. وفي آخرهم أبو علي ابن سينا الذي وَلَده الإسماعيلية وتربَّى وترعرع في حُجورهم، كما قال ابن سينا عن نفسه (راجع ترجمته في طبقات «الأطباء» لابن أبي أصيبعة وانظر في هذا الكتاب في صحيفة ١٨٣). ثم جاء الغزالي من فقهاء الشافعية زمن ملوك السَّلاجقة من أهل السنة، والباطنية في جبالهم يحملون على شيوخ أهل السنة بشككهم وخناجرهم وعلى شبيبتهم بشكوكهم ودفاترهم، فتزلزل عالم الإسلام وزلت أقدامُ الأفهام وضلت آراء حملة الأقلام . فقام الغزالي أحسن قيام وتسلّح بسلاحهم وتدرع بدروعهم، واختار حقهم وردَّ باطِلَهم، فمنع ثغور الدين عن غاراتهم وكتب وألف ووضع كتباً ورسائل و مجلدات في توفيق الرأيين، فخلط بين العلمين وآخى بين الحزبين (راجع الكتاب، صفحة ٢٣٨ و ٢٣٩). فنشأ به متكلّمون غَرَّهم زَخْرَفة القول ومموّهات العقول، فتفرقوا فرَقاً واختلقوا أقوالاً وهم يَحْسَبون أنهم يُحسنون صُنْعا (راجع هذا الكتاب، صفحة ١٨٩ - ١٨٣). ثم قدر الله تعالى لهذه الأمة المرحومة من علماء الدين رجلاً نافذ البصيرة غيوراً على الدين عارفاً بكتاب الله وسنة رسوله وعالماً بأقوال الحكماء ومميّزاً بين حقهم وباطلهم وعارفاً بفنون الحكمة كلها وآراء عقلائهم كلهم ولم يقصر علمه على أرسطاليس وشارحه ابن سينا بل نظر في علوم جميع طبقاتهم وعرف أفكار فرقهم وطوائفهم وأساكلهم، فرد هذا بهذا ورَجّح ذاك بذاك . وهو العلامة الإمام الحافظ ابن تيمية صاحب هذا الكتاب. (صفحة ١٧) قد بسطتُ في مقالتي في رد مَنْ قال إن حكماء المسلمين لم يكونوا إلا خَدَمة لأرسطو التي ظهرت في مجلة «الثقافة الإسلامية الصادرة في حيدرآباد الدكن بالإنكليزية، المجلد الأول سنة ١٩٢٧ م . فعدّدت مواضع ذكر فيها ابن تيمية فلاسفة اليونانيين وآراءهم وفند آراء ابن سينا وجَهله وقال فيه : إنه لا يعرف غير أرسطو . وقد أكثر هذا المعنى في كتابه . وترى في هذا الكتاب ما يدل على أن ابن تيمية له ولوع بكتاب «المعتبر» لأبي البركات البغدادي وجمعت فيما كتبتُ في آخر كتاب «المعتبر» الذي طبعته دائرة المعارف العثمانية أقوال الإمام فيه وفي كتابه في هذا الكتاب وكتابه المعبر «ببيان موافقة صريح المعقول الصحيح المنقول»، و«منهاج السنة». فأكثر الثناء عليه، وأخذ منه مسائل استحسنها والقول بتسلسل حوادث لا أول لها فأول من قال بهذا أبو البركات في معتبره»، واتبعه فيه ابن تيمية، فقلَّ من كتبه ومقالاته إلا وفيه تصريح بهذه المسئلة، وقد عابه معاصره الأستاذ الإمام السبكي في قصيدته بقوله بهذه المسئلة (1) . وأبو البركات هذا لم يقلد أرسطو تقليد ابن سينا فقال ابن تيمية في هذا الكتاب : وأبو البركات وأمثاله قد رَدّوا على أرسطو ما شاء الله». والجزء الأول من (۱) هذا ما قال السبكي في قصيدته : الله ، سبحـانـه عمـا يَظُـن بـه يَرَى حوادث لا مبدا لأولهــــا في وهذا ما رده به الشيخ محمد اليافعي الشافعي اليمني : وخالق قبل مخلوق يكونـه وقاهر قبل مقهور یکون به وراحـــم قبـــل مـــرحـــــوم فيــــرحمـــــه ورازق قبل مرزوق بأضربه عن أمره صَدّر المخلوق أجمعه والأمر - ويحك ـ لا شك يقوم به وقد تكلم ربُّ العرش بالكتـب الـ منزلات کلاماً لا شبیه به ولم يزل فاعلاً أو قائلاً أزلاً إذا يشاء، فارض بــــــه هذى حوادث لا مبدا لأولها بالنص فافهمـه یـا نـومـان! فانتبه الناشر
Introduction by Dr. Nadwi: And between them there was enmity and hostility, so the scholars of transmitted knowledge consider the philosophers of intellectual knowledge to be heretics and atheists, and the philosophers attribute to them ignorance of truth and rejection of what is established by reason as truth. Then some people arose in the time of the Daylamites and wanted to reconcile the two groups and harmonize the two sciences, and they are the authors of the Epistles of the Brethren of Purity and their likes. They said: What the philosophers produced and what the prophets brought is one religion, and both are true. So they established what the philosophers said and interpreted what the prophets brought, and reduced it to their own sayings and teachings. They are the Batinis and Ismailis. And the last of them was Abu Ali Ibn Sina, whom the Ismailis fathered and he was raised and grew up in their care, as Ibn Sina said about himself (see his biography in the Generations of Physicians by Ibn Abi Usaybi'a, and see in this book on page 183). Then came al-Ghazali from the Shafi'i jurists in the time of the Saljuq kings from the Sunnis, while the Batinis were in their mountains attacking the Sunni elders with their doubts and daggers, and their youth with their doubts and notebooks. So the world of Islam was shaken, the feet of understandings slipped, and the opinions of those who carried pens went astray. So al-Ghazali arose in the best manner, armed himself with their weapons, donned their armor, chose their truth, and refuted their falsehood. He defended the frontiers of the religion against their raids, and wrote, authored, and composed books, treatises, and volumes in reconciling the two views. So he mixed the two sciences and fraternized between the two parties (see the book, pages 238 and 239). There arose from him theologians whom the ornamentation of speech and the deceptions of the intellects deluded, so they split into groups and invented sayings, thinking that they were doing well (see this book, pages 183-189). Then Allah Almighty destined for this mercy-covered nation a man from the religious scholars, penetrating in insight, jealous for the religion, knowledgeable of Allah's Book and the Sunna of His Messenger, knowledgeable of the sayings of the philosophers and discerning between their truth and falsehood, knowledgeable of all the arts of philosophy and all the opinions of their rationalists, and he did not limit his knowledge to Aristotle and his commentator Ibn Sina, but rather looked into the sciences of all their classes and knew the ideas of their groups, sects, and schools. He refuted one with another and weighed one against another. He is the great scholar, the Imam, the Hafiz, Ibn Taymiyya, the author of this book. (Page 17) I have elaborated in my article refuting those who said that the Muslim philosophers were only servants of Aristotle, which appeared in the magazine 'Islamic Culture' published in Hyderabad Deccan in English, Volume 1, 1927 CE. I listed the places where Ibn Taymiyya mentioned the Greek philosophers and their opinions, and he criticized Ibn Sina's opinions and his ignorance, and said of him: He knows nothing besides Aristotle. And he repeated this meaning in his book. And you see in this book what indicates that Ibn Taymiyya was fond of the book 'al-Mu'tabar' by Abu al-Barakat al-Baghdadi, and I collected in what I wrote at the end of the book 'al-Mu'tabar' (published by the Ottoman Knowledge Circle) the Imam's statements about him and in his book in this book and his book 'Bayān Muwāfaqat Ṣarīḥ al-Maʿqūl al-Ṣaḥīḥ al-Manqūl' and 'Minhāj al-Sunna'. So he praised him abundantly, and took from him issues that he approved of, such as the statement of the sequence of events without a beginning. The first to say this was Abu al-Barakat in his 'al-Mu'tabar', and Ibn Taymiyya followed him in it. So rarely do you see any of his books and articles except that there is an explicit mention of this issue. His contemporary, the teacher Imam al-Subki, criticized him in his poem for holding this issue (1). And this Abu al-Barakat did not imitate Aristotle the way Ibn Sina did. So Ibn Taymiyya said in this book: 'Abu al-Barakat and his likes have refuted Aristotle as much as Allah willed.' Commentary
This passage is the introduction by Dr. Nadwi, setting the historical and intellectual context for Ibn Taymiyya's work. The author begins by describing the deep enmity between the scholars of transmitted knowledge (ashab al-naql) and the philosophers (ashab al-aql). Then he narrates the attempt at reconciliation by the Brethren of Purity and the Ismailis, who sought to harmonize philosophy and revelation by reinterpreting religious texts to align with philosophical doctrines. Ibn Sina is presented as the culmination of this trend, having been raised in an Ismaili environment. Next, the author discusses al-Ghazali, who arose to defend Sunni Islam against the Batinis. Al-Ghazali's method, however, was to engage with philosophy using its own tools, mixing the two sciences and ultimately leading to confusion among later theologians who were misled by rhetorical embellishments. Finally, the author introduces Ibn Tayyima as a unique figure: one who was thoroughly grounded in both Islamic sciences and Greek philosophy, yet was able to distinguish truth from falsehood without falling into syncretism. Ibn Taymiyya studied all philosophical schools, not just Aristotle and Ibn Sina, and he refuted them on their own grounds. The passage then discusses Ibn Taymiyya's appreciation for Abu al-Barakat al-Baghdadi's 'al-Mu'tabar', particularly the doctrine of the temporal sequence of events without a first event (a controversial position that denied the temporal origination of the world in a certain sense). Ibn Taymiyya adopted this view, and al-Subki criticized him for it. The introduction concludes by noting that Abu al-Barakat did not blindly imitate Aristotle, and Ibn Taymiyya praised him for refuting Aristotle. This historical background is crucial for understanding Ibn Taymiyya's critical stance toward formal logic and his epistemological project.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner

Ibn Taymiyya's Independence from Greek Philosophy
Author states Ibn Taymiyya wrote an article refuting the notion that Muslim philosophers were mere servants of Aristotle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify Ibn Taymiyya's critical stance toward Greek philosophical authority and explain how his rejection of Aristotelian servitude shaped his critique of logic.

Core Idea
Ibn Taymiyya was no servant of Aristotle; he critiqued Greek philosophy from within the Islamic tradition.

This lesson introduces the historical context of Ibn Taymiyya's critique of Aristotelian logic. Dr. al-Nadwi's article refutes the orientalist claim that Muslim philosophers merely repeated Aristotle. Instead, Ibn Taymiyya actively challenged Greek authorities, including Ibn Sina, whom he accused of knowing nothing besides Aristotle. Understanding this independence is crucial before engaging with Ibn Taymiyya's logical refutations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the orientalist claim being refuted
Notice that Dr. al-Nadwi directly opposes the idea that Muslim philosophers were 'nothing but servants of Aristotle.' This is the target of his article.
2
Locate Ibn Taymiyya's targets
The passage mentions Ibn Taymiyya's criticism of Greek philosophers generally and Ibn Sina specifically. He accuses Ibn Sina of ignorance and of knowing only Aristotle.
3
Understand the methodological implication
Ibn Taymiyya's rejection of Aristotelian authority implies that his critique of logic is not a sectarian attack but an independent epistemological stance rooted in Islamic sources.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قد بسطتُ في مقالتي في رد مَنْ قال إن حكماء المسلمين لم يكونوا إلا خَدَمة لأرسطو التي ظهرت في مجلة «الثقافة الإسلامية الصادرة في حيدرآباد الدكن بالإنكليزية، المجلد الأول سنة ۱۹۲۷ م . فعدّدت مواضع ذكر فيها ابن تيمية فلاسفة اليونانيين وآراءهم وفند آراء ابن سينا وجَهله وقال فيه : إنه لا يعرف غير أرسطو . وقد أكثر هذا المعنى في كتابه .
I have detailed in my article on refuting those who said that the Muslim philosophers were nothing but servants of Aristotle, which appeared in the journal 'Islamic Culture' published in Hyderabad Deccan in English, volume one, year 1927. I enumerated places in which Ibn Taymiyya mentioned the Greek philosophers and their views, and criticized the views of Ibn Sina and his ignorance, and said about him: 'He knows nothing other than Aristotle.' And he repeated this meaning in his book.

Commentary
This passage is an introductory statement by Dr. al-Nadwi explaining his earlier work. He says he wrote an article refuting the claim that Muslim philosophers were mere servants of Aristotle. In that article, he listed instances where Ibn Taymiyya criticized Greek philosophers and particularly Ibn Sina, calling him ignorant and claiming he knew only Aristotle. This sets the stage for the radical critique of Aristotelian logic found in Ibn Taymiyya's book. The passage establishes Ibn Taymiyya's independence from the Greek tradition, contrary to the common orientalist narrative.

D) Ibn Sina was a faithful Muslim philosopher.

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya's critique of Greek logic is rooted in his independence from Aristotelian authority, a fact often overlooked by those who view him as merely a polemicist.

Introduction and Front Matter

Ibn Taymiyya's Debt to Abu al-Barakat
Author discusses Ibn Taymiyya's fondness for al-Mu'tabar and his adoption of the theory of an eternal series of events.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key intellectual influence of Abu al-Barakat al-Baghdadi on Ibn Taymiyya and state his significance in the critique of Aristotelian logic.

Core Idea
Ibn Taymiyya's criticism of logic is indebted to Abu al-Barakat, who opened the door to its refutation.

This lesson explores Ibn Taymiyya's intellectual relationship with Abu al-Barakat al-Baghdadi, an earlier philosopher who criticized Aristotle. You will see how Ibn Taymiyya admired al-Mu'tabar, adopted key ideas, and expanded upon them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main thinkers
Recognize Ibn Taymiyya and Abu al-Barakat al-Baghdadi as the central figures in this passage. Note the context: Ibn Taymiyya quotes al-Mu'tabar extensively.
Abu al-Barakat lived in the 12th century, Ibn Taymiyya in the 13th-14th.
2
Note Ibn Taymiyya's praise for al-Mu'tabar
Ibn Taymiyya praised Abu al-Barakat's book greatly and took many issues from it. This shows intellectual continuity.
3
Recognize the adopted theory
Ibn Taymiyya adopted the theory of an eternal series of events (tasalsul al-hawadith) from Abu al-Barakat. The passage says 'The first to say this was Abu al-Barakat, and Ibn Taymiyya followed him.'
This concept is controversial; note al-Subki's criticism.
4
Understand Abu al-Barakat's independence from Aristotle
Abu al-Barakat did not imitate Aristotle like Ibn Sina did. Ibn Taymiyya praises him as a refuter of Aristotle.
This sets the stage for the critique of Greek logic.
5
See Ibn Taymiyya's expansion
Ibn Taymiyya followed Abu al-Barakat's path but added his own fiery intellect and critical nature, producing an expanded critique.
Ibn Taymiyya's work 'Bayan Muwafaqat Sarih al-Ma'qul' and 'Minhaj al-Sunna' continue this tradition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وترى في هذا الكتاب ما يدل على أن ابن تيمية له ولوع بكتاب «المعتبر» لأبي البركات البغدادي وجمعت فيما كتبتُ في آخر كتاب «المعتبر» الذي طبعته دائرة المعارف العثمانية أقوال الإمام فيه وفي كتابه في هذا الكتاب وكتابه المعبر «ببيان موافقة صريح المعقول الصحيح المنقول»، و«منهاج السنة». فأكثر الثناء عليه، وأخذ منه مسائل استحسنها والقول بتسلسل حوادث لا أول لها فأول من قال بهذا أبو البركات في معتبره»، واتبعه فيه ابن تيمية، فقلَّ من كتبه ومقالاته إلا وفيه تصريح بهذه المسئلة، وقد عابه معاصره الأستاذ الإمام السبكي في قصيدته بقوله بهذه المسئلة. وأبو البركات هذا لم يقلد أرسطو تقليد ابن سينا فقال ابن تيمية في هذا الكتاب : وأبو البركات وأمثاله قد رَدّوا على أرسطو ما شاء الله». والجزء الأول من كتاب «المعتبر» يشتمل على المنطق. وأبو البركات هذا هو الذي فتح الباب للنقد على منطق أرسطو . واتبعه ابن تيمية في هذا الكتاب وزاد عليه ما جادت به قريحته الوقادة وطبيعته النقادة، وقلمه السيَّال وعقله الفعال.
And you see in this book what indicates that Ibn Taymiyya had a fondness for the book 'al-Mu'tabar' of Abu al-Barakat al-Baghdadi. And I have collected in what I wrote at the end of the book 'al-Mu'tabar,' which was printed by the Ottoman Encyclopedia, the sayings of the Imam (Ibn Taymiyya) about him and about his book in this book and his book 'Bayan Muwafaqat Sarih al-Ma‘qul al-Sahih al-Manqul' and 'Minhaj al-Sunna.' So he praised him greatly and took from him issues he approved, including the statement about the series of events without a beginning. The first to say this was Abu al-Barakat in his 'al-Mu'tabar,' and Ibn Taymiyya followed him in it. Seldom is there any of his books or articles without explicit mention of this issue. And his contemporary, the master imam al-Subki, criticized him in his poem for holding this issue. And this Abu al-Barakat did not imitate Aristotle as Ibn Sina did. So Ibn Taymiyya said in this book: 'Abu al-Barakat and his likes refuted Aristotle mightily.' And the first part of the book 'al-Mu'tabar' includes logic. And this Abu al-Barakat is the one who opened the door to criticism of Aristotle's logic. And Ibn Taymiyya followed him in this book and added to it what his fiery intellect, critical nature, flowing pen, and active mind produced.
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage explains Ibn Taymiyya's intellectual relationship with Abu al-Barakat al-Baghdadi. Dr. al-Nadwi states that Ibn Taymiyya greatly admired al-Mu'tabar and quoted it extensively. A key idea Ibn Taymiyya adopted from Abu al-Barakat is the concept of an eternal series of events (tasalsul al-hawadith) without a first beginning. This was controversial; al-Subki criticized Ibn Taymiyya for it in a poem. The passage highlights that Abu al-Barakat was an independent thinker who did not blindly follow Aristotle, unlike Ibn Sina. Ibn Taymiyya praised him as a refuter of Aristotle. The first part of al-Mu'tabar deals with logic, and Abu al-Barakat is credited with initiating criticism of Aristotelian logic, which Ibn Taymiyya continued and expanded with his own contributions.

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya's approach to logic was shaped by Abu al-Barakat, who initiated a critical tradition that Ibn Taymiyya expanded.

The Eternal Series of Events Controversy
Author discusses Ibn Taymiyya's fondness for al-Mu'tabar and his adoption of the theory of an eternal series of events.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the concept of an eternal series of events (tasalsul al-hawadith) and identify why it was controversial among medieval Islamic scholars.

Core Idea
The idea of an infinite past of events without a first beginning was defended by Ibn Taymiyya and criticized by al-Subki.

This lesson focuses on a specific theological-philosophical concept that Ibn Taymiyya adopted: the eternal series of events. You will see what it means, who first proposed it, and why it provoked strong opposition from contemporaries like al-Subki.

Guided Path
1
Understand the term 'tasalsul al-hawadith'
Literally 'chain of events without a first'. It means an infinite temporal sequence of events with no initial beginning. Consider the theological implications: if the universe has an infinite past, does it conflict with the idea of creation ex nihilo?
This concept is distinct from the eternity of the world; it allows for events that are temporally infinite.
2
Identify the originator in Islam
The passage states that Abu al-Barakat al-Baghdadi was the first Muslim thinker to explicitly state this view in his book al-Mu'tabar.
3
Note Ibn Taymiyya's adoption
Ibn Taymiyya enthusiastically adopted this theory and mentioned it in nearly all his books and articles. This shows the central importance he placed on it.
Ibn Taymiyya's works like 'Bayan Muwafaqat' and 'Minhaj al-Sunna' contain clear statements.
4
Recognize the criticism from al-Subki
Al-Subki, a contemporary and major Shafi'i scholar, criticized Ibn Taymiyya specifically for this view, even composing a poem against it.
This highlights the controversial nature of the concept within mainstream Ash'arism.
5
Reflect on the theological stakes
If events have no beginning, then what does that mean for God's attribute of pre-eternity? Does it imply an eternal creation? Mainstream kalām held that the world is temporally originated, so an infinite past was problematic.
This debate touches on the nature of divine power and free will.

Source Text

Tracing Manuscript Lineage: The Journey of Radd Mantiqiyyin
Author describes the original manuscript and its journey from Yemen to Hyderabad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to trace the provenance of an Islamic manuscript and assess its reliability based on its chain of custody.

Core Idea
A manuscript's chain of custody is as crucial as its content for establishing its authority.

This passage from Dr. al-Nadwi provides a rare glimpse into the journey of the original manuscript of Ibn Taymiyya's 'Radd Mantiqiyyin'. Understanding how scholars track manuscript pedigrees is essential for verifying textual authenticity in Islamic scholarship, especially in hadith and fiqh where a single copy can be the source of entire traditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the origin and key markers
Note that the original copy is Yemeni and bears the handwriting of Zaydi imams. This tells you the geographic and sectarian milieu of the manuscript.
Handwriting analysis is a primary tool in manuscript studies.
2
Trace the chain of transmission
The manuscript moved from Yemen to India through the collection of King Siddiq Hasan Khan of Bhopal. After his death, his books were scattered, and this copy was sold to the Asifiya Library via a bookseller.
Each transfer represents a link in the chain of custody.
3
Evaluate the evidence of ownership
The author asserts that Siddiq Hasan Khan owned the manuscript because he quoted from it in his own works. This is a typical method to verify provenance: cross-referencing citations.
Ownership can be inferred from quotations, marginal notes, or library stamps.
4
Assess the reliability of the manuscript
With a known chain from Yemen to Hyderabad, and the presence of Zaydi imams' handwriting, the manuscript is considered a reliable source. Multiple independent copies (Indian copies) trace back to this 'mother copy'.
A well-documented provenance strengthens the manuscript's authority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونسخة هذا الكتاب الأصلية التي هي أم النسخ الهندية كلها : يمانية، عليها خط بعض أئمة الزيدية . والذي علق بذهني في شأن هذه النسخة أنها نُقلت في ضمن الكتب التي جَلَبها الملك الإمام النواب صديق حَسَن خان ملك بوفال من اليمن . وتبعثرت كتبه بعد وفاته، فانتقل هذا الكتاب بيد الكتبي أحمد المكي إلى المكتبة الآصفية بحيدرآباد الدكن والذي يدل على أن هذا الكتاب كان عند النواب الإمام ذكره في كتبه واقتباس عباراته في مصنفاته .
And the original copy of this book, which is the mother of all Indian copies, is Yemeni, with the handwriting of some Zaydi imams on it. And what I recall regarding this copy is that it was transferred among the books brought by the king Imam Nawab Siddiq Hasan Khan, the king of Bhopal, from Yemen. And his books were scattered after his death, so this book came by the hand of the bookseller Ahmad al-Makki to the Asifiya Library in Hyderabad Deccan. And what indicates that this book was with the Nawab Imam is his mentioning it in his books and quoting its phrases in his works.
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage provides bibliographic information about the manuscript. Dr. al-Nadwi states that the original copy, the source of all Indian copies, is from Yemen, containing handwriting of Zaydi scholars. He speculates that it came with the collection of Siddiq Hasan Khan of Bhopal from Yemen. After his death, a bookseller named Ahmad al-Makki brought it to the Asifiya Library in Hyderabad. The fact that Siddiq Hasan Khan quoted from the book confirms it was in his possession. This establishes the provenance and reliability of the manuscript.

يمانية
السيد صديق حسن خان

Key Takeaway
The reliability of a manuscript depends not only on its age but on the clarity of its chain of custody from author to present day.

Ibn Taymiyya's Critical Approach to Aristotelian Logic
Introduction to Ibn Taymiyya's critical approach to logic.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key elements of Ibn Taymiyya's critique of Aristotelian logic and explain its significance in the Islamic intellectual tradition.

Core Idea
Ibn Taymiyya anticipated modern critiques of Aristotelian logic and prioritized induction.

This passage from Dr. al-Nadwi's edition sets the stage for Ibn Taymiyya's groundbreaking critique. It highlights how Ibn Taymiyya, following Abu al-Barakat, challenged the Aristotelian monopoly on logic and offered insights that resonate with later Western philosophers like Mill and Hume. Understanding this critique is essential for appreciating the Islamic intellectual tradition's independence from Greek thought.

Guided Path
1
Identify the historical figures
Note the roles of Abu al-Barakat, Ibn Taymiyya, Mill, and Hume. Abu al-Barakat opened the door to criticism; Ibn Taymiyya expanded it. Mill refined induction; Hume addressed causality.
2
Extract the core critique
The passage states that Muslim logicians followed Aristotle in making universals the foundation and prioritizing demonstrative arguments over induction. Ibn Taymiyya's critique targets this hierarchy.
3
Identify parallels with Western philosophy
The editor claims Ibn Taymiyya's views on cause and concomitance match Hume's, and his emphasis on induction aligns with Mill's work. This shows the timeliness of his critique.
4
Recognize the significance for Islamic sciences
Ibn Taymiyya's critique allows for an epistemology that integrates revelation and induction, crucial for fields like kalam and usul al-fiqh, where causality and definition are central.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب «المعتبر» يشتمل على المنطق. وأبو البركات هذا هو الذي فتح الباب للنقد على منطق أرسطو . واتبعه ابن تيمية في هذا الكتاب وزاد عليه ما جادت به قريحته الوقادة وطبيعته النقادة، وقلمه السيَّال وعقله الفعال. وإذا أنعمت النظر في هذا الكتاب تجد مسائل منطقية وفلسفية ابن تيمية أبو عُذرتها، وهي تطابق كل المطابقة بما قال فلاسفة الأفرنج في هذا العصر في بعض مسائل المنطق والفلسفة . فَمناطقة المسلمين كلهم اتبعوا أرسطو في جعل الكليات أصل العلم وترجيح ما سموه برهانيات وحط الشأن من الاستقراء، حتى قال العلماء الأفرنج : إن مِلْ (Mill) المنطقي الإنكليزي هو الذي هذَب الاستقراء ووضع المنطق . فمما يجب عليّ في هذه الوجيزة الإلماعُ به هو ما قال المصنف في حقيقة الحدّ والجنس والفصل واللزوم، وحقيقـة العلـة والقياس والاستقراء، والاستدلال بالمشهورات والاكتفاء بمقدمة واحدة في القياس وغيره من المباحث العويصة التي حل المصنف مُشكلها ببيان واضح ودليل راهن وما قال في العلة واللزوم هو عين ما (Hume) الفلسفي في كتبه ومسئلة اللزوم والعِلّية من المسائل العويصة التي ضلّت في واديها الأفهام ونبعت من عيونها ضلالات الطبائعيين من أهل الإلحاد. وكم لهذا النابغة في الكتاب من نوادر لم يسبقه إليها أحد، رضى الله عنه
The book 'al-Mu'tabar' contains logic. This Abu al-Barakat is the one who opened the door to criticism of Aristotle's logic. Ibn Taymiyya followed him in this book and added to it what his blazing intellect, critical nature, fluent pen, and active mind produced. If you contemplate this book, you will find logical and philosophical issues that Ibn Taymiyya is the father of their justification, and they perfectly match what Western philosophers said in this age regarding some issues of logic and philosophy. For all Muslim logicians followed Aristotle in making universals the foundation of knowledge and preferring what they called demonstrative arguments and disparaging induction, until Western scholars said that Mill, the English logician, is the one who refined induction and established logic. So what I must allude to in this brief is what the author said concerning the reality of definition, genus, differentia, concomitance, the reality of cause, syllogism, induction, reasoning with accepted premises, and sufficiency of one premise in a syllogism, and other difficult investigations that the author solved with clear explanation and conclusive proof. And what he said about cause and concomitance is exactly what the philosopher Hume said in his books. The problem of concomitance and causality is among the difficult issues in whose valley minds strayed and from whose springs flowed the misguidance of naturalists among the atheists. How many rarities does this genius have in the book, which no one preceded him in, may God be pleased with him.
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage is a prefatory critique by the editor, Dr. al-Nadwi, setting the stage for Ibn Taymiyya's work. It first identifies Abu al-Barakat as the pioneer who opened the door to criticism of Aristotelian logic, and notes that Ibn Taymiyya followed and expanded upon him. The author emphasizes that the book contains logical and philosophical discussions that align with modern Western thought, particularly the critique of prioritizing universals and demonstrative arguments over induction. He references John Stuart Mill's work on induction as parallel to Ibn Taymiyya's insights. The passage then lists key topics that the author of 'al-Mu'tabar' addressed: the nature of definition (hadd), genus (jins), differentia (fasl), concomitance (luzum), cause ('illa), syllogism (qiyas), induction (istiqra'), reasoning with accepted premises (mashhurat), and the sufficiency of a single premise in a syllogism. The editor highlights that Ibn Taymiyya's treatment of cause and concomitance anticipates David Hume's philosophy, and that misunderstandings of causality have led to atheistic naturalism. The passage concludes by praising Ibn Taymiyya's original contributions.

Key Terms
الحدّ
الجنس
الفصل
اللزوم
العلة
القياس
الاستقراء
المشهورات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Aristotle
B) David Hume
C) John Stuart Mill
D) Immanuel Kant

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya's critique of Aristotelian logic underscores the need for an epistemology rooted in revelation and empirical induction, not just Greek deduction.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

The Journey of Ibn Taymiyya's Manuscript: From Dictation to Print
Editor recounts the preservation history and publication efforts of the manuscript.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to trace the key stages in the preservation and publication of Ibn Taymiyya's Radd Mantiqiyyin.

Core Idea
A manuscript's survival depends on generations of dedicated scholars.

This passage from the editor's introduction reveals the remarkable efforts of multiple scholars over two decades to bring Ibn Taymiyya's critique of Greek logic to print. Understanding this history shows how Islamic intellectual heritage is preserved through collective scholarly labor.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first scholar to discover the manuscript
Find who first noticed the book in India. Shibli Nu'mani is mentioned.
He wrote articles based on it.
2
Describe the original manuscript's condition
Note that the Asafiyya copy was Ibn Taymiyya's dictation, with corrections in margins, but it was unordered with no divisions.
Only a critical scholar could navigate it.
3
Trace the editing efforts
List the subsequent scholars: al-Farahi organized it but left incomplete, Abu al-Jalal completed the copy, then Abd al-Samad printed it.
Each added something but errors remained.
4
Assess the final outcome
Although not perfect, the printed edition made the text accessible for future scholars.
The editor hopes to improve it later.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مقدمة الدكتور الندوي
وأول من تنبه لهذا الكتاب في هذه الديار حضرة الأستاذ المؤرخ الإمام شبلي النعماني. فتجد في رسائله المعروفة بـ«مكاتيب شبلي إلماماً بهذا الكتاب وأمره باستنساخه ووجود نسخة منه عنده وهي الآن في كتبخانة ندوة العلماء بلكناؤ ضمن كتبه الموقوفة عليها. وللأستاذ مقالات في خطأ منطق اليونانيين نشرت بمجلة «الندوة» سنة ١٩٠٤ وهي مقتبسة من نفس هذا الكتاب .
وأخذت نُسخ أخرى من هذه النسخة الآصفية استنسخها في الهند بعض المولعين بالكتب النادرة مثل الطبيب نور الدين القادياني، والشيخ بير صاحب جهندا بالسند . والنسخة الأصفية عندي هي النسخة الأصلية التي أملاها الشيخ الإمام ابن تيمية، ودون ما أملاه الشيخ صاحبه محمد بن أحمد بن حسن الشافعي. فتجد خطها خطاً عربياً، وفيها حذف وزيادة وقطع وإصلاح بعضه على الهوامش وبعضه بين السطور، وذلك لا يصح إلا للمؤلف نفسه. وفي آخر النسخة بلغت مقابلة بأصل المصنف بخطه المقروء عليه في سنة ثمان وعشرين وسبع مئة وقد قرأتُ عليه أوائل هذه النسخة وكتب بخطه على هوامشها زيادات» .
والنسخة غير مرتبة بلا تقسيم على الأبواب والفصول، وقطع وزيادة لا يتنبه لها إلا العالم الناقد البصير. فلما عُيّن الأستاذ الشيخ عبد الحميد الفَرَاهي صاحب نظام القرآن) أستاذاً بدار العلوم بحيدر آباد ،الدكن، أخذ النسخة واستنسخ نصفها بيده بقلم الرصاص، ووَضَع كل فقرة بموضعها من الكتاب، وبوّب وفصل وكتب العناوين على الهامش. ثم خرج من حيدر آباد ولم يتم الكتاب. وناولني نسخته هذه لأقوم بما لم يتم . فقلّدت هذا العمل أحد أصحابي أبا الجلال الندوي بدار المصنفين. فأخذ بإتمامه ونقل الناقص نسخة ندوة العلماء المذكورة. فكملت النسخة ولم يتم العمل .
الكتبي
مقدمة الدكتور الندوي
ثم قدّر الله تعالى لهذا العمل الجليل صديقي الفاضل عبد الصمد بن شرف الدين أن يقوم بما لم تقم به الدوائر والإدارات. فاشترى النسخة واستخدم مصحّحَيْنِ من مصححي الدائرة أن يهتما بالنقل والتصحيح والمقابلة، ولكنهما كما نبأني الصديق الفاضل لم يهتما بالأمر أحسنَ اهتمام فأخذَتْه الغَيرة على العلم فاعتنى به أحسنَ اعتناء، وقام بطبعه في مطبعته القيّمة، وأصلح وصحح وكتب تعليقات وملحقات، ولكن لم يَسُدَّ الخلل والخطأ كما أراد وينبغي ولكنه جَعَل الكتاب بحيث يستفيد منه المستفيدون ويخدمه العلماء الناقدون في المستقبل. فشكر الله تعالى جميله وجزاه أحسن الجزاء. كتبتُ هذه العُجالة وأنا على وشك الرحيل غداً وممتط ظهر الباخرة إلى الحجاز، فازجي إلى القراء ما تيسر لي في سويعات. فإن أتاح الله تعالى بعد عودتي من السفر عودتي إلى هذا الموضوع أوفٌ حقه إن شاء الله تعالى. والسلام خير ختام .
بمباي
غرة ذي قعدة سنة ١٣٦٨ هـ
٢٦ من أغسطس سنة ١٩٤٩
م
أنا المستعين بحبل الله القوي
سليمان الندوي
القاضي بالمحكمة الشرعية ببوفال
Introduction by Dr. al-Nadwi
The first to notice this book in this region was His Excellency the historian Imam Shibli Nu'mani. You find in his famous letters called 'Makatib Shibli' familiarity with this book and his order to copy it, and he had a copy of it, which is now in the library of Nadwat al-Ulama in Lucknow among his endowed books. The professor also had articles on the error of Greek logic published in the magazine 'al-Nadwa' in 1904, which are derived from this same book.
Other copies were taken from this Asafiyya copy, copied in India by some lovers of rare books, such as the doctor Nur al-Din al-Qadiyani, and Shaykh Pir Sahib Jhandah in Sindh. The Asafiyya copy in my possession is the original copy that Shaykh Imam Ibn Taymiyya dictated, and what he dictated was recorded by his companion Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Hasan al-Shafi'i. You find its script is Arabic, and it contains deletions, additions, cuts, and corrections, some in the margins and some between the lines, which is only valid from the author himself. At the end of the copy it says: 'Collated with the original manuscript in the author's handwriting read to him in the year 728 AH, and I read before him the beginnings of this copy and he wrote additions on its margins.'
The copy is not arranged, with no division into sections and chapters; its cuts and additions are not noticed except by a critical, perceptive scholar. When the professor Shaykh Abd al-Hamid al-Farahi, author of 'Nizam al-Quran', was appointed as a teacher at Dar al-Ulum in Hyderabad, Deccan, he took the copy and copied half of it by hand in pencil, and placed each paragraph in its proper location in the book, and sectioned and divided and wrote headings in the margin. Then he left Hyderabad without completing the book. He gave me his copy to complete what was not done. So I entrusted this work to one of my companions, Abu al-Jalal al-Nadwi, at Dar al-Musannifin. He undertook to complete it and transferred the missing parts from the aforementioned copy of Nadwat al-Ulama. Thus the copy was completed but the work was not finished.
Then Allah Almighty destined for this great work my virtuous friend Abd al-Samad ibn Sharaf al-Din to accomplish what the circles and departments could not. He bought the copy and employed two correctors from the correctors of the Da'ira (circle) to attend to copying, correction, and collation, but they, as my virtuous friend informed me, did not attend to the matter with the utmost care, so scholarly zeal took hold of him and he attended to it with the best attention, and he printed it in his valuable printing press, and he corrected, emended, and wrote commentaries and appendices, but error and mistake were not eliminated as he wished and as is proper, but he made the book such that seekers benefit from it and critical scholars serve it in the future. May Allah reward his kindness and recompense him with the best recompense. I wrote this brief note while on the verge of departure tomorrow, riding the back of the ship to Hejaz, so I offer to the readers what was possible for me in a few hours. If Allah grants after my return from travel my return to this subject, I will give it its due, if Allah wills. Peace is the best conclusion.
Bombay
1st of Dhu al-Qa'dah 1368 AH
26 August 1949 CE
I am the one seeking aid from the strong rope of Allah
Sulayman al-Nadwi
Judge at the Sharia Court in Bhopal
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage is the editor's introduction to the book 'Radd Mantiqiyyin' (Refutation of the Logicians) by Ibn Taymiyya. The editor, Dr. Sulayman al-Nadwi, recounts the history of the manuscript and the efforts of various scholars to preserve and publish it. He begins by mentioning that the first person to notice the book in India was the historian Imam Shibli Nu'mani, who had a copy made and used it in his own articles against Greek logic. The editor notes that other copies were taken from the Asafiyya copy by rare book enthusiasts like Nur al-Din al-Qadiyani. He then describes the Asafiyya copy as the original dictated by Ibn Taymiyya himself, written in Arabic with corrections in the margins, indicating it was directly authorized by the author. The manuscript was unordered, lacking clear divisions. The next scholar to work on it was Shaykh Abd al-Hamid al-Farahi, who organized it into sections but left it incomplete. The editor then entrusted the work to Abu al-Jalal al-Nadwi, who finished the copy but did not complete the full editing. Finally, a friend named Abd al-Samad ibn Sharaf al-Din took charge, bought the manuscript, employed correctors, and printed it with his own funds, adding corrections and appendices, though some errors remained. The editor wrote this introduction while traveling to Hejaz, hoping to later produce a more complete edition. The passage concludes with the editor's signature and date.

Key Terms
رَدّ المَنْطِقِيِّين
تَحْقِيق
مَخْطُوط

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The publication of Ibn Taymiyya's Radd Mantiqiyyin was a multi-generational effort involving discovery, organization, and printing by several scholars.

Introduction and Front Matter

Scholarly Zeal in Preserving Islamic Texts
Editor thanks his friend for acquiring and proofreading the manuscript.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the role of a muhaqqiq (critical editor) and the importance of scholarly zeal (ghayra) in preserving Islamic texts.

Core Idea
A single scholar's zeal can rescue a critical manuscript where institutions fail.

This passage from the editor's introduction to Ibn Taymiyya's 'Radd al-Mantiqiyyin' reveals the behind-the-scenes efforts that bring a classical work to publication. It introduces us to the concept of 'ghayra ʿalā al-ʿilm' — a passionate zeal for knowledge that drives scholars to correct and preserve texts. Understanding this context helps us appreciate the chain of transmission and the human effort behind every Islamic scholarly work.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key actors
The editor mentions his friend Abdul Samad bin Sharaf al-Din, the proofreaders he employed, and himself (the editor). Notice how each person contributes to the project.
The friend is the patron/publisher, the proofreaders are initial workers, and the editor writes this note.
2
Extract the problem
The proofreaders did not attend to the task with 'the best attention'. This is the central difficulty: hired professionals failed to meet the required standard.
The text says 'lam yah_tammā bi al-amr aḥsana ihtimām'.
3
Recognize the solution: ghayra
The friend's 'zeal for knowledge' (al-ghayratu ʿalā al-ʿilm) motivated him to personally take over the correction, printing, and addition of commentary.
This concept is key — it is not just hard work, but a religious and intellectual drive to safeguard truth.
4
Note the outcome and limitations
The effort improved the book, but errors remain. The friend 'made the book such that those who benefit may benefit and critical scholars may serve it in the future'.
This humility reflects the reality of textual scholarship: it is a cumulative process.
5
Reflect on the editor's context
The editor writes this hastily on the eve of his Hajj journey, showing how scholars balance multiple duties. He prays to return to the topic later.
This adds a personal dimension and shows the urgency and sincerity of the work.

Source Text

ثم قدّر الله تعالى لهذا العمل الجليل صديقي الفاضل عبد الصمد بن شرف الدين أن يقوم بما لم تقم به الدوائر والإدارات. فاشترى النسخة واستخدم مصحّحَيْنِ من مصححي الدائرة أن يهتما بالنقل والتصحيح والمقابلة، ولكنهما كما نبأني الصديق الفاضل لم يهتما بالأمر أحسنَ اهتمام فأخذَتْه الغَيرة على العلم فاعتنى به أحسنَ اعتناء، وقام بطبعه في مطبعته القيّمة، وأصلح وصحح وكتب تعليقات وملحقات، ولكن لم يَسُدَّ الخلل والخطأ كما أراد وينبغي ولكنه جَعَل الكتاب بحيث يستفيد منه المستفيدون ويخدمه العلماء الناقدون في المستقبل. فشكر الله تعالى جميله وجزاه أحسن الجزاء. كتبتُ هذه العُجالة وأنا على وشك الرحيل غداً وممتط ظهر الباخرة إلى الحجاز، فازجي إلى القراء ما تيسر لي في سويعات. فإن أتاح الله تعالى بعد عودتي من السفر عودتي إلى هذا الموضوع أوفٌ حقه إن شاء الله تعالى. والسلام خير ختام . بمباي غرة ذي قعدة سنة ١٣٦٨ هـ ٢٦ من أغسطس سنة ١٩٤٩ م أنا المستعين بحبل الله القوي سليمان الندوي القاضي بالمحكمة الشرعية ببوفال
Then Allah decreed for this noble work that my virtuous friend Abdul Samad bin Sharaf al-Din would undertake what the circles and departments had not done. He bought the copy and employed two proofreaders from among the proofreaders of the circle to attend to transcription, correction, and comparison. But as my virtuous friend informed me, they did not attend to the matter with the best attention, so zeal for knowledge seized him and he attended to it with the best care, and undertook its printing in his valuable press, and corrected and wrote comments and appendices. But the error and mistake did not cease as he wished and as it ought to be, but he made the book such that those who benefit may benefit from it and critical scholars may serve it in the future. May Allah reward his kindness and recompense him with the best recompense. I wrote this hasty note while I am on the verge of departure tomorrow, boarding the ship to the Hijaz, presenting to the readers what was easy for me in a few hours. If Allah grants me after my return from travel a return to this topic, I will give it its due, Allah willing. And peace is the best conclusion. Bombay, 1 Dhu al-Qa'dah 1368 AH, 26 August 1949 CE. I am the one seeking aid through the strong rope of Allah, Sulayman al-Nadwi, judge in the Sharia court of Bhopal.
Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This passage is from the editor's introduction to Ibn Taymiyya's 'Radd al-Mantiqiyyin'. The editor, Syed Sulaiman Nadvi, acknowledges the efforts of his friend Abdul Samad bin Sharaf al-Din in acquiring and publishing the manuscript. He describes how his friend employed proofreaders, but when they did not perform adequately, he took over the task with great care, printing the book with corrections and notes. The editor then mentions that he is writing this on the eve of his departure for Hajj, hoping to return to the topic later. He ends with a prayer and his credentials as a judge in the Sharia court of Bhopal. This is a front-matter biographical account that establishes the context of the book's publication.

Key Takeaway
The zeal for knowledge (ghayra) is a driving force behind the preservation and transmission of Islamic scholarly works.

The Significance of Ibn Taymiyya's Critique of Logic
Nadvi introduces Ibn Taymiyya's refutation of Greek logic

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to characterize Ibn Taymiyya's critique of logic as presented by Dr. Nadvi and distinguish it from a simple rejection of philosophy.

Core Idea
Ibn Taymiyya's critique was a profound epistemological engagement, not anti-intellectualism.

This lesson introduces you to a biographical sketch provided by Dr. Syed Sulaiman Nadvi, setting the stage for Ibn Taymiyya's 'Radd alal-Mantiqiyin'. Nadvi's article in 'Islamic Culture' (1927) frames Ibn Taymiyya not as a mere opponent of logic but as a pioneer who anticipated later Western philosophers like Mill and Hume. Understanding this framing is essential before diving into the actual arguments of the text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and context
Dr. Syed Sulaiman Nadvi wrote an English article in 'Islamic Culture' that introduces Ibn Taymiyya's work. Note that this is a 20th-century scholarly framing, not a medieval one.
2
Extract the key claim about Ibn Taymiyya
Nadvi claims that Ibn Taymiyya was 'the first founder of Mill's system of Logic and the fore-runner of Hume's Philosophy.' This is a strong claim about influence and anticipation.
Consider what this implies for the originality of Western logic.
3
Interpret the claim's significance
Nadvi is arguing that Ibn Taymiyya's critique was not a crude rejection but a sophisticated philosophical project that engages with fundamental issues of reasoning and causation.
4
Connect to the Islamic intellectual tradition
This framing helps students of Islamic thought see that critiques of Greek logic were part of a rich tradition of epistemological reflection, not an anti-rational stance.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Introduction by Dr. Nadvi. And among what the author of this introduction said in his English article in the magazine 'Islamic Culture', year 1927 CE:

Commentary
This passage is the beginning of an introduction by Dr. Syed Sulaiman Nadvi to Ibn Taymiyya's 'Radd alal-Mantiqiyin'. It sets the stage for the reader by referencing an earlier English article by Nadvi that praised Ibn Taymiyya's philosophical critique. The introduction serves to contextualize Ibn Taymiyya's work as a profound engagement with Greek philosophy, not a simple rejection. The English extract that follows highlights Ibn Taymiyya's unique position as both a critic and a philosopher, comparing him to Mill and Hume. This biographical framing is meant to elevate the importance of the text for students of Islamic sciences.

Key Takeaway
Dr. Nadvi presents Ibn Taymiyya as a pioneering critic whose work foreshadowed modern Western empiricist logic, not as a mere opponent of reason.

Ibn Taymiyya and the Rare Manuscript
Publisher introduces author and rare manuscript.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the author of 'Radd al-Mantiqiyyin' and describe the rarity of its manuscript based on the publisher's introduction.

Core Idea
A single manuscript of a groundbreaking critique of logic survived in Hyderabad.

The publisher introduces Ibn Taymiyya as a genius and renewer of the eighth century, highlighting his work 'Radd al-Mantiqiyyin'. This lesson focuses on the biographical details and the unique manuscript location, which are essential for understanding the book's significance in Islamic intellectual history.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author
Note the full name, lineage, birth (661 AH, Harran), and death (728 AH, Damascus). Recognize his title: Taqi al-Din Abu al-Abbas Ahmad ibn Taymiyya.
He is the 'renewer of the eighth century'.
2
Locate the manuscript
The passage states it is in the Asafiyya Library in Hyderabad, Deccan, number 219, in the Theology section. Understand that this is the only known complete copy existent today.
The manuscript is rare and complete.
3
Explain the rarity's significance
Reflect on why a single manuscript matters for scholarship: it preserves Ibn Taymiyya's critique of logic, a work that might otherwise be lost. This rarity underscores the importance of manuscript recovery and preservation in Islamic studies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم
الحمد لله الذي أرسل رسوله بالهدى ودين الحق ليظهره على الدين كله، وكفى بالله شهيداً. وأشهد أن لا إله إلا الله وحده لا شريك له إقراراً به وتوحيداً. وأشهد أن محمداً عبده ورسوله صلى الله عليه وعلى آله وسلم تسليماً مزيداً.
أما بعد، فإن لعبقري الإسلام مجددِ القرن الثامن الإمام الأعظم، تقي الدين أبي العباس أحمد ابن تيمية في خِزانة الكتب الآصفية بحيدر آباد الدَّكَّن أثر مهم وسِفر لا يكاد يوجد على وجه الأرض اليوم نسخة منه سواها إلا ما نُسخ منها . ألا وهو كتاب الردّ على المنطقيين» مخطوط نادر سالم کامل من قسم الكلام، رقم ۲۱۹ ومصنفه هو الإمام تقي الدين أبو العباس أحمد بن عبد الحليم بن عبد السلام بن عبد الله بن الخَضِر بن علي بن عبد الله الشهير بابن تيميّة الحرّاني، المولود بحران سنة ٦٦١ ، والمتوفي بدمشق سنة ٧٢٨ هـ كتاب الرد على المنطقيين». وما أدراك ما كتاب الرد على المنطقيين»! كتاب موضوع يبحث عما اتخذوه أساساً للفكر البشري منذ أقدم العصور قبل الإسلام، وتطوّراته في عهد الإسلام إلى عصر المصنف ويبين ما لذاك الأساس في الأفكار الإسلامية والعلوم الشرعية من عميق الأثر وعظيم السلطان، ثم يكشف ما فيه من فساد وعوج بتحقيق دقيق نافذة وجُرأة نادرة المثال. كتاب يفرّق بين الحق والباطل ويميز بين الصحيح والفاسد ويهدي إلى صراط مستقيم، ويقذف بالحق على الباطل فيَدْمَغُه فإذا هو زاهِق .
وبصيره قام مصنفه أمام جيش كثيف من شُبهات مشككة وظنون كاذبة وبدع مُضِلَّة ومحدثات مزخرفة، فحمل عليه حملات صادقة متسلّحاً بسلاح لا ينكسر ومتدرّعاً بدرع الكتاب
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Praise be to Allah who sent His Messenger with guidance and the religion of truth to make it prevail over all religions, and sufficient is Allah as a Witness. I bear witness that there is no deity but Allah alone, with no partner, in acknowledgment and monotheism. And I bear witness that Muhammad is His servant and Messenger, may Allah bless him and his family and grant them abundant peace. To proceed: Indeed, for the genius of Islam, the renewer of the eighth century, the greatest Imam, Taqi al-Din Abu al-Abbas Ahmad ibn Taymiyya, in the Asafiyya Library in Hyderabad, Deccan, there is an important work and a book whose like on the face of the earth today no copy exists except that one, save those copied from it. That is the book 'Al-Radd 'ala al-Mantiqiyyin', a rare complete manuscript from the section on Theology (Kalam), number 219. Its author is the Imam Taqi al-Din Abu al-Abbas Ahmad ibn Abd al-Halim ibn Abd al-Salam ibn Abd Allah ibn al-Khidr ibn Ali ibn Abd Allah, known as Ibn Taymiyya al-Harrani, born in Harran in the year 661, and died in Damascus in the year 728 AH. The book 'Al-Radd 'ala al-Mantiqiyyin'—and what will make you know what the book 'Al-Radd 'ala al-Mantiqiyyin' is! A book whose subject examines what they have taken as the basis of human thought since the earliest times before Islam, and its developments during the Islamic era up to the author's time, and it explains the deep impact and great authority of that basis in Islamic ideas and religious sciences, then it uncovers its corruption and crookedness with precise penetrating investigation and rare courage. A book that distinguishes between truth and falsehood and differentiates between the sound and the corrupt, guiding to a straight path, and it hurls the truth against falsehood, which it destroys, and behold, it vanishes. And with his insight, its author stood before a dense army of doubting specious arguments, false conjectures, misleading innovations, and embellished novelties, so he launched truthful attacks against it, armed with an unbreakable weapon and shielded by the armor of the book.
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage is the publisher's introduction to the book 'Radd 'ala al-Mantiqiyyin' by Ibn Taymiyya. It begins with the basmala and hamdala, then praises the author as the renewer of the eighth Islamic century. It notes the rarity of the manuscript, found only in the Asafiyya Library in Hyderabad. The author's full lineage and birth/death dates are given. The passage extols the book's importance: it examines the foundations of human thought from pre-Islamic times, traces their development in Islam, and critiques the corruption in logic with incisive analysis. The book is described as distinguishing truth from falsehood and demolishing specious arguments. The author is portrayed as courageously confronting doubts and innovations.

Introduction and Front Matter

The Book's Mission: Refuting the Logicians
Publisher describes the book's mission and method.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the central claim of 'Radd al-Mantiqiyyin' and how it aims to distinguish truth from falsehood.

Core Idea
Ibn Taymiyya's book exposes the corruption of Greek logic and defends Islamic epistemology.

The publisher extols the book's scope and method. This lesson unpacks how the book examines the foundations of thought, traces their development, and reveals their flaws. You will learn to articulate the book's mission as a tool for separating truth from falsehood in Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Summarize the scope
The passage says the book examines the basis of human thought 'from the earliest times before Islam' and its developments 'in the Islamic era up to the author's time'. Identify that this is a historical and critical survey.
The author traces how logic entered Islamic thought.
2
Identify what the book uncovers
The book 'uncovers its corruption and crookedness'—meaning it reveals the flaws in logical reasoning. Note the words 'فساد' (corruption) and 'عوج' (crookedness).
The critique is precise and courageous.
3
Recognize its method
The book 'distinguishes between truth and falsehood' and 'differentiates between the sound and the corrupt'. It uses 'precise penetrating investigation' and 'rare courage'. Understand that this is a methodological refutation, not mere polemic.
The goal is to 'destroy falsehood with truth'.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Ibn Taymiyya's Refutation of the Logicians: Purpose and Method
Publisher introduces the book and Ibn Taymiyya's methodology.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe Ibn Taymiyya's universal criterion for evaluating all beliefs and explain how it frames his refutation of the logicians.

Core Idea
The Quran and Sunnah are the sole measure of truth; reason is valid only when it aligns with revelation.

The publisher's introduction to Ibn Taymiyya's 'The Refutation of the Logicians' sets the stage for one of the most powerful critiques of Greek logic in Islamic history. In this lesson, we will learn what makes this book so significant and grasp its author's foundational principle: that all human opinions must be weighed against the Book and the Sunnah. Understanding this method is key to appreciating Ibn Taymiyya's entire project.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the book's subject and rarity
The passage describes the book as a rare manuscript that investigates the foundations of human thought from pre-Islamic times, showing its influence on Islamic sciences and exposing its corruption.
The manuscript's rarity underscores its importance and the urgency of preserving such works.
2
Extract the universal principle
Ibn Taymiyya's method: all opinions and beliefs must be weighed against what Allah revealed in the Quran and Sunnah. Sound reason never contradicts revelation.
This principle is presented as a 'valid criterion and a true scale' for all times.
3
Understand the two types of words
Words are divided into those found in the Quran and Hadith (first type) and those not found there (second type). The meanings of the first type are the principle, and the second type must be referred back to the first.
This classification is key to Ibn Taymiyya's linguistic and epistemological critique.
4
Apply the method to the logicians
The logicians' terms and categories (e.g., substance, accident) belong to the second type. They must be judged by whether they agree with the Quran and Sunnah, not accepted uncritically.
This leads to a radical re-evaluation of the foundations of logic.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم
الحمد لله الذي أرسل رسوله بالهدى ودين الحق ليظهره على الدين كله، وكفى بالله شهيداً. وأشهد أن لا إله إلا الله وحده لا شريك له إقراراً به وتوحيداً. وأشهد أن محمداً عبده ورسوله صلى الله عليه وعلى آله وسلم تسليماً مزيداً .
أما بعد، فإن لعبقري الإسلام مجددِ القرن الثامن الإمام الأعظم، تقي الدين أبي العباس أحمد ابن تيمية في خِزانة الكتب الآصفية بحيدر آباد الدَّكَّن أثر مهم وسِفر لا يكاد يوجد على وجه الأرض اليوم نسخة منه سواها إلا ما نُسخ منها . ألا وهو كتاب الردّ على المنطقيين» مخطوط نادر سالم کامل من قسم الكلام، رقم ۲۱۹ ومصنفه هو الإمام تقي الدين أبو العباس أحمد بن عبد الحليم بن عبد السلام بن عبد الله بن الخَضِر بن علي بن عبد الله الشهير بابن تيميّة الحرّاني، المولود بحران سنة ٦٦١ ، والمتوفي بدمشق سنة ٧٢٨ هـ كتاب الرد على المنطقيين». وما أدراك ما كتاب الرد على المنطقيين»! كتاب موضوع يبحث عما اتخذوه أساساً للفكر البشري منذ أقدم العصور قبل الإسلام، وتطوّراته في عهد الإسلام إلى عصر المصنف ويبين ما لذاك الأساس في الأفكار الإسلامية والعلوم الشرعية من عميق الأثر وعظيم السلطان، ثم يكشف ما فيه من فساد وعوج بتحقيق دقيق نافذة وجُرأة نادرة المثال. كتاب يفرّق بين الحق والباطل ويميز بين الصحيح والفاسد ويهدي إلى صراط مستقيم، ويقذف بالحق على الباطل فيَدْمَغُه فإذا هو زاهِق .
وبصيره
قام مصنفه أمام جيش كثيف من شُبهات مشككة وظنون كاذبة وبدع مُضِلَّة ومحدثات مزخرفة، فحمل عليه حملات صادقة متسلّحاً بسلاح لا ينكسر ومتدرّعاً بدرع
الكتاب
العالم الإسلامي المتحيّر من الظلمات إلى النور . قابل وَحْدَه أساطينه العظام ونازل فرداً صناديده الجسام وهو رابط الجأش ثابتُ الجَنَان غير هَيَّاب ولا مِحْجام. فإن سألت عن سرّ هذا الإقدام القاهر والهجوم الظاهر تجده مضمراً في الاعتصام بكلام مهيمن طاهر، ونور ساطع باهر وميزان عادل غير جائر، ذلك الكتاب لا ريب فيه، لا يأتيه الباطل من بين يديه ولا من خلفه، تنزيل من حكيم حميد . ولقد صدق القائل حيث قال :
لا تَخشَ من بدع لهم وحوادث ما دمت في كنف الكتاب وحِرْزِهِ من كان حارسه الكتاب ودِرْعُه لم يخشَ من طعن العدوّ ووَخْزِهِ لا تَخشَ من شُبهاتهم واحمل إذا ما قابلتك بنصره وبعزّه والله ما هاب امرؤ شُبُهاتِهم إلا لضعف القلبِ منه وعَجْزِهِ
وقد أطلعنا المصنف رحمه الله على طريقته بل قد ضَرَب لنا قاعدة كلية هي معيار صالح و میزان صادق یوزن به كلُّ ما حدث أو سيحدث من آراء ومعتقدات أو أفكار ونظريات أو قضايا ومقالات لمِلَّة من الملل أو نِحْلة من النّحل في زمن من الأزمان
حيث قال في بعض مصنفاته :
إن الواجب طلب علم ما أنزل الله على رسوله من الكتاب والحكمة، ومعرفة ما أراده بألفاظ القرآن والحديث كما كان على ذلك الصحابة والتابعون لهم بإحسان ومَنْ سلك سبيلهم . ثم إذا عرف ما بينه الرسولُ نَظَر في أقوال الناس وما أرادوه بها، فعُرِضَتْ على الكتاب والسنة لينظر المعاني الموافقة للرسول والمعاني المخالفة له. والعقل الصريح دائماً موافق للرسول لا يخالفه قط، فإن الميزان مع الكتاب، والله أنزل الكتاب بالحق والميزان. فهذا سبيل الهدى والسنة والعلم . وقال أيضاً: «الألفاظ نوعان : نوع يوجد في كلام الله ورسوله ونوع لا يوجد في كلام الله ورسوله. فيعرف معنى الأول ويجعل ذلك المعنى هو الأصل، ويعرف ما يعنيه الناس بالثاني ويردّ إلى الأول. هذا طريق أهل الهدى والسنة .
ولقد أوتي المصنف رحمه الله حظاً وافراً من هذه الحكمة وسُلّط على استعمالها
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Praise be to Allah who sent His Messenger with guidance and the religion of truth to make it prevail over all religions, and sufficient is Allah as a Witness. And I bear witness that there is no god but Allah alone, with no partner, acknowledging Him and affirming His oneness. And I bear witness that Muhammad is His servant and Messenger, may Allah bless him and his family and grant them abundant peace.
To proceed: Indeed, for the genius of Islam, the reviver of the eighth century, the supreme imam, Taqi al-Din Abu al-Abbas Ahmad ibn Taymiyya, in the Asafiyya library in Hyderabad, Deccan, there is an important work and a book whose copy on the face of the earth today is hardly found except that one, unless copies have been made from it. It is the book "The Refutation of the Logicians", a rare and complete manuscript from the section on theology, number 219, and its author is the imam Taqi al-Din Abu al-Abbas Ahmad ibn Abd al-Halim ibn Abd al-Salam ibn Abd Allah ibn al-Khidr ibn Ali ibn Abd Allah, famous as Ibn Taymiyya al-Harrani, born in Harran in the year 661 and died in Damascus in the year 728 AH, the book "The Refutation of the Logicians". And what will make you understand what "The Refutation of the Logicians" is! A book whose subject is an investigation of what they took as the foundation of human thought from the earliest times before Islam, and its developments in the Islamic era up to the author's time, and it shows the deep influence and great authority of that foundation in Islamic thought and religious sciences, then it reveals its corruption and crookedness with precise penetrating investigation and rare courage. A book that distinguishes between truth and falsehood, differentiates between sound and unsound, guides to a straight path, and hurls the truth against falsehood, which destroys it, and then it vanishes.
And with insight, its author stood before a dense army of doubting ambiguities, false conjectures, misleading innovations, and ornate novelties, and he launched truthful attacks against them, armed with an unbreakable weapon and shielded with the armor of the Book, leading the bewildered Islamic world from darkness to light. Alone he confronted its great masters and individually faced its huge champions while calm of heart, firm of spirit, neither fearful nor hesitant. If you ask about the secret of this overwhelming advance and manifest attack, you will find it hidden in clinging to a pure and dominant speech, a bright and brilliant light, and a just and fair balance, that book in which there is no doubt, falsehood cannot approach it from before or behind, a revelation from the Wise and Praiseworthy. And the speaker spoke truly when he said:
Do not fear their innovations and events as long as you are in the shelter and protection of the Book. Whoever has the Book as his guard and armor will not fear the thrust and stab of the enemy. Do not fear their ambiguities and carry on when they confront you with His support and might. By Allah, no man has feared their ambiguities except due to weakness of heart and incapacity.
And the author, may Allah have mercy on him, has acquainted us with his method; indeed he laid down for us a universal principle which is a valid criterion and a true scale by which to weigh everything that has occurred or will occur of opinions and beliefs, ideas and theories, issues and statements of any religious community or sect at any time. For he said in some of his writings:
Indeed it is obligatory to seek knowledge of what Allah has revealed to His Messenger of the Book and wisdom, and to know what He intended by the expressions of the Quran and Hadith as was the practice of the Companions and the Successors who followed them in excellence and those who followed their path. Then, when he knows what the Messenger has clarified, he looks at the statements of the people and what they intended by them, and they are presented to the Book and the Sunnah to see the meanings that agree with the Messenger and the meanings that oppose him. And sound reason is always in agreement with the Messenger, never opposing him at all, for the scale is with the Book, and Allah sent down the Book with truth and the scale. This is the path of guidance, the Sunnah, and knowledge. He also said: "Words are of two types: a type found in the speech of Allah and His Messenger, and a type not found in the speech of Allah and His Messenger. The meaning of the first is known and that meaning is made the principle, and what people mean by the second is known and is referred back to the first. This is the way of the people of guidance and the Sunnah."
And the author, may Allah have mercy on him, was given a generous share of this wisdom and was enabled to use it.
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage is the publisher's introduction to the book 'The Refutation of the Logicians' by Ibn Taymiyya. It begins with the basmala and hamdala, then praises the author and describes the rarity of the manuscript. The publisher highlights the book's significance: it examines the foundation of human thought (Greek logic) from pre-Islamic times to the author's era, showing its influence on Islamic sciences and then exposing its corruption. The book is presented as a decisive separator between truth and falsehood. The publisher then describes Ibn Taymiyya's courageous confrontation with the logicians' doubts and innovations, attributing his success to clinging to the Quran and Sunnah. A poetic couplet reinforces reliance on the Book. The introduction then quotes Ibn Taymiyya's own methodological principle: all opinions must be weighed against the Quran and Sunnah; sound reason never contradicts revelation. He divides words into those found in revelation and those not, requiring the latter to be interpreted in light of the former. This is the path of guidance. The publisher concludes that Ibn Taymiyya was granted much wisdom in this regard.

Key Terms
الرد على المنطقيين
الكتاب والحكمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) To present a new system of logic based on Greek thought.
B) To analyze the foundations of human thought and expose the corruption in Greek logic while highlighting the role of revelation.
C) To reconcile Greek philosophy with Islamic teachings.
D) To provide a biography of the logicians.

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya's universal principle: the Quran and Sunnah are the ultimate criterion for all truth claims, and all human concepts must be evaluated by them.
