Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Ibn Taymiyya's Method: Revelation as Criterion
Publisher lays out Ibn Taymiyya's epistemological foundation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain Ibn Taymiyya's universal rule for evaluating opinions by presenting them to the Quran and Sunnah, and describe the role of sound reason as always compatible with revelation.

Core Idea
For Ibn Taymiyya, revelation is the ultimate criterion; sound reason never contradicts it.

This passage from the publisher’s introduction sets the stage for Ibn Taymiyya’s entire project. He is not anti-reason, but he subordinates reason to revelation. The key is his universal rule: all opinions, from any sect or era, must be weighed against the Quran and Sunnah, understood as the Salaf understood them. Sound reason—reason that is pure and uncorrupted—will always align with revelation. This principle is the foundation of his critique of Greek logic in the rest of the book.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem
The publisher describes Ibn Taymiyya as a lone figure fearlessly confronting the great scholars of his time. Ask: what gave him such boldness? The answer is his reliance on the Quran.
2
Locate the universal rule
Find where Ibn Taymiyya lays down the 'universal rule' (قاعدة كلية). It is quoted: the obligation to seek knowledge of what Allah revealed (الكتاب والحكمة) and to understand it as the Salaf did. Then present people's statements to the Quran and Sunnah to see if they agree or disagree.
The term 'Wisdom' (الحكمة) here refers to the Sunnah.
3
Examine the role of reason
Notice the statement: 'Sound reason is always in agreement with the Messenger, never opposing him.' This clarifies that reason is not rejected but is placed under the authority of revelation. Reason is a tool, not an independent source.
The phrase 'العقل الصريح' means pure/sound reason, not flawed speculative reason.
4
Apply the principle
Consider how this method works: first, learn the revealed texts; then, understand people's statements; then, compare. The scale (ميزان) is the Book itself. All opinions are weighed against it.
This is the criterion by which all later arguments in the book will be judged.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
العالم الإسلامي المتحيّر من الظلمات إلى النور . قابل وَحْدَه أساطينه العظام ونازل فرداً صناديده الجسام وهو رابط الجأش ثابتُ الجَنَان غير هَيَّاب ولا مِحْجام. فإن سألت عن سرّ هذا الإقدام القاهر والهجوم الظاهر تجده مضمراً في الاعتصام بكلام مهيمن طاهر، ونور ساطع باهر وميزان عادل غير جائر، ذلك الكتاب لا ريب فيه، لا يأتيه الباطل من بين يديه ولا من خلفه، تنزيل من حكيم حميد . ولقد صدق القائل حيث قال : لا تَخشَ من بدع لهم وحوادث ما دمت في كنف الكتاب وحِرْزِهِ من كان حارسه الكتاب ودِرْعُه لم يخشَ من طعن العدوّ ووَخْزِهِ لا تَخشَ من شُبهاتهم واحمل إذا ما قابلتك بنصره وبعزّه والله ما هاب امرؤ شُبُهاتِهم إلا لضعف القلبِ منه وعَجْزِهِ وقد أطلعنا المصنف رحمه الله على طريقته بل قد ضَرَب لنا قاعدة كلية هي معيار صالح و میزان صادق یوزن به كلُّ ما حدث أو سيحدث من آراء ومعتقدات أو أفكار ونظريات أو قضايا ومقالات لمِلَّة من الملل أو نِحْلة من النّحل في زمن من الأزمان حيث قال في بعض مصنفاته : إن الواجب طلب علم ما أنزل الله على رسوله من الكتاب والحكمة، ومعرفة ما أراده بألفاظ القرآن والحديث كما كان على ذلك الصحابة والتابعون لهم بإحسان ومَنْ سلك سبيلهم . ثم إذا عرف ما بينه الرسولُ نَظَر في أقوال الناس وما أرادوه بها، فعُرِضَتْ على الكتاب والسنة لينظر المعاني الموافقة للرسول والمعاني المخالفة له. والعقل الصريح دائماً موافق للرسول لا يخالفه قط، فإن الميزان مع الكتاب، والله أنزل الكتاب بالحق والميزان. فهذا سبيل الهدى والسنة والعلم .
The Islamic world moving from darkness to light. He alone confronted its great masters and individually challenged its huge champions, while he was calm-hearted, steadfast, neither fearful nor hesitant. If you ask about the secret of this overwhelming boldness and apparent attack, you find it hidden in clinging to a dominant pure speech, a brilliant shining light, and a just non-oppressive scale: that Book in which there is no doubt, falsehood does not come to it from before it or behind it, a revelation from the Wise, Praiseworthy. And the speaker spoke truth when he said: Do not fear innovations and events as long as you are in the shelter and protection of the Book. Whoever has the Book as his guard and armor will not fear the stab and jab of the enemy. Do not fear their doubts; advance when they meet you with His help and might. By Allah, no man fears their doubts except due to weakness of heart and incapacity. And the author—may Allah have mercy on him—informed us of his method, indeed he laid down for us a universal rule, a valid criterion and a truthful scale by which is weighed everything that has occurred or will occur of opinions, beliefs, ideas, theories, issues, or articles of any sect or denomination at any time. He said in some of his writings: Indeed it is obligatory to seek knowledge of what Allah revealed to His Messenger from the Book and Wisdom, and to know what He intended by the words of the Quran and Hadith, as the Companions, the Followers who did well, and those who followed their path did. Then, when one knows what the Messenger clarified, one looks at people's statements and what they intended by them, and they are presented to the Book and Sunnah so that the meanings agreeing with the Messenger and the meanings opposing him may be seen. Sound reason is always in agreement with the Messenger, never opposing him. For the scale is with the Book, and Allah sent down the Book with truth and the scale. This is the path of guidance, Sunnah, and knowledge.
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage is the publisher's introduction, praising Ibn Taymiyya and presenting his core methodological principle. It begins with a poetic description of Ibn Taymiyya as a lone figure fearlessly confronting the great scholars of his time, attributing his boldness to his clinging to the Quran, described as a 'dominant pure speech' and a 'just scale'. The poem reinforces that protection by the Quran makes one fearless against innovations and doubts. The publisher then states that Ibn Taymiyya laid down a universal criterion for weighing all opinions and beliefs. The crux of the passage is Ibn Taymiyya's own quote: the duty is to seek knowledge of Allah's revelation—the Book (Quran) and Wisdom (Sunnah)—and to understand it as the Salaf understood it. Then, after knowing what the Messenger taught, one examines people's statements and presents them to the Quran and Sunnah to distinguish their agreement or opposition to the Messenger. A key point is that 'sound reason' (al-'aql al-sarih) is always in harmony with revelation, never contradicting it. This establishes the primacy of revelation as the ultimate criterion, with reason in a subordinate but compatible role. The passage thus sets the epistemological foundation for Ibn Taymiyya's critique of Greek logic in the rest of the book.

Key Terms
الكتاب
الحكمة
العقل الصريح

B) The Quran and Sunnah
C) Consensus of scholars
D) Personal judgment

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya's method: all opinions must be weighed against the Quran and Sunnah, and sound reason always aligns with revelation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Take a contemporary theological opinion (e.g., 'God is everywhere, including inside creation'). Present it to the Quran and Sunnah: find verses and hadith that mention God's 'istiwa' (rising above the Throne). Determine if the opinion agrees or disagrees with the revealed texts. Then check if sound reason (as defined by the Salaf) supports this opinion.
?
Explain in your own words why Ibn Taymiyya insists that sound reason never contradicts revelation. Use the passage to support your explanation.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
8 min
Ibn Taymiyya's Two Types of Words: A Hermeneutical Tool
Ibn Taymiyya's word types and biographical references

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply Ibn Taymiyya's two-type classification of words to determine how a term's meaning should be derived from revelation versus common usage.

Core Idea
All words are judged by revelation: non-revealed meanings are referred back to revealed ones.

Ibn Taymiyya provides a key methodological principle for distinguishing between revealed and non-revealed terms. This principle is essential in Islamic theology and jurisprudence to avoid innovation (bid'a). The passage also highlights the importance of understanding the author's life, directing readers to major biographical sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Types
Locate in the Arabic the two categories: words found in revelation (Quran and Sunnah) and words not found there. Note that the first type is the authoritative norm.
The first type includes words like 'salat', 'zakat'; the second includes technical terms from philosophy or common parlance.
2
Understand Epistemic Priority
Recognize that the meanings of revealed words are known and made the principle (al-asl). These are the standard against which all other meanings are measured.
This prioritizes divine revelation over human convention.
3
Analyze the Operation for Non-Revealed Words
For words not in revelation, their common meaning is first understood, then 'referred back' to the revealed meaning. This is not a rejection of common usage but a subordination of it.
The reference back (radd) ensures consistency with revelation.
4
Connect to the Methodology of Ahl al-Huda wa al-Sunna
Ibn Taymiyya presents this as the path of the orthodox Muslims. Realize that this principle is a distinctive tool used throughout his works to critique foreign concepts.
This classification is a key to understanding Ibn Taymiyya's approach in Naqd al-Mantiq and other writings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال أيضاً: «الألفاظ نوعان : نوع يوجد في كلام الله ورسوله ونوع لا يوجد في كلام الله ورسوله. فيعرف معنى الأول ويجعل ذلك المعنى هو الأصل، ويعرف ما يعنيه الناس بالثاني ويردّ إلى الأول. هذا طريق أهل الهدى والسنة . ولقد أوتي المصنف رحمه الله حظاً وافراً من هذه الحكمة وسُلّط على استعمالها كل التسليط، والله يؤتي الحكمة من يشاء، ومن يُؤْتَ الحكمة فقد أوتي خيراً كثيراً. وهذه إشارة إلى خلاصة ما في الكتاب، أما تفصيله فموضوع بحث مستوعب ونقد تحليلي مستفيض لا نستطيع القيام بحقه الآن وقد تأخر صدور الكتاب غاية التأخير . ولا يكمل الكلام على كتاب بدون الكلام على حياة مصنفه ولوددنا استيفاء حياة المصنف الكلام على ذلك ولكننا نؤجّله إلى فرصة أخرى ونحيل القارىء على مصادرها المعروفة، مثل «العقود الدرّية في مناقب شيخ الإسلام أحمد بن تيمية» لتلميذه الرشيد الحافظ شمس الدين محمد بن أحمد بن عبد الهادي المقدسي، صاحب «الصارم المُنْكِي في الرد على ابن السبكي، المتوفى سنة ٧٤٤ هـ، ط . مصر سنة ١٣٥٦ هـ ؛ و«القول الجلى في ترجمة شيخ الإسلام ابن تيمية «الحنبلي لصفي الدين الحنفي البخاري؛ والكواكب الدرية في مناقب الإمام ابن تيمية للشيخ مَرْعِيّ بن يوسف الكرمي الحنبلي، المتوفى سنة ۱۱۳۳ هـ ، كلاهما ط مصر سنة ١٣٢٩ هـ . وقد ترجم له جماعة منهم تلميذه الحافظ شمس الدين الذهبي، صاحب تاريخ الإسلام الكبير، المتوفى سنة ٧٤٨ هـ؛ وتلميذه الحافظ عماد الدين ابن كثير، صاحب البداية والنهاية، المتوفى سنة ٧٧٤ هـ؛ والحافظ ابن رجب الحنبلي المتوفى سنة ٧٩٥ هـ في طبقات الحنابلة والحافظ ابن حجر العسقلاني المتوفى سنة ٨٥٢ هـ في «الدرر الكامنة في أعيان المئة الثامنة ، ط. حيدر آباد الدكن سنة ١٣٤٨ هـ، ج ۱، ص ١٤٤ - ١٦٠ . وقد أوردَتْ دائرة المعارف الإسلامية للمستشرقين المطبوعة بأوروبا ترجمة الشيخ فما أنصفته، وأصح منها ما كتبه المستشرق الألماني «غولدزيهر» في مقالته على ابن تيمية في المجلد السابع من دائرة معارف الديانة والأخلاق» الإنجليزية للمستر هيستنج ، ط. أيدمبرو سنة ١٨١٤ م. ونسخة الآصفية كتبها بعضُ تلامذة الشيخ المصرَّح اسمه بآخر الكتاب، وهو وصف النسخة الخطية محمود بن أحمد بن حسن الشافعي . كتبها بخط النسخ الجلي المسلسل، ممتد الحروف مستديرة الزوايا غير منقوطة إلا قليلاً، ومحلّى في كثير من المواضع بفضول
He also said: 'Words are of two types: a type found in the speech of Allah and His Messenger, and a type not found in the speech of Allah and His Messenger. The meaning of the first is known and that meaning is made the principle; the meaning intended by people of the second is known and referred back to the first. This is the way of the people of guidance and Sunnah.' And the author—may Allah have mercy on him—was given an abundant share of this wisdom and was empowered to use it to the fullest. Allah gives wisdom to whom He wills, and whoever is given wisdom has been given much good. This is an indication of the essence of the book; as for its detail, it is a topic of comprehensive research and extensive analytical critique which we cannot do justice to now, and the publication of the book has been greatly delayed. A discussion of a book is not complete without discussing the life of its author. We wish we could fully cover the author's life, but we postpone that to another opportunity and refer the reader to well-known sources, such as al-'Uqud al-Durriyya fi Manaqib Shaykh al-Islam Ahmad ibn Taymiyya by his insightful student al-Hafiz Shams al-Din Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn 'Abd al-Hadi al-Maqdisi, author of al-Sarim al-Munki fi al-Radd 'ala Ibn al-Subki, died 744 AH, printed in Egypt 1356 AH; and al-Qawl al-Jali fi Tarjamat Shaykh al-Islam Ibn Taymiyya al-Hanbali by Safi al-Din al-Hanafi al-Bukhari; and al-Kawakib al-Durriyya fi Manaqib al-Imam Ibn Taymiyya by Shaykh Mar'i ibn Yusuf al-Karmi al-Hanbali, died 1133 AH, both printed in Egypt 1329 AH. Many others have translated his life, among them his student al-Hafiz Shams al-Din al-Dhahabi, author of Tarikh al-Islam al-Kabir, died 748 AH; his student al-Hafiz 'Imad al-Din Ibn Kathir, author of al-Bidaya wa al-Nihaya, died 774 AH; al-Hafiz Ibn Rajab al-Hanbali, died 795 AH, in Tabaqat al-Hanabila; and al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar al-'Asqalani, died 852 AH, in al-Durar al-Kamina fi A'yan al-Mi'a al-Thamina, printed in Hyderabad-Deccan 1348 AH, vol. 1, pp. 144-160. The Encyclopedia of Islam by the Orientalists printed in Europe presented a biography of the shaykh but did not do him justice. More accurate is what the German Orientalist Goldziher wrote in his article on Ibn Taymiyya in volume seven of the English Encyclopedia of Religion and Ethics by Mr. Hastings, printed in Edinburgh 1814 CE. The Asafiyya copy was written by one of the shaykh's students, whose name is mentioned at the end of the book. It is a description of the manuscript by Mahmud ibn Ahmad ibn Hasan al-Shafi'i, written in clear chancellery naskh script, with extended letters, rounded corners, seldom dotted, and embellished in many places with superfluous additions.
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage continues the publisher's introduction, presenting a second quote from Ibn Taymiyya that further articulates his hermeneutical principle. Ibn Taymiyya divides words into two types: those found in divine revelation (Quran and Hadith) and those not found there. The meanings of the first type are taken as the authoritative norm; the meanings of the second type are understood according to common usage but must be referred back to the revealed meanings. This is presented as the methodology of 'the people of guidance and Sunnah.' The publisher then praises Ibn Taymiyya's wisdom and ability to apply this principle. He apologizes for not providing a detailed analysis of the book, but emphasizes that understanding the author's life is essential. Accordingly, he directs readers to several major biographical works: al-'Uqud al-Durriyya by Ibn 'Abd al-Hadi, al-Qawl al-Jali by al-Bukhari, al-Kawakib al-Durriyya by al-Karmi, and mentions other notable biographers such as al-Dhahabi, Ibn Kathir, Ibn Rajab, and Ibn Hajar. The publisher also critiques Orientalist scholarship, particularly the Encyclopedia of Islam, and recommends Goldziher's article and a specific manuscript copy. This section provides essential context for studying Ibn Taymiyya's life and works.

أهل الهدى والسنة

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya's two-type classification ensures that all linguistic analysis is grounded in revelation, preserving the integrity of Islamic concepts.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner

Biographical Sources on Ibn Taymiyya
Publisher lists sources for Ibn Taymiyya's biography and defers full treatment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify reliable biographical sources for an Islamic scholar and evaluate the accuracy of external accounts.

Core Idea
A scholar's biography is the key to understanding his work — trust only verified sources.

Before diving into Ibn Taymiyya's critique of logic, it is essential to understand who he was. The publisher of Radd al-Mantiqiyyin directs us to the most reliable biographical sources, written by Ibn Taymiyya's students and later historians. He also warns against less accurate accounts from Orientalist encyclopedias. This lesson trains you to evaluate biographical sources critically.

Guided Path
1
Identify the need for biography
The publisher states that a discussion of a book is not complete without discussing its author's life. Understand why context matters: the author's experiences, teachers, and era shape his writing.
2
Distinguish primary from secondary sources
The publisher lists works by Ibn Taymiyya's students (primary sources) and then by later historians (secondary). Note the difference: students had direct access, later historians rely on earlier accounts.
Primary: al-Maqdisi, al-Bukhari, al-Karmi. Secondary: al-Dhahabi, Ibn Kathir, etc.
3
Evaluate source credibility
The publisher critiques the Orientalist Encyclopedia of Islam as unfair and recommends Goldziher's article as more accurate. This shows the need to check the reliability of external, non-Muslim sources.
The publisher uses scholarly reputation and comprehensiveness as criteria.
4
Apply to your own research
When studying any Islamic scholar, first seek biographical works by their students, then look at later historians, and finally verify against multiple independent sources.
This method applies to figures like al-Ghazali, Ibn Rushd, or al-Shafi'i.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مقدمة الناشر
كل التسليط، والله يؤتي الحكمة من يشاء، ومن يُؤْتَ الحكمة فقد أوتي خيراً كثيراً. وهذه إشارة إلى خلاصة ما في الكتاب، أما تفصيله فموضوع بحث مستوعب ونقد تحليلي مستفيض لا نستطيع القيام بحقه الآن وقد تأخر صدور الكتاب غاية التأخير .
ولا يكمل الكلام على كتاب بدون الكلام على حياة مصنفه ولوددنا استيفاء حياة المصنف الكلام على ذلك ولكننا نؤجّله إلى فرصة أخرى ونحيل القارىء على مصادرها المعروفة، مثل «العقود الدرّية في مناقب شيخ الإسلام أحمد بن تيمية» لتلميذه الرشيد الحافظ شمس الدين محمد بن أحمد بن عبد الهادي المقدسي، صاحب «الصارم المُنْكِي في الرد على ابن السبكي، المتوفى سنة ٧٤٤ هـ، ط . مصر سنة ١٣٥٦ هـ ؛ و«القول الجلى في ترجمة شيخ الإسلام ابن تيمية «الحنبلي لصفي الدين الحنفي البخاري؛ والكواكب الدرية في مناقب الإمام ابن تيمية للشيخ مَرْعِيّ بن يوسف الكرمي الحنبلي، المتوفى سنة ۱۱۳۳ هـ ، كلاهما ط مصر سنة ١٣٢٩ هـ.
وقد ترجم له جماعة منهم تلميذه الحافظ شمس الدين الذهبي، صاحب تاريخ الإسلام الكبير، المتوفى سنة ٧٤٨ هـ؛ وتلميذه الحافظ عماد الدين ابن كثير، صاحب البداية والنهاية، المتوفى سنة ٧٧٤ هـ؛ والحافظ ابن رجب الحنبلي المتوفى سنة ٧٩٥ هـ في طبقات الحنابلة والحافظ ابن حجر العسقلاني المتوفى سنة ٨٥٢ هـ في «الدرر الكامنة في أعيان المئة الثامنة ، ط. حيدر آباد الدكن سنة ١٣٤٨ هـ، ج ۱، ص ١٤٤ - ١٦٠ .
وأوردَتْ دائرة المعارف الإسلامية للمستشرقين المطبوعة بأوروبا ترجمة الشيخ فما أنصفته، وأصح منها ما كتبه المستشرق الألماني «غولدزيهر» في مقالته على ابن تيمية في المجلد السابع من دائرة معارف الديانة والأخلاق» الإنجليزية للمستر هيستنج ، ط. أيدمبرو سنة ١٨١٤ م.
Publisher's Introduction
All authority is from Allah, who grants wisdom to whom He wills, and whoever is granted wisdom has been granted abundant good. This is an indication of the summary of what is in the book; as for its detail, it is a subject of comprehensive research and extensive analytical criticism that we cannot do justice to now, and the publication of the book has been extremely delayed.
A discussion of a book is not complete without discussing the life of its author, and we would have liked to fully cover the life of the author, but we postpone it to another opportunity and refer the reader to its well-known sources, such as 'al-'Uqud al-Durriyya fi Manaqib Shaykh al-Islam Ahmad ibn Taymiyya' by his student the memorizer Shams al-Din Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Abd al-Hadi al-Maqdisi, author of 'al-Sarim al-Munki fi al-Radd ala Ibn al-Subki', died 744 AH, published in Egypt 1356 AH; and 'al-Qawl al-Jali fi Tarjamat Shaykh al-Islam Ibn Taymiyya al-Hanbali' by Safi al-Din al-Hanafi al-Bukhari; and 'al-Kawakib al-Durriyya fi Manaqib al-Imam Ibn Taymiyya' by Shaykh Mar'i ibn Yusuf al-Karmi al-Hanbali, died 1133 AH, both published in Egypt 1329 AH.
Several of his students wrote his biography, including his student the memorizer Shams al-Din al-Dhahabi, author of the large Tarikh al-Islam, died 748 AH; and his student the memorizer Imad al-Din Ibn Kathir, author of al-Bidaya wa al-Nihaya, died 774 AH; and the memorizer Ibn Rajab al-Hanbali, died 795 AH, in Tabaqat al-Hanabila; and the memorizer Ibn Hajar al-Asqalani, died 852 AH, in 'al-Durar al-Kamina fi A'yan al-Mi'a al-Thamina', published in Hyderabad Deccan 1348 AH, vol. 1, pp. 144-160.
The Encyclopedia of Islam by Orientalists printed in Europe published a biography of the Shaykh but did not do him justice; more accurate is what the German Orientalist Goldziher wrote in his article on Ibn Taymiyya in the seventh volume of the English 'Encyclopedia of Religion and Ethics' by Mr. Hastings, published in Edinburgh 1814 CE.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage is part of the publisher's introduction to the book 'Radd al-Mantiqiyyin'. The publisher begins by acknowledging that a full treatment of the book's content and a detailed biography of Ibn Taymiyya are beyond the scope of this introduction. Instead, he directs the reader to several key biographical sources. These include works by Ibn Taymiyya's students: al-Maqdisi's 'al-Uqud al-Durriyya', al-Bukhari's 'al-Qawl al-Jali', and al-Karmi's 'al-Kawakib al-Durriyya'. He also lists later historians who wrote about Ibn Taymiyya, such as al-Dhahabi, Ibn Kathir, Ibn Rajab, and Ibn Hajar, providing their full names, dates of death, and relevant works. Finally, he critiques the Orientalist Encyclopedia of Islam's treatment of Ibn Taymiyya and recommends Goldziher's article as more accurate. The passage demonstrates the publisher's concern with directing readers to trustworthy sources for Ibn Taymiyya's biography, rather than attempting to summarize it himself.

Key Terms
مقدمة الناشر
العقود الدرية
القول الجلي

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
The Value of a Collated Manuscript
Publisher describes the physical manuscript, collation, and handwriting.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the evidence that a manuscript was collated during the author's lifetime and explain why this makes it a primary source for scholarly work.

Core Idea
A manuscript collated during the author's lifetime is the gold standard for textual accuracy.

When studying a work like Ibn Taymiyya's refutation of the logicians, we need a reliable text. This passage, from the publisher's introduction, provides the evidence that the manuscript in question meets that standard: it was collated with the author's original during his lifetime, corrected in his own hand, and contains his additions. Understanding manuscript evidence is a key skill for anyone engaging seriously with Islamic scholarly works.

Guided Path
1
Identify the physical details
Note the paper, ink, page dimensions, and numbering systems (Urdu numerals vs. Arabic abjad). These details are the first level of manuscript identification.
This helps distinguish the manuscript from other copies.
2
Find the collation note
Locate the statement on the last page: 'collated with the original of the author in his own handwriting.' The date given is 728 AH, the year of Ibn Taymiyya's death, and it specifies the 20th of Dhu al-Qa'dah.
This is the key evidence that the manuscript was corrected against the author's own copy.
3
Determine the manuscript's authority
Because it was collated during the author's lifetime and contains his handwritten additions, this manuscript is considered a primary source—it transmits the text as intended by the author, with corrections and even extra material not in his original.
Such manuscripts are highly valued in tahqiq (critical editing).
4
Recognize the value for studying logical refutation
For a work like 'Radd 'ala al-Mantiqiyyin', having a manuscript that goes back to the author's own time ensures that the arguments we study are authentic. Any analysis of Ibn Taymiyya's critique of logic must rely on a textually sound basis.
This connects manuscript studies to the broader goal of rigorous intellectual inquiry.

Cover
26
Publisher's Introduction
The dots and marks mislead the reader, with ink black tending slightly to red on sturdy brown paper, light in the large format. Its number of pages is 541 with modern numbering in pencil using Urdu numerals. As for the original numbering, it is in ink with alphabetical letters on each leaf without pages, so the last leaf is 'ra'ayin jim' i.e. 274. The length of the page is 10 qirats or 1 25/2 centimeters, and its width is 7 qirats or 3 17/4 centimeters. The length of the written area is 7 qirats or 191 centimeters, and its width is 4/4 h qirats or 12 centimeters. The number of lines in each page varies between 18 and 25 lines, generally 20, 21, and 23 lines.
The title of the book on the cover is 'Kitab al-Radd 'ala al-Mantiqiyyin' by Shaykh al-Imam al-Hafiz Abu (sic) al-'Abbas Ahmad ibn 'Abd al-Halim ibn 'Abd al-Salam al-Harrani known as Ibn Taymiyya, may Allah forgive him with His grace and generosity. Other phrases are written on it mentioning those who authored refutations of the logicians, and a poem censuring logic (which Ibn al-Qayyim, may Allah have mercy on him, transmitted in 'Miftah Dar al-Sa'adah' vol. 1, p. 166, with slight variation, and in its presentation some supplications; we refrain from reproducing that here in this brief note, suffice with its image at the beginning of the book.
In the margins, the book has been handled by multiple hands; their traces appear in the margins in different scripts: headings for some topics, comments on some places, repetitions of some writings especially the shaykh's writings. Much correction of the book upon collation has been done on it, such as filling omissions, additions, variations in some readings, and in places of the text and margins repeated phrases have been struck out and other changes made, and some words are vocalized.
The collation with the original: it states on the last page (see image): 'It was collated with the original of the author in his own handwriting read to him, may Allah be pleased with him, in the year eight in the year eight and twenty and seven hundred (728 AH). I read the beginning of this copy to him, and he wrote in his handwriting on its margins additions for it, etc.' This suffices to show the majesty and greatness of this manuscript. For it is established that the copy was written during the lifetime of the author, may Allah Almighty have mercy on him; that it was collated with the author's original in his own handwriting read to him; that its collation was completed in the year 728 - the year of the author's death - indeed continuously after his death and it was on the 20th of Dhu al-Qa'dah; that its beginning had been read to the author so it has on the margin of p. 75 'it reached its author, may Allah be pleased with him'; that the author, may Allah have mercy on him, wrote on its margins in his noble handwriting; and that among those writings are additions by him to his original composition, so it contains materials not found in it - this is what distinguishes this copy from the author's own copy in his handwriting.
We examined the shaykh's handwriting and writing, and we found it in several places at the beginning of the author's handwriting in the book. We found it on pages 5, 9, 10, 11, 12, 13, 14, 15, 21, 22, 23, 24, 28, 29, 31, 32, 34, 38, 42, 45, 49, 55, 62, and 65. His handwriting matches the handwriting of his signature whose image was published at the beginning of the treatise 'al-Ijtima' wa al-Iftiraq fi al-Khulf bi al-Talaq' by Professor Muhammad 'Abd al-Razzaq Hamza, Egypt, year 1342 AH. And we present to the reader photographic images of five important pages of the book in which the shaykh's handwriting in his noble script is revealed, a precious treasure and a lavish gift for those who appreciate its value: pages 10, 29, 45, 55, and 65, along with images of the book's cover, the first page, and the last two pages. The aim is to represent the book to the reader in a way that suffices for lengthy description. The shaykh's handwriting, may Allah have mercy on him, has a characteristic not hidden from one who studies it intently, and his personality emerges from it to the utmost degree, as with anyone's handwriting. For he writes with a firm, concise, fast script; the author can be described as concise yet complete, fast yet clear; it indicates a brilliant, thoughtful mind, a living, adventurous heart, a mature, flowing intellect, and fingers of steadiness and skill. It can hardly be read due to its extreme conciseness, but when read it can hardly be denied or rejected. He writes with a pen medium between thick and fine, with ink more red than black. The shaykh wrote on the margins of the book and between its lines as required for filling what the scribe omitted, correcting an error, or adding clarification. Perhaps he would write a word or two in his own handwriting and then the rest was completed by some scribes.
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage is the publisher's introduction describing the physical manuscript of Ibn Taymiyya's 'Radd 'ala al-Mantiqiyyin'. It begins with details of the paper, ink, and page numbering, then discusses the title and additional content on the cover. The publisher notes that the manuscript has been handled by many hands, with various marginal annotations and corrections. Crucially, the manuscript was collated against the author's original during his lifetime, as evidenced by a note on the last page dated 728 AH, the year of Ibn Taymiyya's death. The publisher emphasizes the manuscript's importance because it contains the author's own handwriting and additional material not in his original. The final part describes the distinctive features of Ibn Taymiyya's handwriting: concise, fast, firm, and indicative of his intellectual vigour. The publisher also mentions providing photographic images of key pages for the reader.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Evaluating Manuscript Authority
Publisher describes the manuscript's origin and its superiority over the author's own copy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the authority of a manuscript for a classical Islamic text using the criteria of provenance, collation, and authorial additions.

Core Idea
A manuscript with authorial additions can be more valuable than the author's own copy.

Scholars of Islamic texts rely on careful manuscript evaluation to establish the most authentic version of a work. This lesson examines a publisher's description of a manuscript that surpasses even the author's holograph because it contains the author's own marginal additions. Understanding these criteria is essential for rigorous textual scholarship in any Islamic science.

Guided Path
1
Identify the manuscript's provenance
Note that the manuscript was written during the author's lifetime (Ibn Taymiyya). This increases its authority because it is contemporary with the author.
Provenance is the first indicator of reliability.
2
Examine the collation process
The manuscript was collated against the author's original (in his own handwriting) and the collation was completed in the year of the author's death. This ensures accuracy.
Collation (muqabala) is a standard method to verify textual correctness.
3
Check for authorial verification
The beginning of the manuscript was read back to the author, who approved it. This direct verification adds further authority.
Reading back (qira'a) is a known validation method in Hadith and other sciences.
4
Identify authorial additions
The author himself wrote additions (ziyadat) on the margins. These contain material not found in his original composition, making this manuscript more complete.
Authorial marginalia can be crucial for understanding the final intentions of the author.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النسخة وعِظَم شأنها. فقد ثبت أن النسخة كتبت في حياة المصنف رحمه الله تعالى؛ وأنها قوبلت على أصل المصنف بخطه المقروء عليه ; وأن مقابلتها قد انتهت في سنة ۷۲۸ - سنة وفاة المصنف - بل متصلاً بعد وفاته وكانت في ٢٠ ذي القعدة منها ; وأن أوائلها قد قرأت على المصنف فجاء على هامش ص ٧٥ بلغ على مؤلفه رضى الله عنه ; وأن المصنف رحمه الله تعالى قد كتب على هوامشها بخطه الشريف ; وأن من تلك الكتابات ما هو زيادات له على أصل تصنيفه، فاحتوت على مواد لا توجد فيه، وذلك ما امتازت به هذه النسخة على نسخة المصنف بخطه
The copy and its great importance. It has been established that the copy was written during the lifetime of the author, may Allah have mercy on him; and that it was collated against the author's original in his own handwriting that was read to him; and that its collation was completed in the year 728 - the year of the author's death - rather continuously after his death, and it was on the 20th of Dhu al-Qa'dah of that year; and that its beginning was read to the author, so it came on the margin of page 75: 'It reached its author, may Allah be pleased with him'; and that the author, may Allah have mercy on him, wrote on its margins in his noble handwriting; and that among those writings are additions to his original composition, so it contained materials not found in it, and that is what distinguishes this copy from the author's copy in his own handwriting.
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage is a description of the manuscript's provenance by the publisher. It establishes the manuscript's authenticity and value by documenting that it was written during Ibn Taymiyya's lifetime, collated against his original, and even includes his own handwritten corrections and additions. The publisher emphasizes that this copy contains material not present in the author's own holograph, making it a superior witness to the text. The passage follows a clear sequence: the manuscript was written in the author's lifetime, collated against the original (with the collation finishing shortly after his death), the beginning was read back to the author for verification, and the author himself wrote additions on the margins. Each point reinforces the manuscript's authority.

Key Takeaway
A manuscript's authority is enhanced by provenance, collation, authorial verification, and especially authorial additions that go beyond the original text.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate

Deciphering Authorial Handwriting in Manuscripts
Publisher describes author's handwriting and correction examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key features of Ibn Taymiyya's handwriting described by the publisher and apply principles of textual criticism to resolve ambiguous readings.

Core Idea
An author's handwriting is a window into their mind and a crucial tool for authenticating texts.

In Islamic scholarship, the authenticity of a text often depends on the correct deciphering of the author's own handwriting. Even a scholar of Ibn Taymiyya's stature wrote in a concise, fast hand that posed challenges to later readers. This lesson examines the publisher's detailed description of Ibn Taymiyya's handwriting and two specific examples of difficult readings, showing how careful textual analysis can recover the intended meaning.

Guided Path
1
Identify pages with authorial handwriting
The publisher lists specific page numbers where Ibn Taymiyya's own handwriting appears. Note these pages to understand the extent of the author's direct involvement.
Pages include 5, 9, 10, 11, 12, 13, 14, 15, 21, 22, 23, 24, 28, 29, 31, 32, 34, 38, 42, 45, 49, 55, 62, 65.
2
Extract characteristics of the handwriting
The publisher describes the handwriting as firm, concise, fast, medium pen, reddish-black ink. It is difficult to read but clear to those familiar with it. This reflects the author's sharp mind and character.
These features are important for recognizing authentic authorial additions vs. scribal notes.
3
Analyze the first difficult reading example
On page 45 margin, a phrase was misread as 'فاسد' but correctly read as 'فابْتَل' referring to a hadith on ghusl. The publisher connects it to a hadith from Abu Dawud.
The correction relies on both orthographic similarity and contextual meaning from Islamic legal sources.
4
Analyze the second example and the editor's correction
On page 55, the word 'قَوَّالون' appears twice. The editor hypothesizes that the author first wrote the singular 'قَوَّال' and then corrected it to the plural 'قَوَّالون' by adding letters or striking through.
This shows the author's real-time editing process, revealing his meticulousness in logical discussions.

تفحصنا خط الشيخ وكتابته فوجدناها في عدة مواضع من أوائل خط المصنف عن الكتاب. وجدناها في صفحات ۵، ۹ ، ۱۰ ، ۱۱، ۱۲ ، ۱۳ ، ١٤، ١٥، ٢١، ٢٢، ۲۳ ، ۲۴، ۲۸ ، ۲۹ ، ۳۱ ، ۳۲ ، ۳۴، ۳۸ ، ٤۲، ٤٥ ، ٤٩، ٥٥ ، ٦٢ و ٦٥ . وخطه مطابق لخط إمضائه الذي نُشِرَتْ صورته بأول رسالة الاجتماع والافتراق في الخلف بالطلاق ط. الأستاذ محمد عبد الرزاق حمزة ، مصر سنة ١٣٤٢ هـ. وإنا لنتحف القارىء بصُور فوتوغرافية لخمس صفحات هامة من الكتاب قد تجلت فيها كتابة الشيخ بخطه الشريف تحفة ثمينة وهدية فاخرة لمن يقدّر قدرها ،وهي صفحات ۱۰، ۲۹، ٤٥، ٥٥ و ٦٥ ، مع صور غلاف الكتاب والصفحة الأولى والصفحتين الأخيرتين منه. والمقصود تمثيل الكتاب للقارىء بصورة تغني عن وصفه المسهب . لخط الشيخ رحمه الله ميزة لا تخفى على من دَرَسه بإمعان وتَظْهَرُ منه شخصيته ميزات خط البارزة غاية الظهور شأن خط أي إنسان . فإنه يكتب بخط محكم ، موجز، سريع، يمكن المصنف وصفه بالإيجاز في تمام وبالسُّرْعة في وضوح، ويدل على ذهن وقاد مفكر، وقلب حي مقدام ، وفكر ناضج سیّال ، وبَنان ذاتِ ثبات ومهارة. لا يكاد يُقرأ من شدة إيجازه، وإذا قرأ فلا يكاد يُنكر أو يُجْحَد . يكتب بقلم متوسط بين الغليظ والدقيق بحبر لونه أحمر أكثر من الأسود. وقد كتب الشيخ علي حواشي الكتاب وبين سطوره حيث اقتضى المقام لاستدراك ما سقط من الكاتب أو تصحيح غلط أو زيادة بيان. وربما كتب كلمة أو کلمتین بخطه ثم استكمل الباقي من خط بعض الكتبة . ولنضرب مثالين لما أشكل من خطه . زاد الشيخ عبارة قدر ستة أسطر في عرض الحاشية اليمنى من ص ٤٥ ، وقد أعادها بتمامها بعضُ مَنْ طالع الكتاب بخطه بأسفل الصفحة (انظر (الصورة). ووقع في السطر الثاني منها ما قرأه هذا الكاتب ودخول من خرج منه مني فاسد في قوله وإن كنتم جنباً ،فاطهروا ولكن كلمة «فاسد» لا تشبهها صورة ولا تستقيم معنى بل هي أشبه بكلمة «فابْتَل» ، ولعل الشيخ يشير إلى ما أخرجه أبو داود في كتاب الطهارة عن عائشة رضى الله عنها قالت: سُئل النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم عن الرجل يجد البلل ولا يذكر اختلاماً، قال: «يغتسل ; وعن الرجل يرى أن قد احتلم ولا يجد البلل، قال: «لا غُسلَ عليه - الحديث والمثال الثاني في عبارة كتبها في عرض الحاشية اليمنى من ص ٥٥ انظر الصورة) . فوقع في السطر الثاني منها كلمة لا تكاد تقرأ، وهي وهي كلمة «قَوَّالون» حيث قال وقوّالون بسبق الذاتي للماهية». وفي ابتداء السطر الثالث منها كلمة قد انطمس بعضها وقراءتها أصعب من الأولى، وهي قوالون» أيضاً حيث قال وقَوَّالون بأنه لا يتأخر عن الماهية. ومن عسى أن يقرأها «قوّالون»! وحصلت هنا عجيبة إذا انحلت انحلت الكلمة، وذلك كأن الشيخ قد أخطأ أولاً فكتب وقوّال» بصيغة الإفراد ولكنه استدرك الخطأ حالاً، فإما أَنْ تَرَك اللام على حالها وكتب بعده «لون» أو ضَرَب على اللام بضربة خفيفة لا تظهر الآن في حالتها المطموسة، والله أعلم بالصواب .
We examined the handwriting of the Shaykh and found it in several places at the beginning of the author's handwriting on the book. We found it on pages 5, 9, 10, 11, 12, 13, 14, 15, 21, 22, 23, 24, 28, 29, 31, 32, 34, 38, 42, 45, 49, 55, 62, and 65. And his handwriting matches the handwriting of his signature whose picture was published at the beginning of the treatise 'Al-Ijtimā' wa al-Ifṭirāq fī al-Khalaf bi al-Ṭalāq' published by Prof. Muhammad Abd al-Razzaq Hamza, Egypt, year 1342 AH. And we are presenting to the reader photographic pictures of five important pages of the book in which the Shaykh's handwriting in his noble hand appeared as a precious gift and a fine present for those who appreciate its value: pages 10, 29, 45, 55, and 65, along with pictures of the book's cover, the first page, and the last two pages. The purpose is to represent the book to the reader in a way that dispenses with a lengthy description. The handwriting of the Shaykh, may Allah have mercy on him, has a characteristic that is not hidden from whoever studies it carefully, and from it his personality appears, the prominent features of his handwriting appear to the utmost degree, as is the case with any person's handwriting. For he writes with a firm, concise, fast hand, which the author can describe as concise in completeness and fast in clarity, and it indicates a sharp, thoughtful mind, a lively, courageous heart, a mature, flowing intellect, and fingers of steadiness and skill. It can hardly be read due to its extreme conciseness, and when read, it can hardly be denied or rejected. He writes with a pen medium between thick and fine, with ink whose color is more red than black. And the Shaykh wrote on the margins of the book and between its lines as the occasion required to correct what fell from the scribe, or to correct an error, or to add clarification. And perhaps he would write a word or two in his own hand, then the rest was completed in the handwriting of one of the scribes. We give two examples of what was difficult from his handwriting. The Shaykh added a phrase of about six lines in the width of the right margin of page 45, and some of those who read the book in his hand rewrote it completely at the bottom of the page (see the picture). In the second line of it occurred what this writer read as 'ودخول من خرج منه مني فاسد' in His saying 'And if you are junub, then purify yourselves', but the word 'فاسد' does not resemble it in form nor does it make sense, rather it is more similar to the word 'فابْتَل', and perhaps the Shaykh is referring to what Abu Dawud narrated in the book of Tahara from Aisha, may Allah be pleased with her, who said: The Prophet, peace be upon him, was asked about a man who finds wetness but does not remember a nocturnal emission; he said: 'He should perform ghusl'; and about a man who sees that he had a nocturnal emission but finds no wetness; he said: 'No ghusl upon him' - the hadith. And the second example is in a phrase he wrote in the width of the right margin of page 55 (see the picture). In the second line of it occurred a word that can hardly be read, and it is the word 'قَوَّالون' where he said 'wa qawwālūn bi sabq al-dhātī li al-māhiyya'. And at the beginning of the third line a word whose part is erased and its reading is more difficult than the first, and it is 'qawwālūn' also, where he said 'wa qawwālūn bi annahu lā yata'akhkhar 'an al-māhiyya'. And who might read it as 'qawwālūn'! And here a wonder occurred, that if it is resolved, the word is resolved: it is as if the Shaykh first made a mistake and wrote 'wa qawwāl' in the singular form, but then corrected the error immediately, so either he left the lam as it was and wrote after it 'lūn', or he struck the lam with a light strike that does not appear now in its effaced state, and Allah knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage is a detailed description of Ibn Taymiyya's handwriting by the publisher. It first lists pages where the author's handwriting appears, then compares it to the author's signature. The publisher includes photographic reproductions. The description emphasizes that the handwriting is concise and fast yet clear, reflecting the author's intellect and personality. The publisher then provides two specific examples of difficult readings from the margins. The first example involves a phrase that was misread as 'فاسد' but is more likely 'فابْتَل', connected to a hadith about ghusl. The second example concerns the word 'قَوَّالون' (many sayers) in a discussion about the priority of the essential (al-dhātī) over the quiddity (al-māhiyya), where the author may have first written the singular and then corrected it. The passage shows the careful editorial work done to decipher the manuscript.

Key Takeaway
The handwriting of a scholar like Ibn Taymiyya, though concise and fast, can be deciphered through careful study and comparative analysis, ensuring the integrity of transmitted texts.

Introduction and Front Matter

The Architecture of Ibn Taymiyya's Radd
Publisher outlines the book's structure into four main parts and explains the placement of headings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the four-maqam structure of Ibn Taymiyya's Radd 'ala al-Mantiqiyyin and identify which textual features are authorial versus editorial.

Core Idea
Ibn Taymiyya's book is one continuous argument; the headings are editorial scaffolds.

This passage from the publisher gives us a bird's-eye view of Ibn Taymiyya's Radd 'ala al-Mantiqiyyin. Instead of a modern chapter structure, the book unfolds in four progressively larger sections called maqamat, each attacking a specific claim of the logicians. The publisher also reveals that all headings in the text and margins are later additions—a crucial fact for anyone who wants to read the work as the author intended. Let's unpack this structure and its implications for studying the book.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four maqams
The passage states the book is divided into four maqams (stations). Each maqam contains several 'wujuh' (aspects) of proofs against a specific claim of the logicians. Note that the first maqam lacks a general introduction, while the others begin with one.
These maqams are not named in the passage, but they are thematic units.
2
Map the size progression
The last maqam contains more than half of the book. This suggests that the author's strongest or most extensive refutation is reserved for the final part. Observe how the argument builds across the maqams.
3
Distinguish authorial from editorial
The original manuscript was written continuously without any headings. The publisher added all headings in the body and margins, except for a few that were taken from the margins themselves. This means the headings are not part of Ibn Taymiyya's original text.
When quoting or analyzing the text, be careful not to treat the headings as authorial divisions.
4
Recognize digressions and repetitions
The passage mentions that the book contains various discussions, some repeated, as digressions (istitrad) following the author's custom. Understanding this helps you follow the flow of argument without being confused by apparent tangents.
Ibn Taymiyya often engages in side discussions; be patient and track the main thread.

تقسيم الكتاب انقسم الكتاب في أربع مقامات كل منها أكبرُ من الذي قبله حتى الأخير منها قد احتوى على أكثر من نصف الكتاب واشتمل كلٌّ منها على عدة وجوه الأدلة على بطلان دعوى من دعاوي أهل المنطق، وافتتح كل منها سوى الأول بكلام عمومي على سبيل التمهيد، واختتم المقام الثالث بزيادة ثلاثة فصول وقد تخلل الكتاب أبحاث شتى - وبعضها مكررة - على سبيل الاستطراد على عادة المصنف . وضع هذه الطبعة وقد كتب الكتاب من أوله إلى آخره بكتابة متصلة على منوال واحد من غير فصل ولا عنوان. فكل ما تَرَى فيه من العنوانات في صُلب المتن أو في الحواشي فمن وَضْعِنا، المصنف، اللهم إلا قسماً من العنوانات قد اخترناها مما كُتب على حواشي وليس من
Division of the book: The book is divided into four stations (maqams), each larger than the one before it, until the last of them contains more than half of the book. Each one includes several aspects of proofs concerning the invalidity of one of the claims of the logicians. Each of them, except the first, opens with general talk by way of introduction. The third station concludes with an addition of three chapters. The book is interspersed with various discussions - some of them repeated - by way of digression, as is the author's custom. Setting of this edition: The book was written from its beginning to its end in continuous writing on a single pattern, without separation or heading. So all that you see in it of headings in the body of the text or in the margins are from our placement, not from the author, except for a portion of headings that we chose from what was written on the margins and not from
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage describes the overall structure of the book 'Radd 'alā al-Mantiqiyyīn' by Ibn Taymiyya. The publisher explains that the book is divided into four 'maqams' (stations or sections), each one larger than the previous, with the last containing over half the book. Each maqam covers several proofs (wujuh al-adilla) against a specific claim of the logicians. The first maqam does not have an opening general discussion, but the others do. The third maqam ends with three additional chapters. The publisher also notes that the book contains various digressions, some repeated, which was the author's habit. Then the publisher explains the editorial choices for this edition: the original manuscript was written continuously without headings, so the publisher added headings in the text and margins, except for some taken from the margins themselves. The passage ends abruptly, likely continuing to explain which headings are from the author.

Key Takeaway
The structure of Ibn Taymiyya's Radd is organic and continuous; its modern chapter divisions are editorial scaffolds, not authorial.

Introduction and Front Matter

Critical Editing in Islamic Scholarship
Editor describes textual difficulties and his methodology for producing the critical edition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key steps a critical editor takes to produce a reliable edition of an Islamic manuscript and explain the importance of textual criticism for sound scholarship.

Core Idea
A reliable text is the foundation for sound reasoning.

This lesson examines the editor's introduction to Ibn Taymiyya's 'Radd Mantiqiyyin'. The editor details the painstaking process of deciphering the author's handwriting, correcting errors, and adding a critical apparatus. Understanding this process is essential for any scholar who relies on printed editions of classical Islamic texts. It demonstrates that textual accuracy is not automatic—it requires deliberate effort and methodological rigor.

Guided Path
1
Identify the textual challenge
The editor gives two examples of difficult readings from the manuscript. In the first, a word originally read as 'fāsid' (corrupt) is argued to be 'fābtal' (so seek) based on context and a hadith reference. Locate these examples in the translation and note how the editor uses context to correct the text.
This shows that manuscript readings are not always trustworthy; context and external sources (like hadith) help determine the correct reading.
2
Understand the book's structure
The editor describes the division into four 'maqāmāt', each arguing against a claim of the logicians. Note that the third maqām ends with three additional chapters. This structure, not obvious from the manuscript, is clarified by the editor's analysis.
3
Examine the editorial additions
The editor explains that all headings, punctuation, verse numbering, hadith references, and even some headings are his own additions, indicated as such. He also placed page numbers of the original manuscript in parentheses.
A critical edition does not simply reproduce the manuscript; it adds value through explanatory and organizational tools.
4
Review the correction process
The editor obtained a copy of the unique manuscript, had it transcribed and corrected twice, and finally collated against the original. This multi-step process ensures maximum accuracy.
The effort and expense involved underscore the importance of textual precision in Islamic scholarship.
5
Connect to broader Islamic methodology
Compare the editor's methodology to that of hadith scholars (e.g., verifying chains, comparing variants) and jurists (e.g., establishing the correct text of a ruling). Both seek to eliminate error from the transmitted source.
This shows that textual criticism is an integral part of the Islamic sciences, not a modern innovation.

ولنضرب مثالين لما أشكل من خطه . زاد الشيخ عبارة قدر ستة أسطر في عرض الحاشية اليمنى من ص ٤٥ ، وقد أعادها بتمامها بعضُ مَنْ طالع الكتاب بخطه بأسفل الصفحة (انظر (الصورة). وقع في السطر الثاني منها ما قرأه هذا الكاتب ودخول من خرج منه مني فاسد في قوله وإن كنتم جنباً ،فاطهروا ولكن كلمة «فاسد» لا تشبهها صورة ولا تستقيم معنى بل هي أشبه بكلمة «فابْتَل» ، ولعل الشيخ يشير إلى ما أخرجه أبو داود في كتاب الطهارة عن عائشة رضى الله عنها قالت: سُئل النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم عن الرجل يجد البلل ولا يذكر اختلاماً، قال: «يغتسل ؛ وعن الرجل يرى أن قد احتلم ولا يجد البلل، قال: «لا غُسلَ عليه - الحديث والمثال الثاني في عبارة كتبها

مقدمة الناشر
۲۹
الأصل وقد فاتنا الإشارة إليه بعلامة خاصة. وكذلك ما يوجد فيه من تفصيل المباحث وتقطيعها وترتيبها وجميع ما فيه من علامات الوقف والابتداء المختلفة، وعلاماتِ أقوال القائلين والاصطلاحات الفنية بين قوسين صغيرين وعلاماتِ العبارات المعترضة أو المفسرة، وعلامتي السئوال والتعجب وضبط الكلمات المهمة أو المشكلة فمن اجتهادنا وبذمتنا . والأرقامُ الصغيرة بين قوسين في صلب المتن تدل على أعداد صفحات أصل الكتاب وما وضعنا كلَّ ذلك إلا تسهيلاً لاقتناء أبحاث الكتاب وتقريباً لفهم معانيه كما هو المعهود في أرقى فن الطباعة الحديثة في الغرب والشرق .
•
أما الآيات فقد بالغنا في تصحيحها بعد عرضها على المصحف بالرسم المصري وإعرابها كلها أو بعضها المشكل وترقيم أعدادها مسبوقاً باسم السورة الواقعة فيها مع رقم عددها واستخرجنا ما ورد فيه من الأحاديث النبوية وعَزَوْناها إلى من خَرَّجها من أرباب كتب الحديث وعلقنا عليها ما احتاج إلى تعليقه. وقد أرخنا ترجمة من جاء ذكره من الأعلام على وجه الاختصار المفيد . وأشرنا إلى ما حَضَرَنا من مراجع بعض الأبحاث في تأليفات أخر للمصنف أو للحافظ ابن القيم رحمه الله تعالى، ووضعنا فهرساً لمحتويات الكتاب واهتممنا فيه ما استطعنا من أمر التصحيح إذ هو المقصود الأعظم، المطلوب رعايته في طبع الكتب، ولو كَلَّفَنا ذلك صرفَ الوقت الكثير والجهد المتعب الخطير ومن المال غير يسير. وبالجملة كان قصارى جهدنا إبراز هذا السفر الجليل إلى عالم المطبوعات في قالب قشيب جميل بلب سليم غير عليل. ولا ندعي الكمال ولا ينبغي، بل نرجو العفو وغَضَّ الطَّرْف عما فيه من النقص والخلل .

فلما أحجمت عن ذلك لأسباب هي أعرفُ بها عَزَمْنا على طبعه بمطبعتنا. تفضلت الإدارة بمنحنا نسخة من الكتاب نقلها لنا أحد مصحيحها عن نسختها من غير تعرض للأصل. ولما تبينا فيها أغلاطاً رددناها ثانياً وكلفنا رجُلين فاضلين من مصححيها بمقابلتها على الأصل وتصحيحها تصحيحاً كاملاً وأخيراً طبعنا الكتاب استناداً إلى
Features of the author's handwriting. 28. Publisher's introduction. We give two examples of what was difficult from his handwriting. The Sheikh added a phrase of about six lines in the margin of the right side of page 45, and one of those who read the book in his handwriting copied it in full at the bottom of the page (see image). In the second line of it occurred what this writer read as 'and the entry of what came out of me is corrupt (fāsid) in his saying: 'If you are in a state of major ritual impurity, purify yourselves.' But the word 'corrupt' does not resemble it in form nor is it consistent in meaning; rather it resembles the word 'so seek (fābtal)'. Perhaps the Sheikh is pointing to what Abu Dawud narrated in the Book of Purity from Aisha, may God be pleased with her: the Prophet, peace be upon him, was asked about a man who finds wetness but does not remember a dream, he said: 'He performs full ablution (ghusl).' And about a man who thinks he had a wet dream but does not find wetness, he said: 'No ghusl upon him.' The hadith. And the second example is in a phrase he wrote a in the margin of the right side of page 55 (see image). In the second line of it occurred a word hardly readable, and it is the word 'qawwālūn' (sayers) where he said 'and sayers that the essence precedes the quiddity'. And at the beginning of the third line of it a word partly erased, and reading it is more difficult than the first; it is also 'qawwālūn' where he said 'and sayers that it is not delayed from the quiddity'. And who can read it as 'qawwālūn'! Here a wonder occurred; if it is solved, the word is solved. That is, it seems the Sheikh first made an error and wrote 'wa-qawwāl' in the singular form, but he immediately corrected the error, so either he left the lām as it was and wrote after it 'lūn', or he struck the lām with a light stroke that now does not appear in its erased state. And God knows best. Division of the book: The book is divided into four maqāmāt (stations), each larger than the previous, until the last of them contains more than half the book. Each of them includes several aspects of evidence for the invalidity of one of the claims of the logicians. Each of them, except the first, opens with a general statement as an introduction. The third maqām concludes with an additional three chapters. Various discussions intersperse the book, some repeated, as digressions, according to the author's habit. And their arrangement. This edition: The book was written from beginning to end in continuous writing, in one style, without separation or headings. So every heading you see in the text or in the margins is from our own placement, not from the author, except for a portion of headings we chose from what was written on the margins and is not from the original, and we neglected to indicate it with a special sign. Likewise, what is found in it of detail of topics, segmentation, arrangement, all the different stop and start marks, quotation marks for speakers' statements and technical conventions in small brackets, marks for parenthetical or explanatory phrases, question and exclamation marks, and vocalization of important or problematic words, are from our own effort and responsibility. The small numbers in parentheses in the text denote the page numbers of the original book. We have done all of this only to facilitate acquiring the book's discussions and to bring its meanings closer to understanding, as is customary in the most advanced printing art in the West and East. As for the verses, we made great efforts in correcting them after checking them against the Quran with Egyptian orthography, and fully or partially parsing the problematic ones, and numbering them preceded by the name of the sura in which they occur along with the verse number. We extracted the prophetic hadiths contained in the book and attributed them to their compilers from the authors of hadith books, and we commented on what needed commentary. We provided concise but useful biographical notes for every notable person mentioned. We pointed to what references we had for some discussions in other works by the author or by Hafiz Ibn Qayyim, may God have mercy on him. We made an index of the book's contents and exerted as much effort as possible in correction, for it is the greatest goal that should be observed in printing books, even if it cost us much time, tiring and serious effort, and no small amount of money. In short, our utmost effort was to bring this great work to the world of printed books in a beautiful, fresh form with sound substance, not defective. We do not claim perfection, nor should we, but we hope for pardon and overlooking of any deficiency or fault. Correction and commentary: It has been mentioned that only one manuscript of the book is known. The administration of the Ma'ārif Circle arranged for a copy to be obtained from the 'Uthmāniyya Circle in Hyderabad Deccan, a copy of the original preserved in the Āsafiyya Library for the purpose of printing it. When they refrained from doing so for reasons they know better, we decided to print it in our own press. The administration kindly granted us a copy of the book, copied for us by one of their correctors from their copy without consulting the original. When we noticed errors in it, we returned it a second time and commissioned two virtuous men from their correctors to collate it with the original and correct it completely. Finally, we printed the book based on
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage is from the editor's introduction to the book Radd Mantiqiyyin. The editor begins by discussing difficulties encountered in deciphering the author's handwriting, giving two concrete examples. The first involves a phrase where the word 'fāsid' (corrupt) appears but contextually seems wrong; the editor suggests it might actually be 'fābtal' (so seek) and connects it to a hadith about ritual purity. The second example is a word 'qawwālūn' (sayers) which is difficult to read due to manuscript damage; the editor speculates about a scribal correction. Next, the editor describes the overall structure of the book: it is divided into four 'maqāmāt' (stations), each larger than the previous, containing arguments against the logicians' claims. The third maqām ends with three additional chapters. The editor then explains his own editorial work: he added all headings, punctuation, vocalization, and verse/hadith references, as well as an index. He details the process of correcting the text from the sole manuscript, including collation with the original. The editor emphasizes the great effort and expense undertaken to produce this edition, hoping it will be of benefit despite its imperfections.

Key Takeaway
A critical edition of an Islamic manuscript requires the editor to decipher difficult handwriting, correct readings using context and external sources, add structural and explanatory elements, and undergo a rigorous collation process—all to produce a reliable text for scholars.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
The Role of Critical Editing in Preserving Islamic Texts
Publisher describes editing process and a flood incident.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify key steps in manuscript collation and explain their importance for scholarly accuracy in Islamic works.

Core Idea
A single uncorrected manuscript can lead to widespread error; critical editing is the science of textual integrity.

The publisher's introduction to Ibn Taymiyya's 'Radd 'alā al-Mantiqiyyīn' reveals the immense effort required to produce a reliable edition. This passage shows how even a single manuscript, when improperly transcribed, can introduce errors. More importantly, it teaches us that the process of collation is essential for scholarly authenticity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the publisher's primary concern
Look at the first part where the publisher discusses punctuation, vocalization, and correction. What does the publisher emphasize as the greatest objective? (Answer: al-taṣḥīḥ, correction.)
2
Trace the chain of manuscript transmission
The publisher explains how they obtained a copy from the Dā'irat al-'Uthmāniyya, had it transcribed, found errors, returned it for collation, and later printed. List these steps in order.
3
Evaluate the role of the flood
The publisher thanks Allah for the flood because it revealed errors in the copy they were using. What does this tell us about the reliability of the first copy? (Answer: it was not accurate; only direct collation ensured correctness.)
4
Extract principles of textual criticism
From this account, what are the necessary steps for a reliable edition? (e.g., multiple manuscripts, collation, verification, correction tables.)
5
Apply to your own study
When reading a classical Islamic text, how can you determine the reliability of the edition? Look for publisher's notes, compare editions, check for mention of collation with originals.

مقدمة الناشر الأصل وقد فاتنا الإشارة إليه بعلامة خاصة. وكذلك ما يوجد فيه من تفصيل المباحث وتقطيعها وترتيبها وجميع ما فيه من علامات الوقف والابتداء المختلفة، وعلاماتِ أقوال القائلين والاصطلاحات الفنية بين قوسين صغيرين وعلاماتِ العبارات المعترضة أو المفسرة، وعلامتي السئوال والتعجب وضبط الكلمات المهمة أو المشكلة فمن اجتهادنا وبذمتنا . والأرقامُ الصغيرة بين قوسين في صلب المتن تدل على أعداد صفحات أصل الكتاب وما وضعنا كلَّ ذلك إلا تسهيلاً لاقتناء أبحاث الكتاب وتقريباً لفهم معانيه كما هو المعهود في أرقى فن الطباعة الحديثة في الغرب والشرق . • أما الآيات فقد بالغنا في تصحيحها بعد عرضها على المصحف بالرسم المصري وإعرابها كلها أو بعضها المشكل وترقيم أعدادها مسبوقاً باسم السورة الواقعة فيها مع رقم عددها واستخرجنا ما ورد فيه من الأحاديث النبوية وعَزَوْناها إلى من خَرَّجها من أرباب كتب الحديث وعلقنا عليها ما احتاج إلى تعليقه. وقد أرخنا ترجمة من جاء ذكره من الأعلام على وجه الاختصار المفيد . وأشرنا إلى ما حَضَرَنا من مراجع بعض الأبحاث في تأليفات أخر للمصنف أو للحافظ ابن القيم رحمه الله تعالى، ووضعنا فهرساً لمحتويات الكتاب واهتممنا فيه ما استطعنا من أمر التصحيح إذ هو المقصود الأعظم، المطلوب رعايته في طبع الكتب، ولو كَلَّفَنا ذلك صرفَ الوقت الكثير والجهد المتعب الخطير ومن المال غير يسير. وبالجملة كان قصارى جهدنا إبراز هذا السفر الجليل إلى عالم المطبوعات في قالب قشيب جميل بلب سليم غير عليل. ولا ندعي الكمال ولا ينبغي، بل نرجو العفو وغَضَّ الطَّرْف عما فيه من النقص والخلل . التصحيح والتعليق قد تقدم أن الكتاب لا يُعلم له نسخة غير واحدة. وقد أعدت إدارة دائرة المعارف حصول النقل من دائرة العثمانية بحيدر آباد الدكّن نسخة عن الأصل المحفوظ بالمكتبة الآصفية بغرض طبعه . المعارف فلما أحجمت عن ذلك لأسباب هي أعرفُ بها عَزَمْنا على طبعه بمطبعتنا. تفضلت الإدارة بمنحنا نسخة من الكتاب نقلها لنا أحد مصحيحها عن نسختها من غير تعرض للأصل. ولما تبينا فيها أغلاطاً رددناها ثانياً وكلفنا رجُلين فاضلين من مصححيها بمقابلتها على الأصل وتصحيحها تصحيحاً كاملاً وأخيراً طبعنا الكتاب استناداً إلى النسخة المصححة المقابلة على أصل الآصفية غير مُرتابين في صحتها. وليتنا صَدَّقنا حُسْنَ ظَنّنا فيها ! من أوشك الكتاب أن ينتهي من الطبع إذ حدثَتْ عاصفة شديدة مع طوفان أصاب بعض متاعنا فيه أوراقُ النسخة التي كنا نطبع عنها الكتاب. فاضطررنا رغم أنفنا إلى زيارة النسخة الأصلية بحيدر آباد الدكن لنقل ما أضاعه الطوفان. ولما اكتشفنا أن النسخة التي اعتمدنا عليها في الطبع ليست صحيحة مطابقة للأصل تولّينا بأنفسنا مقابلة القدر المطبوع وما بقي من الطبع على أصل الآصفية، وذلك بعد تمام طبع ٤٨٠ صفحة الكتاب. فعملنا جدولاً كاملاً لتصحيح الأغلاط كلها وألحقناه في آخر الكتاب، حتى إذا صُحْح بموجبه يُرجَى أن يكون طبق الأصل. وإنا لنأسف جد الأسف على هذا الخلل الفادح ولكنه كان أمراً مَقْضِيّاً، ونحمد الله عز وجل على إرسال ذلك الطوفان إذ لولاه لَمَا اطَّلَعْنا على هذه المَسَاوِي ولَمَا أتيح لنا تصحيحُ كتاب طالما اشتاقت إليه النفوس بشوق ولهف شديدين . فلله الحكمة البالغة في كل ما يقضي ويقدر، وعسى أن تكرهوا شيئاً ويجعلُ الله فيه خيراً كثيراً. وسنستدرك هذه النقائص في الطبعة الثانية إذا شاء الله وقَدَّر . وقد عملنا فهارس مفيدة للكتاب كفهرس الأعلام، والكتب، والأماكن، والفرق، ونريد أن نعمل فهرساً عاماً لموضوعات الكتاب مرتباً على حروف المعجم، فإنه مفتاح لكنوز الكتاب وخزائنه التي تبقى محجوبة عن الأنظار غير متهيّأة للطلاب بدونه، ولكنه لم يتيسر طبعها لضيق الوقت، ولعلنا أتبعنا الكتاب بتتمة تحتوي على ذلك كله، والله هو المستعان .
Publisher's Introduction: The original, and we missed indicating it with a special mark. Likewise, what is found in it of detailed discussions, their division and arrangement, and all the various punctuation marks, quotation marks for sayings and technical terms in small parentheses, marks for parenthetical or explanatory phrases, question and exclamation marks, and the vocalization of important or problematic words – all that is from our own effort and responsibility. The small numbers in parentheses in the text indicate the page numbers of the original book, and we placed all that only to facilitate acquiring the research of the book and to make understanding its meanings easier, as is customary in the finest modern printing art in the West and East. As for the Qur'anic verses, we made great effort to correct them by comparing them with the Egyptian edition of the Mushaf, and their full or partial vocalization where problematic, and numbering them preceded by the name of the surah they are in with their verse number. We extracted the prophetic hadiths that occur in it, attributed them to their compilers from the masters of hadith books, and commented on them as needed. We also provided brief biographies of notable figures mentioned. We indicated the references we had at hand for some research in other works by the author or by al-Hafiz Ibn Qayyim, may Allah have mercy on him. We created a table of contents for the book and paid as much attention as possible to correction, as it is the greatest objective required in printing books, even if it cost us much time and effort and considerable money. In summary, our utmost effort was to produce this great work in the publishing world in a beautiful, attractive format with sound content. We do not claim perfection nor should we, but we hope for forgiveness and overlooking of any deficiency or error. Correction and Commentary: It has been mentioned that only one manuscript of the book is known. The management of the Dā'irat al-Ma'ārif arranged to obtain a copy from the Dā'irat al-'Uthmāniyya in Hyderabad Deccan, a copy of the original preserved in the Āṣifiyya Library, for the purpose of printing it. When they refrained from that for reasons they know best, we resolved to print it in our own press. The management graciously granted us a copy of the book transcribed for us by one of their correctors from their copy without reference to the original. When we noticed errors in it, we returned it a second time and commissioned two capable men from their correctors to collate it with the original and correct it completely. Finally, we printed the book based on the corrected copy collated with the Āṣifiyya original, trusting in its correctness. Would that we had been right in our good assumption! The book was nearly finished printing when a severe storm with a flood occurred, damaging some of our belongings, including the pages of the copy we were printing from. We were compelled, reluctantly, to visit the original copy in Hyderabad Deccan to retrieve what the flood had destroyed. When we discovered that the copy we relied on for printing was not correct and matching the original, we ourselves undertook to collate the printed portion and the remainder of the printing with the Āṣifiyya original, after the complete printing of 480 pages of the book. So we made a complete table of all the errors and appended it at the end of the book, so that if corrected accordingly, it is hoped that it will match the original. We deeply regret this serious flaw, but it was a decreed matter. We praise Allah Almighty for sending that flood, because had it not been for it, we would not have discovered these defects, nor would we have been able to correct a book that souls have long longed for with intense yearning. So to Allah belongs the profound wisdom in all that He decrees and ordains. Perhaps you dislike something and Allah makes it a great good. We will rectify these shortcomings in the second edition if Allah wills and ordains. We have prepared useful indices for the book, such as indices of notable figures, books, places, and sects. We intend to prepare a general subject index arranged alphabetically, for it is the key to the treasures and repositories of the book that remain hidden from view and inaccessible to students without it, but its printing was not possible due to time constraints. Perhaps we will follow the book with a supplement containing all that. And Allah is the One sought for help.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage is the publisher's introduction, describing the editorial work done to produce a reliable edition of Ibn Taymiyya's 'Radd 'alā al-Mantiqiyyīn'. The publisher explains the efforts invested in correcting the text, including detailed punctuation, vocalization, and cross-referencing with original manuscripts. They also recount a significant incident where a flood damaged the copy they were using for printing, forcing them to collate directly with the original manuscript in Hyderabad. This accident, despite causing delay and error, ultimately allowed them to produce a more accurate edition. The publisher also mentions the preparation of indices and expresses hope for a future corrected edition. This passage does not contain logical arguments but provides important context for understanding the transmission of Ibn Taymiyya's work.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Understanding the Publisher's Role in Text Transmission
Publisher describes the abridgment and acknowledgments

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key decisions made by an editor/publisher when preparing a critical edition of a classical Islamic text and explain how those decisions affect the transmission of knowledge.

Core Idea
A publisher's introduction reveals the ethical and scholarly commitments behind preserving a text.

This lesson examines the publisher's introduction to an edition of Ibn Taymiyya's 'Refutation of the Logicians'. Although not a logical argument in itself, this introduction provides a window into the practical challenges of transmitting Islamic scholarly works. You will learn to recognize the editorial choices that shape how we receive classical texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the publisher's stated purpose
Read the first part of the introduction. The publisher says he intended to summarize Ibn Taymiyya's book for students. What does he name his abridgment?
The title 'Jahd al-Qariha fi Tajrid al-Nasiha' indicates his effort to distill the advice.
2
Examine the criteria for omission
The publisher lists what he omitted: digressions, theological refutations, repetitions, and criticisms not relating to universal principles. What does he say he did NOT omit?
He claims to have omitted nothing of importance.
3
Analyze the manuscript sources
The publisher describes a defective Azhar manuscript and his own copy. How did he use the Azhar manuscript?
He used it only to correct some errors in his own copy, marking corrections with (S).
4
Recognize the role of patronage
List the individuals and institutions thanked. What does their support tell us about the social context of scholarly publishing?
Patronage from Saudi officials, Indian academics, and family members enabled the publication.
5
Reflect on the significance of abridgment
Abridgment (talkhis) is common in Islamic learning. Why might a scholar abridge a longer work rather than reproduce it entirely?
For accessibility and focus, as the publisher states: for students and the intelligent.
